201 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Timber Glen Phase III, LLC v. Township of Hamilton


DOCKET NO. A-1775-13T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


441 N.J. Super. 514; 120 A.3d 226; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 125


April 20, 2015, Argued 
August 6, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 6, 2015.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, Docket No. L-0988-12.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where plaintiffs appealed from the summary judgment dismissal of their complaint that challenged an ordinance adopted by defendant township, assessing an annual $ 100 licensing fee on residential apartment units, the appellate court concluded the 1998 amendment to the Licensing Act adding N.J.S.A. § 40:52-1(n), permitting licensure of the "rental of real property for a term less than 175 consecutive days for residential purposes by a person having a permanent place of residence elsewhere," and the accompanying bill statement constituted powerful evidence of an intention to limit licensing residential rentals and constrained the provisions of § 40:52-1(d), which included "hotels, boardinghouses, boardinghouses, lodging and rooming houses,. motels, furnished and unfurnished rented housing or living units" to refer to short term living arrangements.


OUTCOME: The trial court's summary judgment was vacated.

 

202 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


In re Reallocation of Probation Officer


DOCKET NO. A-0056-13T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


441 N.J. Super. 434; 119 A.3d 921; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 119


April 22, 2015, Argued 
July 22, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 22, 2015.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Civil Service Commission, Docket No. 2013-3251.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the Civil Service Commission erred in approving the request by the Administrative Office of the Courts (AOC) for the transfer of two titles, from its competitive division to its noncompetitive division, because, as the N.J. Probation Association argued, the transfer was unconstitutional under N.J. Const. art. VII, § 1, para. 2, which required public employees to be selected on the basis of "merit and fitness to be ascertained, as far as practicable, by examination, which, as far as practicable, shall be competitive," and because the AOC had not established a sufficient factual basis for the transfer under the applicable statutory and regulatory requirements. HOLDINGS: [1]-The Commission failed to consider the constitutional issue at all; [2]-The AOC failed to establish a sufficient factual justification for the transfer under the applicable statutes and regulation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded for further consideration by the Commission, which it instructed to consider the appropriateness of the proposed transfer for each title separately.

 

203 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


New Jersey Div. of Child Prot. & Permanency v. J.L.G.


DOCKET NO. A-1746-13T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


450 N.J. Super. 113; 160 A.3d 112; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 227


January 20, 2015, Submitted 
July 21, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 17, 2017.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Hudson County, Docket No. FN-09-375-12.
New Jersey Div. of Child Prot. & Permanency v. J.L.G., 2015 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1741 (App.Div., July 21, 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not err in finding that defendant, a child's guardian, abused or neglected her under N.J.S.A. 9:6-8.21(c)(4)(b) by unreasonably allowing her mother, his girlfriend, to inflict excessive corporal punishment, as the evidence showed that he saw the mother beating the child, understood the severity of what he witnessed, and did nothing to protect the child or report the abuse; [2]-As the mother had no right to beat the child so severely, the mother's constitutional rights did not absolve defendant of his responsibilities as the child's guardian to protect her from excessive corporal punishment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re A.D.


DOCKET NO. A-5671-13T1, A-2312-14T1, A-2313-14T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


441 N.J. Super. 403; 119 A.3d 241; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 117


May 27, 2015, Argued 
July 20, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 20, 2015.
Certification granted In re Registrant A.D., 224 N.J. 245, 130 A.3d 1247, 2016 N.J. LEXIS 151 (Feb. 11, 2016)
Affirmed by Matter of Registrant A.D., 227 N.J. 626, 153 A.3d 241, 2017 N.J. LEXIS 155 (Feb. 7, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, (A-5671-13) Burlington County, RCNL No. 2000-03-0025; (A-2312-14) Ocean County, Docket No. ML # 97-15-0188; (A-2313-14) Ocean County, Docket No. ML # 02-15-0032.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court affirmed the orders denying appellant's applications to terminate their obligations under Megan's Law's registration requirements, N.J.S.A. §§ 2C:7-1 to 2C:7-5, because the court found that N.J.S.A. § 2C:7-2(f) was unambiguous and that term offense means what the Code's general definitional subsection defines it to mean; [2]-The court held that appellants' applications were properly denied because each appellant had committed an offense, though not a sex offense, within the 15 year period and the term offense in N.J.S.A. § 2C:7-2(f) means a crime, a disorderly persons offense or a petty disorderly persons offense unless a particular subsection in the code is intended to apply to less than all three and did not mean just a sex offense.


OUTCOME: Orders affirmed.

 

205 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Casser v. Township of Knowlton


DOCKET NO. A-1815-13T4, A-2127-14T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


441 N.J. Super. 353; 118 A.3d 1071; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 112


May 12, 2015, Submitted 
July 7, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 7, 2015.
Certification denied by Casser v. Township of Knowlton, 224 N.J. 123, 129 A.3d 329, 2016 N.J. LEXIS 30 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Warren County, Docket Nos. L-125-10, L-151-13, and L-203-14, and Somerset County, Docket No. L-248-13.
Casser v. Twp. of Knowlton, 2015 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1620 (App.Div., July 7, 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In an action wherein a landowner failed to file a timely prerogative writs action challenging variances granted to her by the local planning board, the court upheld the dismissal of her complaint for failure to exhaust administrative remedies; [2]-The court held that the landowner could not circumvent the exhaustion doctrine by waiting until it was too late to file an action in lieu of prerogative writs and then claim that exhaustion would be futile because the action was time-barred; [3]-The court noted that the landowner was not deprived of the right to develop or sell her land but, to the contrary, she owned about 100 acres of land subject to ten-acre zoning and the township planning board's decision safeguarded her right to subdivide the land and build ten houses.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

206 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Toussaint


DOCKET NO. A-3654-13T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


440 N.J. Super. 526; 114 A.3d 1016; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 78


February 3, 2015, Submitted 
May 14, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 14, 2015.
Certification denied by State v. Tousst, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 945 (N.J., Sept. 9, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, Indictment No. 13-03-0915.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where defendant was convicted under N.J.S.A. § 39:3-40(e) (being involved in an accident that caused injury to another, while driving with a suspended license), and N.J.S.A. § 39:6B-2 (driving without insurance, second offense), the trial court had discretion to permit defendant to serve the sentence in an electronic monitoring program instead of in the county jail; in construing those provisions, the appellate court distinguished State v. French, which had held that N.J.S.A. § 2C:40-26(c) did not permit sentencing alternatives for driving during a second or subsequent license suspension imposed for DWI; [2]-As §§ 39:3-40(e) and 39:6B-2 did not unambiguously require a convicted defendant to serve the required imprisonment term "without parole" or "in the county jail," under the rule of lenity, the trial court had the discretion to permit home electronic monitoring.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

State v. Perry


DOCKET NO. A-1767-13T2, A-1768-13T2, A-1769-13T2, A-1770-13T2, A-2531-13T2, A-2533-13T2, A-2536-13T2

439 N.J. Super. 514; 110 A.3d 122; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 31


October 29, 2014, Argued (A-1767-13, A-1768-13, A-1769-13, A-1770 13, A-2533-13) and Submitted (A-2531-13, A 2536-13) 
March 3, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 3, 2015.
Certification denied by State v. Perry, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 830 (N.J., July 14, 2015)
Certification denied by, Sub nomine at State v. Wisser, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 834 (N.J., July 14, 2015)
Certification denied by, Sub nomine at State v. McIntyre, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 839 (N.J., July 14, 2015)
Certification denied by, Sub nomine at State v. Brewer, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 858 (N.J., July 14, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, Indictment Nos. 13 01-0163 (A-1767-13); 13-05-0689 (A-1768-13); 13-03-0370 (A 1769 13); 13-06-0788 (A 1770 13). On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, Indictment No. 13 02-0624 (A-2531-13). On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County, Indictment No. 13-08-0889 (A-2533-13). On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, Indictment No. 13 03 0600 (A-2536-13).


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In seven consolidated appeals involving the act of driving by the respective defendant occurring beyond the determinate sentenced term of suspension, but before reinstatement, while the driver continued on administrative suspension, the court held that N.J.S.A. § 2C:40-26(a) and (b) criminalizes the operation of a motor vehicle only while the operator is serving the court-imposed term of suspension, and not thereafter; [2]-As a result, the court affirmed the dismissals of the indictments in five of the cases and reversed the denial of the motions to dismiss the indictments in two of the cases.


OUTCOME: Dismissals of indictments in five cases affirmed; denial of motions to dismiss the indictments in two cases reversed.

State v. Faucette


DOCKET NO. A-6123-11T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


439 N.J. Super. 241; 108 A.3d 2; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 10


September 15, 2014, Submitted 
January 15, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 15, 2015.
Certification denied by State v. Faucette, 221 N.J. 492, 114 A.3d 361, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 540 (N.J., May 6, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County, Indictment No. 08-08-0865.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court held that the second interrogation of defendant, separated by 14 hours and preceded by newly administered Miranda warnings, resulted in his voluntary uncoerced choice to reveal his involvement in the crimes under investigation with no poisonous taint from the first interrogation's Miranda violations requiring exclusion of his confession as his confession was not the culmination of coercion carrying over from the previous night, but of his own volition upon learning the new evidence against him.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

In re Pontoriero


DOCKET NO. A-1006-12T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


439 N.J. Super. 24; 106 A.3d 532; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 4


November 18, 2014, Argued 
January 7, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication January 7, 2015.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Waterfront Commission of New York Harbor, Case No. RHA-158.
Waterfront Comm'n of N.Y. Harbor v. Pontoriero, 2012 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 485 (App.Div., Mar. 6, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Appellant sought review of the order of the Waterfront Commission of New York Harbor, which revoked his license to work as a hiring agent on the New Jersey waterfront under the Waterfront Commission Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 32:23-1 to 32:23-225, because of an association with two career offenders, members of a crime family, "inimical to the policies" of the Act, contrary to N.J.S.A. § 32:23-93(6) to (7), and for lack of good character and integrity, contrary to N.J.S.A. §§ 32:23-14(a), 32:23-18(a). The appellate court concluded that the Commission's findings that appellant associated with career offenders, and lacked good character and integrity, were supported by the evidence; [2]-As allowing appellant to continue working would undermine public confidence in the integrity of the operation of the waterfront, revocation of his license was not disproportionate to the offenses.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Rutgers University Student Assembly (RUSA) v. Middlesex County Bd. of Elections


DOCKET NO. A-2383-13T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


438 N.J. Super. 93; 102 A.3d 408; 2014 N.J. Super. LEXIS 156


November 5, 2014, Argued 
November 19, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 19, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Middlesex County, Docket No. C-85-11.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Plaintiffs appealed from the order of the trial court granting the motion of defendants, a county board of elections and a commissioner of registrations, for summary judgment and dismissing plaintiffs' complaint challenging the constitutionality of N.J.S.A. § 19:31-6.3(b), which required all eligible persons to register to vote no later than 21 days prior to an election; plaintiffs also appealed the denial of their motion for summary judgment. Because the trial court did not make adequate findings of fact and conclusions of law concerning defendants' justification for maintaining the 21-day advance registration requirement in the face of the evidence submitted by plaintiffs that the requirement was no longer necessary to protect the integrity of the electoral process, the appellate court was constrained to reverse both decisions and remand for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The judgments were reversed.

Strategic Envtl. Partners, LLC v. New Jersey Dep't of Envtl. Prot.


DOCKET NO. A-5283-12T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


438 N.J. Super. 125; 102 A.3d 939; 2014 N.J. Super. LEXIS 152


September 8, 2014, Argued 
November 13, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 13, 2014
Certification denied by Strategic Environmental Partners, LLC v. New Jersey Dept. of Environmental Protection, 221 N.J. 218, 110 A.3d 931, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 322 (2015)
Related proceeding at State v. Strategic Envtl. Partners, LLC, 2015 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2657 (App.Div., Nov. 19, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection.
Strategic Envtl. Partners, LLC v. Bucco, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 106170 (D.N.J., Aug. 1, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-An emergency order issued by the Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Protection under N.J.S.A. §§ 13:1E-9.5(c) and 13:1E-125.9 enjoined the owner of a solid waste landfill from accepting any material onto the landfill, and authorized the Department to immediately seize control of the landfill to abate an alleged imminent threat to the environment arising from continued emissions of hydrogen sulfide. The Department exceeded its authority under N.J.S.A. § 13:1E-125.4 by seizing control of the landfill without first obtaining judicial approval, and erred in basing the emergency order on past hydrogen sulfide emissions by applying a statutory emissions standard that did not yet exist until the applicable statute was enacted the same morning the order was issued; [2]-The Department had not made the requisite showing to justify an emergency order under § 13:1E-125.9.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the emergency order and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

213 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


In re Winston


DOCKET NO. A-1512-12T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


438 N.J. Super. 1; 101 A.3d 1120; 2014 N.J. Super. LEXIS 148


January 29, 2014, Submitted 
October 31, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 31, 2014.
Certification denied by In re Winston, 220 N.J. 573, 108 A.3d 633, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 256 (N.J., Feb. 2, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County, Municipal Appeal No. 11-061.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The question presented was whether the Full Faith and Credit Clause of the United States Constitution required New Jersey to treat appellant's New York criminal convictions, for which he obtained certificates of relief from disabilities, as not disqualifying him from obtaining a firearms purchaser identification card or a permit to purchase a handgun under N.J.S.A. § 2C:58-3c(1). The appellate court concluded that the Constitution did not compel that result because the certificates of relief did not alter the convictions, but merely removed certain disabilities normally attendant to them under New York law, and New Jersey was not constitutionally required to deem appellant not disqualified from obtain a firearm permit simply because New York saw fit to do so.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of firearms permits.

215 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


In re An Initiative Petition for the Adoption of an Ordinance to Amend the Jackson Twp. Admin. Code


DOCKET NO. A-0517-13T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


437 N.J. Super. 203; 97 A.3d 719; 2014 N.J. Super. LEXIS 127


February 26, 2014, Argued 
September 8, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 8, 2014.
Certification denied by In re Petition for the Adoption of an Ordinance to Amend the Jackson Twp. Admin. Code, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 321 (N.J., Mar. 10, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, Docket No. L-1217-13.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The mayor and council of a governing body made a pre-election challenge to an ordinance proposed in an initiative petition; the trial court declared a section of the ordinance unlawful but, notwithstanding a severance clause in the ordinance, declined to sever the unlawful section and order that the excised ordinance be placed on the ballot. The trial court had the authority under the Declaratory Judgment Act to hear the pre-election challenge to the proposed ordinance. [2]-The trial court correctly concluded that it did not have the authority to revise the ordinance and order that the altered ordinance be placed on the ballot, as N.J.S.A. § 40:69A-191 required that initiative petitions under the Faulkner Act reach the voters in substantially the same form as presented to the petitioners. Thus, the court properly declared the petition and proposed ordinance void.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Borjas


DOCKET NO. A-6292-11T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


436 N.J. Super. 375; 94 A.3d 319; 2014 N.J. Super. LEXIS 97


April 29, 2014, Argued 
July 8, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 8, 2014.
Certification denied by State v. Borjas, 220 N.J. 208, 104 A.3d 1076, 2014 N.J. LEXIS 1419 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, Indictment No. 11-02-0314.
State v. Borjas, 2014 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1632 (App.Div., July 8, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant was convicted of knowingly making and knowingly possessing false government documents (N.J.S.A. § 2C:21-2.1(b) and (d)); the incriminating items were created or stored in hard drives on computers at his residence, but officers discovered no printouts of the false items. The appellate court rejected his argument that § 2C:21-2.1(b) and (d) were unconstitutionally overbroad because they allegedly infringed too much upon protected forms of expression; [2]-The statute was not void for vagueness because it lacked an express element requiring the State to prove a defendant's specific intent to use the false items for illicit purposes; [3]-The trial judge's jury instruction defining the term "document" under § 2C:21-2.1 to encompass items or images stored on a computer was consistent with the broader meaning associated with the term "document" in common modern usage.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

217 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Campbell


DOCKET NO. A-5535-12T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


436 N.J. Super. 264; 93 A.3d 416; 2014 N.J. Super. LEXIS 90


May 28, 2014, Argued 
June 27, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 27, 2014.
Certification denied by State v. Campbell, 2014 N.J. LEXIS 1403 (N.J., Dec. 11, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, Summons No. 0112209587-590.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether defendant was properly convicted of DWI and denied relief on his claim that N.J.S.A. § 39:4-50(a) was unconstitutional. HOLDINGS: [1]-His Alcotest BAC reading was above the per se level of.08 prohibited by § 39:4-50(a); he argued that admission of Alcotest results based on "clear-and-convincing" proof, coupled with the conclusively incriminating treatment of a BAC at or above.08, relieved the State of its constitutional burden of proving a guilt "beyond a reasonable doubt." He failed to distinguish the State's initial burden of establishing the Alcotest's admissibility from its ultimate burden of establishing guilt of a per se offense beyond a reasonable doubt; [2]-Even if a pretrial motion to suppress the BAC results was denied, a defendant could present evidence that the testing procedures were flawed and that his guilt had not been proven beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Berg v. Christie


DOCKET NO. A-5973-11T4, A-6002-11T4, A-0632-12T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


436 N.J. Super. 220; 93 A.3d 387; 2014 N.J. Super. LEXIS 92


January 28, 20141, Argued


1 After oral argument, we directed supplemental briefing, which was completed on February 25, 2014.

 
June 26, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 26, 2014.
Certification granted by Berg v. Christie, 222 N.J. 311, 118 A.3d 351, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 850 (2015)
Certification granted by Berg v. Christie, 222 N.J. 311, 118 A.3d 351, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 843 (2015)
Reversed by, Judgment entered by Berg v. Christie, 2016 N.J. LEXIS 561 (N.J., June 9, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, Docket Nos. L-2996-11 and L-1354-12.
N.J. Educ. Ass'n v. New Jersey, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 142301 (D.N.J., Dec. 12, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in granting state officials summary judgment dismissing the claims of plaintiffs, active and retired public employees, challenging the constitutionality of the suspension of their COLAs under N.J.S.A. § 43:3B-2. Construing 1997 pension legislation, the appellate court concluded that the legislature intended to create a contractual right to receive pension benefits, including COLAs, and that plaintiffs' claims for payment of benefits from the pension funds were not barred by the Debt Limitation and Appropriations Clauses of the New Jersey Constitution; remand was required to determine if the State could satisfy the constitutional standard it had to meet to justify impairing the obligation of a contract; [2]-In a second case, as retired police officers raised separate arguments that were meritless, the officials were properly granted summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment in the first case was reversed; the judgment in the second case was affirmed.

State in Interest of Y.C.


DOCKET NO. A-1030-13T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


436 N.J. Super. 29; 91 A.3d 636; 2014 N.J. Super. LEXIS 78


May 13, 2014, Argued 
June 5, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 5, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the State of New Jersey, New Jersey Juvenile Justice Commission and Department of Corrections.
State ex rel. J.J., 427 N.J. Super. 541, 49 A.3d 877, 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 147 (App.Div., 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court held that the Juvenile Justice Commission's (JJC's) interim policy on transferring juveniles to adult prisons was invalid, because it was not adopted in compliance with the Administrative Procedures Act, N.J.S.A. § 52:14B-4; [2]-The court also found that the JJC's action in transferring the juvenile to an adult facility was contrary to case law, which invalidated the JJC's transfer regulations and indicated that the agency must adopt new regulations before transferring a juvenile to an adult prison; [3]-The court ordered that the JJC give the juvenile a new transfer hearing, to be conducted by the Office of Administrative Law, and ordered the JJC to adopt new regulations within 180 days.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded to JJC for a new transfer hearing; JJC ordered to adopt new regulations within 180 days.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 9, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Salem County, Indictment No. 09-12-00629.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court held that the drug-trafficking recidivist provision in N.J.S.A. § 2C:43-6(f) cannot be the basis to impose a mandatory extended term for the offense of drug trafficking within 500 feet of a public housing facility under N.J.S.A. § 2C:35-7.1 because the statute has never been amended to add the subsequently enacted N.J.S.A. 2C:35-7.1 to its list of drug trafficking offenses for which an extended term is required; [2]-As such, the trial court improperly sentenced defendant under N.J.S.A. § 2C:43-6(f) as a court cannot rewrite a statute; [3]-The court further held that because defendant attempted to explain away the cash in his pocket by using his post-arrest statement that he was unemployed and that he won the money gambling, the prosecutor's reference to his statement and his unemployment was not reversible error.


OUTCOME: Convictions affirmed; sentences vacated and case remanded to trial court for resentencing.

232 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Heyert v. Taddese


DOCKET NO. A-4801-10T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


431 N.J. Super. 388; 70 A.3d 681; 2013 N.J. Super. LEXIS 97


April 29, 2013, Argued 
June 25, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication June 25, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, Docket No. L-1247-10/L-1460-10 (consolidated).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landlords challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, in favor of plaintiff tenants. The tenants brought suit alleging that the landlords violated the New Jersey Consumer Fraud Act (CFA), N.J.S.A. § 56:8-1 et seq., by charging rent in excess of that allowed by local rent control ordinances. The tenants had filed respective actions in lieu of prerogative writs.


OVERVIEW: The tenants had also challenged the local municipality's grant of the landlords' hardship rent increase request. At the hearing, the landlords claimed that the municipality's rent control ordinance was unconstitutional and that the legal base rent calculated under the ordinance was arbitrary, capricious and unreasonable. The trial court vacated the hardship rent increase and dismissed the landlords' challenge to the legal base rent calculations and, in ruling on motions for summary judgment, found in favor of the tenants on their CFA claim. The court entered final judgment in favor of the tenants for treble the amount of excess rent of $ 59,466, and for attorney fees and costs. The court upheld the grant of summary judgment to the tenants on their CFA claim because the landlords knew about the rent control ordinance, charged rent in excess of that ordinance, and were in the business of renting apartments. As such, the trial court properly concluded that no genuine issue of material fact existed as to whether the landlords made an affirmative misrepresentation by raising the rents in violation of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Paff v. New Jersey State Firemen's Ass'n


DOCKET NO. A-4111-11T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


431 N.J. Super. 278; 69 A.3d 118; 2013 N.J. Super. LEXIS 90


November 1, 2012, Argued 
June 13, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication June 13, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, Docket No. L-4371-11.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff requestor challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, which dismissed the complaint against defendant, the New Jersey State Firemen's Association, under the Open Public Records Act (OPRA), N.J.S.A. §§ 47:1A-1 to 47:1A-13.


OVERVIEW: In response to plaintiff's suit, defendant maintained that it was not a public agency; therefore, OPRA did not require it to permit plaintiff to inspect its records. The trial court agreed and dismissed plaintiff's verified complaint to compel access. The court found error, concluding that defendant was a public agency under OPRA. The court held that defendant was created pursuant to state law, N.J.S.A. § 43:17-41, and was the direct recipient of taxes on certain fire insurance premiums, pursuant to N.J.S.A. §§ 54:18-1 and 54:18-2. The court further held that under N.J.S.A. § 17:22-6.59, defendant was an independent State instrumentality and, therefore, a public agency, pursuant to N.J.S.A. § 47:1A-1.1. As such, the trial court erred in concluding otherwise.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Maeker v. Ross


DOCKET NO. A-3034-11T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


430 N.J. Super. 79; 62 A.3d 310; 2013 N.J. Super. LEXIS 18


September 12, 2012, Argued 
February 4, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication February 4, 2013.
Certification granted by Maeker v. Ross, 215 N.J. 485, 73 A.3d 511, 2013 N.J. LEXIS 859 (2013)
Reversed by, Remanded by Maeker v. Ross, 2014 N.J. LEXIS 910 (N.J., Sept. 25, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Somerset County, Docket No. FM-18-126-12.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant former boyfriend appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Somerset County, which denied his motion to dismiss plaintiff former girlfriend's palimony complaint and that granted her cross-motion for pendente lite support, which the motion judge fixed at $ 6,000 per month.


OVERVIEW: The motion judge found that plaintiff's complaint was not barred by the 2010 amendment to the Statute of Frauds, N.J.S.A. § 25:1-5(h) (Amendment), requiring a writing memorializing palimony agreements and independent advice of counsel for each party in advance of executing any such agreement. The court found error, concluding that the Amendment was enforcement legislation that addresses under what circumstances a claimed breach of a palimony agreement may be enforced irrespective of when the purported agreement was entered. The court held that the trial court erred in finding that the Amendment applied only to palimony agreements entered after the January 18, 2010, effective date of the amendment. Since the purported palimony agreement between the parties did not comply with the Amendment, plaintiff's complaint failed to state a cause of action. As such, the court held that the trial court erred in ordering defendant to pay pendente lite support and an award of counsel fees to plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and held that the Amendment was enforcement legislation that addresses under what circumstances a claimed breach of a palimony agreement may be enforced irrespective of when the purported agreement was entered.

 

236 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pomianek


DOCKET NO. A-2694-10T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


429 N.J. Super. 339; 58 A.3d 1205; 2013 N.J. Super. LEXIS 10; 117 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 479


October 23, 2012, Submitted 
January 30, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication January 30, 2013.
Certification granted by State v. Pomianek, 216 N.J. 359, 80 A.3d 742, 2013 N.J. LEXIS 1275 (2013)
Certification granted by State v. Pomianek, 216 N.J. 363, 80 A.3d 745, 2013 N.J. LEXIS 1276 (2013)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by, Dismissed by, in part State v. Pomianek, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 275 (N.J., Mar. 17, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, Indictment No. 0902-0646.
Brodie v. Gloucester Twp., 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 12260 (D.N.J., Feb. 1, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, which convicted him of harassment by communication, N.J.S.A. § 2C:33-4(a); harassment by alarming conduct, N.J.S.A. § 2C:33-4(c); bias intimidation, N.J.S.A. § 2C:16-1(a)(3); and, official misconduct, N.J.S.A. § 2C:30-2(a), following a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had worked for a township and his convictions arose from an incident in which an African-American co-worker was locked in an equipment cage and taunted. On appeal, defendant asserted that the bias intimidation statute, N.J.S.A. § 2C:16-1(a)(3), was unconstitutional. The court determined that § 2C:16-1(a)(3) would be unconstitutional if it permitted a defendant to be convicted of a bias offense based on the victim's perception of the defendant's conduct, without requiring the State to prove defendant's biased intent in committing the underlying crime. Thus, to avoid an interpretation that would render the provision unconstitutional, and to effectuate the New Jersey Legislature's purpose in enacting the statute, as reflected in the legislative history, the court held that subsection (3) required proof of defendant's biased intent. Since the jury in the case was instructed that it could consider the victim's perception of the crime, rather than defendant's intent in committing it, that conviction required reversal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for bias intimidation as well as his conviction for official misconduct, because it was based solely on the underlying, invalid conviction for bias intimidation. The court affirmed the harassment convictions and remanded the case to the trial court for a re-trial on the charges of bias intimidation and official misconduct.

 

237 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


D.N. v. K.M.


DOCKET NO. A-3021-11T3, A-3022-11T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


429 N.J. Super. 592; 61 A.3d 150; 2013 N.J. Super. LEXIS 6


December 11, 2012, Argued 
January 24, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication January 24, 2013.
Certification denied by D.N. v. K.M., 2014 N.J. LEXIS 8 (N.J., Jan. 13, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Burlington County, Docket Nos. FV-03-876-12 and FV-03-864-12.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, appellant ex-girlfriend challenged the orders of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Burlington County, which granted respondent ex-boyfriend a final restraining order against her and that dismissed her complaint for domestic violence against the ex-boyfriend.


OVERVIEW: The parties were unmarried and shared a teenage child. They had previously resided with each other but, in contemplation of the termination of their relationship, they entered into a consent order granting the ex-boyfriend exclusive use of the residence they had shared and named him as the parent of primary residence. On appeal, the ex-girlfriend asserted that the trial court erred in finding the evidence insufficient to support her complaint for domestic violence against the ex-boyfriend. The court disagreed, finding that the evidence established that she was not injured by the ex-boyfriend's vehicle but that she purposefully violated the order granting the ex-boyfriend exclusive possession of the home as she admitted the same, and the testimony from the ex-boyfriend was sufficient to show that she punched and smacked him in the face at least several times. The court also held that the ex-girlfriend understood her right to employ counsel and that she clearly and intentionally relinquished that right. The court further held that the ex-girlfriend was not entitled to assigned counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

 

238 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


In re Veto by Governor Chris Christie of Minutes of New Jersey Racing Comm'n from June 29


DOCKET NO. A-6028-10T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


429 N.J. Super. 277; 58 A.3d 735; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 186


September 11, 2012, Argued 
December 7, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication December 7, 2012.
Certification denied by In re Veto by Governor Chris Christie of the Minutes of the N.J. Racing Comm'n from the June 29, 2013 N.J. LEXIS 639 (N.J., June 4, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Racing Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A race horse breeders' association filed suit, seeking to reverse the New Jersey Governor's veto of the minutes of a meeting of the New Jersey Racing Commission and to remand the matter to the Commission with instructions to reconsider distribution of funds to stakeholders in New Jersey's horse racing and breeding industry.


OVERVIEW: The Commission decided to distribute $ 15 million collected by the New Jersey Casino Redevelopment Authority (CRDA) for the purpose of augmenting "purse monies" at New Jersey racing venues. The association challenged the constitutionality of the legislative scheme, adopted as part of the creation of the Atlantic City Tourism District, that expressly permitted the Commission to request the monies for this purpose and the CRDA to distribute them, but, at the same time, preserved the Governor's power under N.J.S.A. § 5:5-22.1 to veto the Commission's minutes, thereby rendering any action taken null and void. The appellate court examined the various constitutional arguments made by the association and rejected them. The association also argued that, even if the legislative scheme was constitutional and the Governor's veto permissible, his action was arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable. The appellate court concluded that its usual standard of review applicable to executive agency action did not apply to the discretionary actions of the Governor pursuant to the express legislative grant embodied in § 5:5-22.1.


OUTCOME: The Governor's veto was affirmed.

 

239 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Santiago v. New York & New Jersey Port Authority


DOCKET NO. A-5773-10T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


429 N.J. Super. 150; 57 A.3d 54; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 184


September 25, 2012, Argued 
December 5, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication December 5, 2012.
Certification denied by Santiago v. New York & N.J. Port Auth., Tunnel, 2013 N.J. LEXIS 769 (N.J., July 9, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, Docket No. L-5545-10.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former worker appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, which granted the motion to dismiss filed by defendants, the Port Authority of New York and New Jersey (the Port Authority), and one of its employees. Plaintiff's suit alleged wrongful termination of her employment with the Port Authority after what she alleged was a sham internal investigation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's suit alleged violations of the New Jersey Conscientious Employee Protection Act, N.J.S.A. § 34:19-1 et seq., the New Jersey Law Against Discrimination, N.J.S.A. § 10:5-1 et seq., common law claims for abuse of process, interference with contractual rights, defamation, and claims for violations under the New Jersey Constitution. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss upon agreeing with defendants that plaintiff failed to serve any notice of claim prior to filing her complaint, as required by N.J.S.A. § 32:1-163. The court agreed and held that the Port Authority's waiver of sovereign immunity and limited consent to suit was expressly conditioned on pre-litigation notice. Given the failure to provide such notice on the part of plaintiff, the trial court lacked subject matter litigation, regardless of the nature of plaintiff's claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

240 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carrigan


DOCKET NO. A-3751-11T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


428 N.J. Super. 609; 55 A.3d 87; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 178


October 22, 2012, Argued 
November 15, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication November 15, 2012.
Certification denied by State v. Carrigan, 213 N.J. 539, 65 A.3d 263, 2013 N.J. LEXIS 457 (2013)
Related proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Carrigan, 2016 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 79 (App.Div., Jan. 14, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, Municipal Appeal No. W2011-451-1518.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with driving under a suspended license in violation of N.J.S.A. § 2C:40-26(b). The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, granted defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint; the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Section 2C:40-26(b), which became effective on August 1, 2011, made it a fourth-degree crime for a motorist to operate a vehicle at a time when his or her driver's license was suspended or revoked for a second or subsequent conviction for driving while intoxicated (DWI) or refusal to submit to an alcohol breath test. Defendant was charged with that crime, upon being found driving a car in September 2011 while his license was suspended due to multiple prior DWI offenses. The trial court dismissed the complaint, concluding that the application of § 2C:40-26(b) to defendant violated ex post facto principles, essentially because his ongoing license suspensions had been imposed before § 2C:40-26(b)'s effective date. The appellate court disagreed. It concluded that a violation of § 2C:40- 26(b) comprised a new offense based upon new conduct, and that it did not impose retrospective punishment for a prior offense. Hence, the law could be constitutionally applied to drivers with suspended licenses, such as defendant, who were caught driving after August 1, 2011, regardless of whether their DWI-based suspensions were imposed before that date.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the criminal complaint was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

241 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. McInerney


DOCKET NO. A-5292-09T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


428 N.J. Super. 432; 54 A.3d 281; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 163


January 9, 2012, Argued 
October 10, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication October 10, 2012.
Certification denied by State v. McInerney, 214 N.J. 175, 68 A.3d 890, 2013 N.J. LEXIS 745 (July 9, 2013)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. McInerney, 2017 N.J. Super. LEXIS 70 (App.Div., June 9, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County, Indictment No. 08-10-2334.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County, defendant was convicted of 10 counts of the second degree crime of endangering the welfare of a child (N.J.S.A. § 2C:24-4(a)). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a high school athletic coach, directed the student-victims to masturbate instead of having intercourse with girls, thereby avoiding unwanted pregnancies, and paid them to send him reports about their masturbatory practices. The appellate court held that the evidence was sufficient to prove that defendant "assumed responsibility for the care of a child" within the meaning of § 2C:24-4(a) by assuming the role of a regular supervisor in matters suitable for parental oversight and wholly unrelated to performance and behavior on the playing field. However, defendant's conviction for second-degree child endangerment could not stand because the trial court's jury instruction, patterned after the New Jersey Model Jury Charge, allowed for a conviction based on a relationship between defendant and student-victims not statutorily prescribed. The trial court directed the jurors that under appropriate circumstances, one who assumed responsibility for the care of a child could include a staff member of a school, but did not, however, explain what the "appropriate circumstances" were and effectively left the legal standard to the judgment of the jurors.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

242 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Gonzalez v. State Apportionment Com'n


DOCKET NO. A-0747-11T4, A-0869-11T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


428 N.J. Super. 333; 53 A.3d 1230; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 149


June 6, 2012, Argued 
September 10, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication September 10, 2012.
Certification denied by Gonzalez v. State Apportionment Comm'n, 2013 N.J. LEXIS 133 (N.J., Jan. 22, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, Docket No. L-1173-11.
Gonzalez v. State Apportionment Comm'n, 2011 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2366 (Law Div., Aug. 31, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff voters appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, which dismissed its complaint against defendants, the State of New Jersey Apportionment Commission (the Commission) and others, challenging the legislative apportionment map approved by the Commission on April 3, 2011.


OVERVIEW: The approved map established New Jersey State Senate and Assembly districts and the apportionment of State Senators and members of the General Assembly among those districts. Plaintiffs contended that the approved map violated various provisions of the New Jersey Constitution by failing to construct New Jersey Assembly districts as nearly compact and equal in the number of their inhabitants as possible and with no or as few as possible county or municipal splits. The trial court found that the plaintiffs failed to state a claim for relief. The court agreed with the trial court's dismissal, finding that it was obligated to follow New Jersey Supreme Court precedent which has established that counties cannot constitute separate districts and are not suitable building blocks for the formation of meaningful districts. The court found that the Commission reasonably viewed its task as unconstrained by a need to create districts within the borders of county lines and that plaintiffs did not make a showing that demographic data shifts had changed the facts from the 1970 Census in a way that would now allow for effective redistricting using county lines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order which dismissed plaintiffs' complaint.

State ex rel. J.J.


DOCKET NO. A-2357-11T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


427 N.J. Super. 541; 49 A.3d 877; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 147


June 6, 2012, Argued 
August 28, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 28, 2012.
Related proceeding at State ex rel Y.C., 2014 N.J. Super. LEXIS 78 (App.Div., June 5, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Juvenile Justice Commission and the Department of Corrections.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner juvenile appealed the order of respondent, the Juvenile Justice Commission (JJC), which transferred him from the custody of the JJC to respondent, the New Jersey Department of Corrections (DOC). The juvenile commenced the action in the Family Part to contest the transfer, seeking return to the custody of the JJC and a declaration that the transfer regulations, N.J.A.C. 13:91-1.1 to 13:91-2.5, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether procedural due process rights should be accorded to an adjudicated juvenile prior to transfer from a juvenile facility operated by the JJC to an adult correctional facility operated by the DOC, pursuant to the provisions of N.J.S.A. § 52:17B-175(e), which permits such transfers. The court held that the rehabilitative purposes of the juvenile justice system combined with the importance of the decision in terms of the availability of rehabilitative services to juveniles at issue required due process at least as extensive as that required for prison discipline. The court held that at a minimum, before a juvenile can be transferred to custody of the DOC, there must be written notice of the proposed transfer and the supporting factual basis, an impartial decision maker, an opportunity to be heard and to present opposition, some form of representation, and written findings of fact supporting a decision to proceed with the transfer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order transferring the juvenile to the custody of the DOC and ordered his return to the custody of the JJC. The court remanded the case to the JJC for further proceedings.

State v. Lenihan


DOCKET NO. A-4667-10T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


427 N.J. Super. 499; 49 A.3d 415; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 140


March 6, 2012, Argued 
August 13, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 13, 2012.
Certification granted State v. Lenihan, 213 N.J. 386, 63 A.3d 226, 2013 N.J. LEXIS 233 (2013)
Affirmed by State v. Lenihan, 2014 N.J. LEXIS 900 (N.J., Sept. 18, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Sussex County, Indictment No. 09-02-00086.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with, inter alia, second-degree violation of a public safety law and recklessly causing death, N.J.S.A. § 2C:40-18(a). The predicate public safety law was the seat belt law, N.J.S.A. § 39:3-76.2f. Pursuant to a plea bargain, she tendered a guilty plea to a third-degree violation of § 2C:40-18(a), which was accepted by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Sussex County. She then appealed her conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lost control of her car, which struck a guard rail; her 16-year-old passenger died of injuries sustained in the crash. Neither had been wearing a seat belt. Defendant was charged with her and her passenger's failure to wear a seat belt, in violation of § 39:3-76.2f(a) and (b). She argued that the seat belt law was not a law "intended to protect the public health and safety" as contemplated by § 2C:40-18(b). The appellate court disagreed. Section 39:3-76.2f was clearly a law addressed and enacted to protect the public health and safety, and § 2C:40-18 had no express or implied limitations as to the type of public health and safety offense that could serve as a predicate violation. The appellate court rejected her claim that § 2C:40-18 was unconstitutionally vague. It was not required to consider her hypothetical examples suggesting that violations of municipal ordinances that were arguably public health and safety laws could be elevated to more serious crimes through the application of § 2C:40-18, as she could test the statute for vagueness as applied only with respect to her particular conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Township of Jefferson v. Director, Div. of Taxation


DOCKET NO. A-3013-10T3, DOCKET NO. A-0613-11T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


427 N.J. Super. 347; 48 A.3d 1126; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 134


May 15, 2012, Argued 
August 6, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 6, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey, Docket No. 20479-2010, whose opinion is reported at 26 N.J. Tax 1 (Tax 2011) and Docket No. 1746-2011, whose opinion is reported at 26 N.J. Tax 129 (Tax 2011).
Township of Jefferson v. Morris County Bd. of Taxation, 26 N.J. Tax 129, 2011 N.J. Tax LEXIS 10 (Tax Ct., 2011)
Township of Jefferson v. Director, Div. of Taxation, 26 N.J. Tax 1, 2011 N.J. Tax LEXIS 3 (Tax Ct., 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff township challenged the Table of Equalized Valuations promulgated by defendant, the Director of the New Jersey Division of Taxation, as well as defendant county board of taxation's county equalization table, which was based on the Director's Equalization Table, which the county had adopted. The Tax Court of New Jersey rejected the township's challenges; the township appealed.


OVERVIEW: The township argued that use of the equalization table was unconstitutional and statutorily prohibited. The township's expert did not know what impact there would be on the township's county taxes if the board uniformly stopped averaging in all county municipalities in which real estate markets were declining. As a result, the tax court found that the township had failed to proffer definite evidence that the average ratio promulgated in the county equalization table was arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable. It rejected the argument that N.J.S.A. §§ 54:4-2.25 and 54:4-2.26 prohibited the board from apportioning the township's share of county taxes based on the average ratio of 94.34 percent since the ratio was based on an average true value in excess of the township's equalized true value. It clarified that §§ 54:4-2.25 and 54:4-2.26 did not apply to the Director, but only to county boards of taxation. The tax court found that the township had failed factually to overcome the presumption in favor of the county equalization table, and rejected its statutory and constitutional arguments. The appellate court held that the tax court's analysis of the facts and the law was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

247 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


In re New Jersey State Funeral Directors Ass'n


DOCKET NO. A-0177-11T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


427 N.J. Super. 268; 48 A.3d 391; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 130


May 29, 2012, Argued 
July 26, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication July 26, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Department of Law and Public Safety, Division of Consumer Affairs, State Board of Mortuary Science.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a state funeral directors association, filed suit challenging amendments adding N.J.A.C. 13:36-4.9(c), 13:36-5.17(c) and 13:36-5.18(a), that were adopted by respondent, the New Jersey Department of Law and Public Safety, Division of Consumer Affairs, State Board of Mortuary Science (Board).


OVERVIEW: The amendments were proposed to clarify a registered mortuary's responsibilities with respect to the participation of unlicensed persons in the removal and preparation of bodies for disposition. The association challenged the amendments as exceeding the Board's regulatory authority, unconstitutionally vague and arbitrary and unreasonable in that they required registered morticians to do the impossible. The appellate court held that the amendments had none of those defects. Taken together, they imposed no obligation on a registered mortuary to monitor unlicensed persons until after it assumed responsibility to direct the removal of human remains pursuant to § 13:36-5.17(b) or did so at some later point between death and final disposition. Because the Board understood §§ 13:36-4.9(c), 13:36-5.17(c), and 13:36-5.18(a) to require no more than reasonable efforts by registered mortuaries to ensure compliance with discernible objective standards in furtherance of the Board's obligation to protect the public health, these amendments were not impermissibly vague.


OUTCOME: The amendments were affirmed.

 

248 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


G.D.M. v. Board of Educ. of the Ramapo Indian Hills Regional High School Dist.


DOCKET NO. A-0953-10T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


427 N.J. Super. 246; 48 A.3d 378; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 127


March 21, 2012, Argued 
July 24, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication July 24, 2012.
Certification denied by G.D.M. v. Bd. of Educ. of the Ramapo Indian Hills Reg'l High Sch. Dist., 2013 N.J. LEXIS 62 (N.J., Jan. 14, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Department of Education, Docket No. 225-9/09.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner parents, on behalf of themselves and their minor child, challenged a regulation enacted by respondent local board of education that allowed the board to suspend students from participating in extracurricular activities based on misconduct occurring off school grounds. The then acting commissioner of education invalidated the regulation. The board appealed and petitioners cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: This appeal presented a facial challenge to the validity of a regulation, promulgated by the board, that sought to control student conduct not only at school or during school related functions and activities, but at all other times and places. The regulation asserted this control by conditioning student participation in extracurricular activities on compliance with a specifically enumerated code of student conduct, without requiring a nexus between the alleged violation of law and school order or safety. The commissioner invalidated the regulation because it exceeded the authority conferred upon local school boards to regulate student conduct under N.J.A.C. 6A:16-7.1 and 6A:16-7.6. She found that § 6A:16-7.6 allowed the board to suspend a student's participation in extracurricular activities for conduct away from school grounds only where 1) the activity substantially interfered with the requirements of discipline in the school's operation, and 2) the suspension was reasonably necessary for the student's physical or emotional safety and well-being or for the safety and well-being of other students, teachers, or school property. The appellate court agreed with this interpretation.


OUTCOME: The commissioner's determination was affirmed, and petitioners' cross-appeal was dismissed.

Estate of Kosakowski v. Director, New Jersey Div. of Taxation


DOCKET NO. A-4499-10T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


427 N.J. Super. 147; 47 A.3d 760; 26 N.J. Tax 524; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 117


February 15, 2012, Argued 
July 11, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:
Approved for Publication July 11, 2012.
Certification granted by Estate of Stanley Kosakowski v. Director, 56 A.3d 395, 2012 N.J. LEXIS 1217 (N.J., Nov. 5, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey, Docket No. 004620-2005, whose opinion is reported at 26 N.J. Tax 21 (Tax 2011).
Estate of Kosakowski v. Director, Div. of Taxation, 26 N.J. Tax 21, 2011 N.J. Tax LEXIS 5 (Tax Ct., 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Director of the New Jersey Division of Taxation, denied appellant estate's refund claim. The estate appealed; the Tax Court of New Jersey granted the Director's motion for summary judgment. The estate sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Due to the retroactive application of amendments to N.J.S.A. § 54:38-1, the estate's tax liability was increased. The tax court found that the doctrine of manifest injustice was inapplicable because the decedent did not rely to his detriment on the former version of § 54:38-1 when drafting his will. The appellate court approved the opinion of the tax court as consonant with the application of the doctrine of manifest injustice as expressed by a plurality of the New Jersey Supreme Court in its decision in Oberhand v. Director, Division of Taxation. Manifest injustice was an equitable principle that could be applied to relieve the adverse consequences of the retroactive application of amended tax legislation in circumstances in which such relief was warranted, and those circumstances were not present in the instant case. The tax court also properly ruled that the retroactive application of § 54:38-1 did not violate the estate's equal protection or due process rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

250 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


In re Board's Main Extension Rules N.J.A.C. 14:3-8.1


DOCKET NO. A-1626-10T2, A-1640-10T2, A-2206-10T2, A-2227-10T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


426 N.J. Super. 538; 46 A.3d 560; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 104


March 13, 2012, Argued 
June 22, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication June 22, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Board of Public Utilities.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, appellant developers challenged the decision of respondent, the New Jersey Board of Public Utilities (BPU), refusing to grant the case law decision entitled Centex full retroactive effect. In Centex, the court invalidated as ultra vires the 2005 BPU regulations known as the Main Extension Rules, N.J.A.C. 14:3-8.1 to 14:3-8.13.


OVERVIEW: The Main Extension Rules required utility companies to pay for the extension of utility lines to new homes in designated smart growth areas of the State of New Jersey, but forced the developer or the homeowner to absorb that cost in portions of the State that were not so designated. Despite the court's sweeping invalidation of the Main Extension Rules, BPU chose to afford the Centex decision only pipeline retroactivity, confining the benefit of Centex to only 18 developers, and denying the benefit of Centex to hundreds of others. The court held that because its opinion in Centex did not announce a new rule of law, but instead accomplished the reinstatement of a well-accepted and well understood century-long procedure, the pipeline retroactivity ordered by BPU was error. The court held that complete retroactivity of Centex was required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed BPU's pipeline retroactivity decision. The court remanded the case to BPU for the adoption of a regulation establishing the procedures for granting refunds to all developers and homeowners affected by the ultra vires 2005 regulation.

 

251 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


N.G. v. J.P.


DOCKET NO. A-3247-10T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


426 N.J. Super. 398; 45 A.3d 371; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 97


May 30, 2012, Argued 
June 18, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication June 18, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Essex County, Docket No. FV-07-321-11.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brother appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Essex County, which granted plaintiff sister a final restraining order (FRO) against him under the Prevention of Domestic Violence Act of 1991 (the Act), N.J.S.A. §§ 2C:25-17 to 2C:25-35.


OVERVIEW: The parties were adult siblings who had not resided together since 1960, when they were both children. The court held that the trial court properly exercised jurisdiction even though the parties had not resided together for such a long period because the harassment of plaintiff by defendant over the intervening decades, although sporadic, conferred jurisdiction to issue the FRO in light of the fact that the present incidents arose directly from the parties' acrimonious family relationship and their status as former household members. The court affirmed the issuance of the ban on defendant from entering the township wherein plaintiff resided but found that a remand was necessary to hold a hearing to give defendant a fuller opportunity to describe his church attendance and any visits to his doctors. The court found no error with the trial court's findings that defendant's conduct constituted stalking and harassment as predicate findings under the Act, N.J.S.A. § 2C:25-19(a)(13)-(14), based on defendant picketing at plaintiff's residence as well as threatening plaintiff by means of offensive hand gestures, shouting curses at her, and blocking her exiting from her property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment but remanded the case to the Family Part for the limited purpose of entertaining defendant's request for a narrowing of the ban on his entry into the confines of the township.

 

252 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


In re Langan Engineering & Environmental Services, Inc.


DOCKET NO. A-2145-11T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


425 N.J. Super. 577; 42 A.3d 240; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 75


April 24, 2012, Argued 
May 15, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication May 15, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Division of Purchase and Property, Department of the Treasury.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the New Jersey Department of the Treasury, Division of Purchase and Property, determined that appellant corporation was disqualified from being awarded state contracts because it had made a political contribution within the 18-month period preceding its submission of a bid. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: N.J.S.A. § 19:44A-20.14 of the New Jersey Campaign Contributions and Expenditure Reporting Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 19:44A-1 to 19:44A-26, provided that a business entity was disqualified from the award of a state contract if the firm made a political contribution within the 18-month period immediately preceding the "commencement of negotiations." Appellant argued that a business entity that made a political contribution could not participate in a government contract exceeding $ 17,500 for 18 months after making the contribution. The appellate court disagreed. In the context of publicly-bid contracts, the appellate court construed the term "commencement of negotiations" to be the date the bid was submitted. As appellant, because of its campaign contribution, was disqualified under § 19:44A-20.14 on the date when bids were due, the Division properly ruled that it was not eligible to be awarded the contract. The appellate court rejected appellant's claim that an executive order's extension of contribution limits to legislative leadership committees was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The Division's determination was affirmed.

 

253 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gibson


DOCKET NO. A-1513-10T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


425 N.J. Super. 523; 42 A.3d 208; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 64


April 17, 2012, Submitted 
May 8, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication May 8, 2012.
Certification granted by State v. Gibson, 212 N.J. 460, 56 A.3d 395, 2012 N.J. LEXIS 1225 (2012)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Gibson, 2014 N.J. LEXIS 1 (N.J., Jan. 7, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County, Indictment Nos. 08-03-0299 and 08-08-0882.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County, which convicted him on drug offenses, in violation of N.J.S.A. § 2C:35-5(a)(1) and (b)(3) and, with regard to a 2009 indictment, third-degree controlled dangerous substance possession with the intent to distribute within 1000 feet of school property, in violation of N.J.S.A. § 2C:35-7, following his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended on appeal that the trial judge erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence seized from him following his arrest for defiant trespass because by the time of the search, the arresting officer did not possess probable cause that defendant had engaged in a defiant trespass because the owner of the property had posted a no loitering instead of a no trespassing sign. The court rejected defendant's arguments. The court found that the lateness of the hour, defendant's immediate departure from the property upon seeing the officer, and his excited and evasive demeanor when questioned were all specific and articulable facts that gave the officer a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity. Further, when defendant failed to assert that he was on the property with permission, the officer possessed probable cause to arrest him for defiant trespass. The court further held that no loitering was a message sufficient to convey the same meaning as no trespassing, therefore, such a direction did not preclude the officer from reasonably concluding that defendant was engaged in criminal activity by leaning against the porch of the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

254 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


In re Plan for Abolition of Council on Affordable Housing


DOCKET NO. A-6301-10T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


424 N.J. Super. 410; 38 A.3d 620; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 33


February 15, 2012, Argued 
March 8, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication March 8, 2012.
Related proceeding at In re Adoption of Five Interim Procedures by the Dep't of Cmty. Affairs, 2012 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 499 (App.Div., Mar. 8, 2012)
Certification granted by In re Plan for the Abolition of the Council on Affordable Housing, 211 N.J. 274, 48 A.3d 355, 2012 N.J. LEXIS 791 (2012)
Modified by, Affirmed by In re Plan for the Abolition of the Council on Affordable Housing, 214 N.J. 444, 70 A.3d 559, 2013 N.J. LEXIS 727 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Governor's Reorganization Plan No. 001-2011, issued June 29, 2011.
In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 5:94 & 5:95 By New Jersey Council On Affordable Housing, 390 N.J. Super. 1, 914 A.2d 348, 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 20 (App.Div., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a fair share housing organization, challenged an executive order of respondent, the Governor of the State of New Jersey, which abolished the Council on Affordable Housing (COAH), pursuant to the Executive Reorganization Act of 1969 (Reorganization Act), N.J.S.A. §§ 52:14C-1 to 52:14C-11. The Governor had issued a reorganization plan, which had the stated purpose of abolishing COAH.


OVERVIEW: COAH was an administrative entity created and charged with implementing and administering the legislative mandates of the Fair Housing Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 52:27D-301 to 52:27D-329. At issue in the appeal was whether the Governor, pursuant to the Reorganization Act, had the power to abolish an independent agency created by the New Jersey Legislature that was in but not of a department of the Executive Branch. The narrower issue was whether the Governor could abolish COAH and transfer its duties, responsibilities, and obligations to the sole authority of an Executive Branch department. The court held that, in strictly construing the Reorganization Act, it did not grant the Governor the power to abolish a legislatively created, representative, independent authority that is in but not of the Executive Branch or any department in that branch of the government. The court held that the power to abolish COAH rested exclusively with the New Jersey Legislature and that, as an in but not of agency, COAH was not subject to the Reorganization Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Governor's abolishment of COAH.

 

255 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Horizon Blue Cross Blue Shield of New Jersey v. State


DOCKET NO. A-2232-09T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


425 N.J. Super. 1; 39 A.3d 228; 26 N.J. Tax 575; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 30


October 4, 2011, Argued 
March 7, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:
Approved for Publication March 7, 2012.
Certification denied by, Appeal dismissed by Horizon Blue Cross Blue Shield of N.J. v. State, 211 N.J. 608, 50 A.3d 41, 2012 N.J. LEXIS 890 (N.J., July 17, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Tax Court, Docket No. 7354-2005, whose opinion is reported at 25 N.J. Tax 290 (Tax Ct. 2009).
Horizon Blue Cross Blue Shield v. State, 25 N.J. Tax 290, 2009 N.J. Tax LEXIS 34 (Tax Ct., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff health service corporation (HSC) sued defendants, the New Jersey Division of Taxation, its Director, the New Jersey Department of Treasury, the New Jersey Department of Banking and Insurance, and its Commissioner, seeking a tax refund and challenging N.J.S.A. § 54:18A-6(b). The Superior Court of New Jersey, Tax Court, denied plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and granted defendants summary judgment motion. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, as the state's sole HSC, was required to serve as the insurer of last resort for the state of New Jersey. The appellate court concluded that New Jersey's Premium Tax Cap Statute, N.J.S.A. § 54:18A-6, as amended by Assembly Bill A4401(A4401), L. 2005, c. 128, was not unconstitutional as a denial of due process or equal protection, a bill of attainder, or special legislation. By its terms A4401 eliminated the tax cap on premiums received by HSCs when at all relevant times, plaintiff was the only HSC in New Jersey. Among its other claims, plaintiff charged that it was singled out for retaliation after it refused to convert to for-profit status. The appellate court determined that A4401 was rationally related to the legislative goals of raising revenue to reduce a budget deficit as well as to eliminate a loophole in the tax law whereby HSCs had a lower effective tax rate than other health insurance carriers. It further concluded that plaintiff's claim of retaliation was likewise without merit. The trial court did not err in denying plaintiff's motion to compel discovery, and, in granting defendants summary judgment, did not improperly weigh the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
