New Jersey Dental Ass'n v. Metropolitan Life Ins. Co.


DOCKET NO. A-2916-10T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


424 N.J. Super. 160; 36 A.3d 1066; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 18


October 17, 2011, Argued 
February 15, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication February 15, 2012.
Certification denied by N.J. Dental Ass'n v. Metro. Life Ins. Co., 2012 N.J. LEXIS 651 (N.J., May 15, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, Docket No. L-2286-10.
N.J. Dental Ass'n v. Metro. Life Ins. Co., 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 99586 (D.N.J., Sept. 21, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff association challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, which granted the motion to dismiss filed by defendant insurance carriers. The association had brought a declaratory judgment action seeking to invalidate and enjoin certain contractual clauses. The Commissioner of the Department of Banking and Insurance (Department) was granted leave to participate as amicus curiae.


OVERVIEW: In conjunction with dental plans approved by the Commissioner, pursuant to the selective contracting law, N.J.S.A. § 17B:27A-54, the insurance carriers offered an ancillary program for dental services not covered by their plans with the association which allowed a subscriber to receive a service not covered by the plan at a price the insurance carriers fixed in contracts with network dentists, pursuant to N.J.A.C. 11:22-5.10(a)(2). Contending that the selective contracting law did not authorize the offering of the ancillary program in conjunction with a dental plan, the association brought the underlying action seeking to invalidate and enjoin the clauses in its members' contracts with the insurance carriers that were essential to the ancillary program. The association contended that by allowing the ancillary program for services, the Commissioner exceeded the authority delegated in the selective contracting law. The court disagreed and upheld the validity of N.J.A.C. 11:22- 5.10 and accepted the Commissioner's position that the Department had the authority to regulate insurance but not programs offering purchasers discounts on dental services under N.J.S.A. § 17B:27A-54.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

258 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Heine


DOCKET NO. A-5858-09T2, A-1720-10T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


424 N.J. Super. 48; 35 A.3d 691; 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 10


November 30, 2011, Submitted 
January 31, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication January 31, 2012.
Related proceeding at State v. Heine, 2012 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 240 (App.Div., Feb. 6, 2012)
Certification granted by State v. Heine, 211 N.J. 608, 50 A.3d 40, 2012 N.J. LEXIS 857 (2012)
Certification denied by State v. Heine, 211 N.J. 608, 50 A.3d 40, 2012 N.J. LEXIS 858 (2012)
Related proceeding at Heine v. Comm'r of the Dep't of Cmty. Affairs of N.J., 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 116904 (D.N.J., Aug. 22, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, Municipal Appeal No. 004-09-10 (A-5858-09) and 009-12-10 (A-1720-10).
State v. Heine, 2012 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 128 (App.Div., Jan. 20, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two appeals, defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, which upheld her convictions finding her guilty of violating several city ordinances. The cases stemmed from the city's enforcement proceedings against defendant under its ordinance-based property maintenance code. Defendant was originally found guilty in a municipal court.


OVERVIEW: Two of defendant's convictions involved her refusal to let the city's construction and fire official inspect her rental property. The third conviction involved the municipal court finding defendant guilty of three property maintenance code violations. The court held that by exercising her constitutional right to refuse to participate in an unwarranted inspection, defendant could not be deemed to have created the circumstances that would criminalize her conduct and cause the forfeiture of the very rights she sought to exercise. The court adhered to the sentiment that an individual is not required to surrender her Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV, protection on the say so of the inspector as the amendment gives her a constitutional right to refuse to consent and her asserting that right cannot be a crime. As a result, the court held that the city's criminalization of defendant's refusal to allow the inspections was not in accordance with the law. The court also noted that search warrants are required to conduct unconsented-to inspections. Thus, the ordinance was found unconstitutional as applied with regard to it authorizing warrantless inspections.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated defendant's convictions and sanctions for the ordinance violations and otherwise affirmed the judgments.

State v. Baylor


DOCKET NO. A-0054-09T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


423 N.J. Super. 578; 34 A.3d 801; 2011 N.J. Super. LEXIS 224


October 4, 2011, Submitted 
December 29, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication December 29, 2011.
Certification denied by State v. Baylor, 210 N.J. 263, 43 A.3d 1168, 2012 N.J. LEXIS 615 (2012)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Baylor, 2016 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 738 (App.Div., Apr. 5, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County, Indictment No. 06-06-0687.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County, which found him guilty on four counts of first-degree murder and other offenses following a jury trial. The trial court imposed four consecutive life sentences, without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from shooting four people at an after-hours club. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred by imposing sentences of life without parole under the amended statute of N.J.S.A. § 2C:11-3(b)(4) in violation of ex post facto principles. The court disagreed, noting that the law in effect in 2005, when the murders were committed, provided that a person convicted of murder shall be sentenced to life without parole if the jury finds at least one aggravating factor, regardless of any mitigating factors. The court held that the jury found that the State had proven beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant committed each murder while engaged in the commission of or attempt of the other murders and while engaging in a robbery, which were aggravating factors under the law in effect in 2005. As a result, the court was satisfied that the imposition of the four consecutive life sentences against defendant was not an ex post facto punishment. The court found no merit to defendant's other challenges raised on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

O'Boyle v. District I Ethics Committee


DOCKET NO. A-4599-09T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


421 N.J. Super. 457; 24 A.3d 809; 2011 N.J. Super. LEXIS 158


November 17, 2010, Argued 
August 12, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 12, 2011.
Certification denied by O'Boyle v. Dist. I Ethics Comm., 2011 N.J. LEXIS 1438 (N.J., Dec. 9, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, Docket No. L-2597-09.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grievant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, which dismissed his suit against defendants, a district ethics committee, the Director of the Office of Attorney Ethics, and the Supreme Court of New Jersey. Plaintiff brought an action in lieu of prerogative writs challenging R. 1:20-3(e)(3), following the decision of the ethics committee declining his grievance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff had been involved in a dispute for an unpaid bill with an electrician and filed a grievance against the electrician's attorney asserting that the attorney violated N.J. R. Prof. Conduct 3.4(g) by threatening criminal charges against plaintiff in order to gain an advantage in a civil contract matter. The secretary of the district ethics committee advised plaintiff that his grievance was declined. Plaintiff asserted that R. 1:20-3(e)(6), which precluded an appeal of an undocketed grievance, violated his right to due process or equal protection of the laws. The court found that plaintiff failed to assert a viable constitutional basis for his challenge. The court found that plaintiff was dissatisfied with the procedure established by the disciplinary rules and the district ethics committee's decision but that did not translate into a cognizable claim in the court system. The court found that plaintiff received all due process to which he was entitled to under the law and his dissatisfaction with the result did not provide any judicial recourse as the district ethics committee's decision was final and unappealable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the complaint.

State v. Handy


DOCKET NO. A-0401-09T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


421 N.J. Super. 559; 25 A.3d 1140; 2011 N.J. Super. LEXIS 152


March 7, 2011, Argued 
August 4, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 4, 2011.
Certification granted by State v. Handy, 209 N.J. 99, 35 A.3d 682, 2012 N.J. LEXIS 30 (2012)
Modified by, Affirmed by, Remanded by State v. Handy, 2013 N.J. LEXIS 841 (N.J., Sept. 9, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County, Indictment No. 04-04-0567.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County, which issued a judgment of acquittal on all counts of the indictment upon finding defendant not guilty by reason of insanity. Defendant was ordered committed to a psychiatric facility, pursuant to N.J.S.A. § 2C:4-8(b)(3). Defendant had been indicted on charges of murder, unlawful possession of a knife, and possession of a weapon.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose from the stabbing death of his uncle. Defendant had pled not guilty to the charges and rejected the State's repeated overtures to agree to a plea of not guilty by reason of insanity. After a bench trial, he was found not guilty by reason of insanity. Defendant had preferred and unsuccessfully sought to have a jury trial to seek acquittal on a theory of self-defense. The trial court followed State v. Khan, 175 N.J. Super. 72 (App.Div.1980), which prescribed a bifurcated procedure that gave primacy to the adjudication of an insanity defense. The court held that it declined to adhere to the bifurcation sequence set forth in Khan. Instead, the court held that a defendant who wishes to present a substantive defense based upon at least some evidence, or who otherwise wishes to put the State to its burden of proving the elements of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt, should not be required to first submit to a trial restricted to the issue of insanity. Thus, the court concluded that defendant was unfairly precluded from having a fact-finder fully consider a defense that could have resulted in his acquittal.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings on certain terms and conditions detailed in the opinion. The court also referred the many issues of procedural design and potential rule making implicated by the case for prospective consideration to the New Jersey Supreme Court's Committee on Criminal Practice.

Guaman v. Velez


DOCKET NO. A-1870-10T2, M-3432-10


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


421 N.J. Super. 239; 23 A.3d 451; 2011 N.J. Super. LEXIS 131


April 5, 2011, Motion Argued 
July 12, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication July 12, 2011.
Judgment entered by Guaman v. Velez, 2013 N.J. Super. LEXIS 120 (App.Div., Aug. 13, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Adoption and Amendment of Regulations by the Department of Human Services, Division of Medical Assistance and Health Services.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, representatives of a putative class of legal, resident immigrants who have resided in the United States for less than five years, sought emergent injunctive relief against defendants, various State of New Jersey officials and agencies, staying the enforcement of N.J.A.C. 10:78-3.2. That regulation adopted the standard of eligibility for federal Medicaid benefits and applied it to New Jersey's State-funded Medicaid program.


OVERVIEW: N.J.A.C. 10:78-3.2 adopted the standard of eligibility for federal Medicaid benefits contained in the Personal Responsibility and Work Opportunity Reconciliation Act (PRWORA), 8 U.S.C.S. §§ 1601 to 1646, and applied it to New Jersey's FamilyCare Program, N.J.S.A. §§ 30:4J-8 to 30:4J-19, a State-funded Medicaid program. Pursuant to PRWORA, legal, resident immigrants who have not resided in the United States for at least five years were ineligible for federally-funded Medicaid benefits. Plaintiffs argued that N.J.A.C. 10:78-3.2 violated the FamilyCare program's enabling legislation and equal protection. The court determined, by applying the standards for preliminary injunctive relief, that plaintiffs failed to demonstrate a legal right to relief and a reasonable probability of ultimate success. The court held that the means selected by defendants in adopting the federal eligibility criteria for aliens bore a real and substantial relationship to PRWORA's compelling governmental interest of assuring that aliens be self reliant in accordance with national immigration policy and New Jersey's interest in providing subsidized health insurance within the set appropriated limits.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiffs' motion for preliminary injunctive relief.

State v. G.L.


DOCKET NO. A-1380-08T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


420 N.J. Super. 158; 19 A.3d 1017; 2011 N.J. Super. LEXIS 97


March 1, 2011, Submitted 
May 20, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication May 20, 2011.
Certification denied by State Op N.J. v. G.L., 2011 N.J. LEXIS 1315 (N.J., Nov. 7, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, Indictment No. 98-03-00505.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, which denied his motion to vacate his two convictions for failing to register as a sex offender, in violation of Megan's Law, N.J.S.A. § 2C:7-2.


OVERVIEW: As a result of it appearing that defendant, a juvenile, had not been adequately advised of the Megan's Law consequences of his plea of guilty to conduct that, if he were an adult, would constitute aggravated sexual assault, his plea was vacated and he was permitted to plead guilty to fourth-degree child abuse, an offense that was not subject to Megan's Law. Following that second plea, defendant moved to vacate two convictions that occurred in 1998 and 2000 for failure to register that had occurred in the interval between the first and second pleas. The trial court denied the motion to vacate upon concluding that the convictions for failure to register were based upon an adjudication that was in full force and effect at the time that the failures took place and were, therefore, validly entered. The court agreed, finding no statutory or equitable basis to vacate the two convictions for failure to register. The court found that nothing in Megan's Law suggested that the requirement of registration should be retroactively annulled because a plea to a crime subject to Megan's act was later withdrawn.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to vacate.

State v. Heisler


DOCKET NO. A-6281-08T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


422 N.J. Super. 399; 29 A.3d 320; 2011 N.J. Super. LEXIS 94


March 28, 2011, Argued 
May 17, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication May 17, 2011.
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by State v. Heisler, 2016 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 557 (App.Div., Mar. 14, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Somerset County, Municipal Appeal No. 40-08-A-T-09.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Somerset County, Municipal Appeal, which convicted him of being under the influence of a controlled dangerous substance (CDS) (N.J.S.A. § 2C:35-10(b)); possession of drug paraphernalia (N.J.S.A. § 2C:36-2); and operating a vehicle while knowingly having a CDS in his possession or in the motor vehicle (N.J.S.A. § 39:4-49.1).


OVERVIEW: The court first harmonize the two deadlines included in the Comprehensive Drug Reform Act, N.J.S.A. § 2C:35-19, and held that the 10-day period in which a defendant must object to the admission into evidence of a lab certificate, or else waive his right to confront the laboratory analyst, begins to run only after the State has provided all reports relating to the analysis in question. In doing so, the court resolved the ambiguity in the statute that required the State to serve its notice of intent to use a lab certificate and supporting data 20 days before trial, but required a defendant to object within 10 days of receiving only the notice of intent. As such, the court found that defendant's objection was timely with regard to the State's failure to comply with § 2C:35-19 and that two of his convictions required reversal since both of those convictions may have rested, in part, on the lab certificate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, the portion of the judgment convicting defendant for possession of drug paraphernalia. The court reversed defendant's convictions for being under the influence of a CDS and for operating a vehicle while knowingly having a CDS in his possession or in the motor vehicle and remanded that portion of the case to the municipal court for further proceedings.

 

266 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Botis v. Estate of Kudrick


DOCKET NO. A-5562-09T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


421 N.J. Super. 107; 22 A.3d 975; 2011 N.J. Super. LEXIS 76


December 13, 2010, Argued 
April 21, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication April 21, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Monmouth County, Docket No. FM-13-371-09C.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a decedent's alleged romantic partner, sued defendant estate, seeking palimony and other relief. The estate moved to dismiss the complaint and for leave to amend its counterclaim to include claims against plaintiff for fraud, perjury, attorneys fees, and punitive damages. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Monmouth County, denied both motions. The estate appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged she and the decedent had lived together in a "marriage-like relationship" and that he had agreed to take care of her financially. She alleged he told her that, in the event of his death, she would be cared for consistent with the lifestyle that they shared together. However, he did not provide for her in his will. After she filed the instant suit, the statute of frauds was amended to include palimony agreements among the types of "agreements or promises" that had to be in writing and signed by the parties in order to be enforceable (N.J.S.A. § 25:1-5(h)). This case required the appellate court to determine whether to accord the amendment retroactive effect in a case filed against the deceased promisor's estate prior to the effective date of the amendment on an alleged palimony agreement enforceable when the complaint was filed. The appellate court concluded that the amendment applied prospectively and held that the trial court properly denied the estate's motion to dismiss the complaint. Plaintiff and decedent could not have anticipated the prerequisites to enforcement of a palimony promise when they were in a position to create such a document.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

 

267 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Saffos v. Avaya Inc.


DOCKET NO. A-3189-08T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


419 N.J. Super. 244; 16 A.3d 1076; 2011 N.J. Super. LEXIS 44; 111 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1509


May 12, 2010, Argued 
March 8, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication March 8, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County, Docket No. L-346-05.
Saffos v. Avaya Inc., 2011 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 566 (App.Div., Mar. 8, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee prevailed in his suit against defendants, his former employer and its director, for violating New Jersey's Law Against Discrimination (LAD), N.J.S.A. §§ 10:5-1 to 10:5-49. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County, awarded him counsel fees but, pursuant to New Jersey's Punitive Damages Act (PDA), N.J.S.A. §§ 2A:15-5.9 to 2A:15-5.17, remitted the jury's punitive damages award. Both sides appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants urged it was error not to either vacate the punitive-damage award or remit it to equal compensatory damages. The appellate court rejected plaintiff's claim that the trial court erred in remitting the punitive-damage award and using a multiplier of five times the compensatory damages, as this was allowed by LAD and N.J.S.A. § 2A:15-5.14(b) of PDA. But, the emotional distress (ED) damages award had to be excluded from the multiplier on substantive due process grounds as he suffered no physical consequences from the distress caused by the discrimination and job loss and did not seek medical or psychological treatment, creating the inference that the ED award had a punitive component. As to attorney's fees, it excluded from the lodestar hours devoted to an unsuccessful motion--an unproductive use of time--but otherwise affirmed the lodestar. The retainer agreement provided for an hourly fee plus a 100 percent fee enhancement, or one-third of the amount recovered, whichever was higher. These alternative fees in excess of the lodestar made an additional 25 percent contingency-fee enhancement inconsistent with the purposes served by such enhancements under Rendine v. Pantzer.


OUTCOME: The punitive damages and attorney's fees awards were reduced and the case was remanded to the trial court for entry of a judgment in conformity with the appellate court's decision. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Jones v. Hayman


DOCKET NO. A-3173-09T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


418 N.J. Super. 291; 13 A.3d 416; 2011 N.J. Super. LEXIS 37


October 27, 2010, Argued 
February 25, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication February 25, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Mercer County, Docket No. C-123-07.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmates appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Mercer County, which denied their motion for attorneys' fees under the Law Against Discrimination, N.J.S.A. § 10:5-27.1, and the New Jersey Civil Rights Act, N.J.S.A. § 10:6-2. Plaintiffs had brought suit against defendants, the New Jersey Department of Corrections (DOC) and others, alleging discrimination.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were all females who were transferred from a prison for women to an all-male prison facility. Their suit alleged discrimination and unconstitutional confinement conditions. Plaintiffs successfully obtained class certification and were granted a preliminary injunction restraining the DOC from continuing to transfer women inmates to the male prison. Thereafter, defendants transferred all women inmates back to the female facility and plaintiffs' action was dismissed as moot. Subsequently, plaintiffs moved from attorneys' fees as the prevailing parties. The trial court denied their application, finding they were not a prevailing party because they did not obtain a judgment on the merits. The court found error, concluding that the trial court erred by accepting at face value the factual allegations and legal positions advanced by defendants without affording plaintiffs the opportunity to challenge the veracity of the allegations proffered in an evidentiary hearing. The court set forth the legal principles and standards courts should follow with regard to the catalyst theory under fee-shifting statutes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the case to the trial court for it to consider plaintiffs' application under the appropriate case law standards and legal principles set forth by the court.

In re T.J.S.


DOCKET NO. A-4784-09T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


419 N.J. Super. 46; 16 A.3d 386; 2011 N.J. Super. LEXIS 34


December 14, 2010, Argued 
February 23, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication February 23, 2011.
Certification granted by In re Parentage of T.J.S., 207 N.J. 228, 23 A.3d 935, 2011 N.J. LEXIS 894 (2011)
Affirmed by, By an equally divided Court at In re Parentage of a Child by T.J.S., 2012 N.J. LEXIS 1063 (N.J., Oct. 24, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Camden County, Docket No. FA-04-0273-09-S.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Camden County, which granted the motion of defendant, the New Jersey State Registrar, and determined that the New Jersey Parentage Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 9:17-38 to 9:17-59, did not permit the wife to be declared the parent of a child through a pre-birth adjudication commenced by plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: The wife was infertile and plaintiffs arranged for the in vitro fertilization of an ovum furnished by an anonymous donor using the husband's sperm. Plaintiffs entered into a gestational surrogacy agreement with another woman, who carried the baby for them. Thus, the wife had no biological connection with the child. The State Registrar successfully moved to vacate the order declaring the wife as a parent. The court held that the provisions of the Parentage Act conferring paternity upon a husband either presumptively, pursuant to N.J.S.A. § 9:17-43(a), or by operation of law, pursuant to N.J.S.A. § 9:17-44, did not extend to automatically confer maternity on an infertile wife whose husband has a child via in vitro fertilization of a gestational carrier. The court held that neither statutory provision offended constitutional principles of equal protection because their different treatment of infertile married men and women was grounded in real physiological differences between the sexes and was necessary to protect the interests of the gestational carrier. Absent legislative reform, the wife's sole means of obtaining parentage to the child was through adoption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Simmons v. Loose


DOCKET NO. A-6382-08T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


418 N.J. Super. 206; 13 A.3d 366; 2011 N.J. Super. LEXIS 16


September 14, 2010, Argued 
January 31, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication January 31, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, Docket No. L-3241-08.
In re A Search Warrant for 33 Lockwood Ave., 2005 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 74 (App.Div., Dec. 27, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following trial, plaintiff homeowners appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, which granted the motions for judgment filed by defendants, a borough, a township, and individual officers, and that awarded them $ 4,312.16 against defendant, the New Jersey State Police on their takings claim. The State Police cross-appealed the judgment. Plaintiffs alleged damages and constitutional violations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs had filed suit against defendants alleging that in the course of executing a search warrant, defendants wantonly and maliciously inflicted damages on their premises, which was a multiunit boarding house. They sought relief a under the New Jersey Tort Claims Act (TCA), N.J.S.A. §§ 59:1-1 to 59:12-3, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and the Takings Clauses of U.S. Const. amend. V and XIV, or N.J. Const. art. I, para. 20. Earlier, the borough, the township, and the individual officers were granted summary judgment and all claims were dismissed except the takings claim. The court reviewed case law holdings extensively and concluded that plaintiffs, as innocent property owners, were not entitled to compensation under the TCA, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, or, in the alternative, just compensation under U.S. Const. amend. V or N.J. Const. art. I, para. 20 since the property damage occurred as a result of the execution of a lawful search warrant. While the court recognized that plaintiffs suffered damages as a result of lawful government action, it held that such loss was not a taking and that the proper remedy must result from legislative action to provide relief.


OUTCOME: The court, reversed the judgment on the cross-appeal and remanded the case to the trial court for entry of a judgment of dismissal. The court affirmed the judgment on the direct appeal.

Related proceeding at In re Declaratory Judgment Actions Filed by Various Municipalities, 2016 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 356 (Law Div., Feb. 18, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Council on Affordable Housing.
In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 5:94 & 5:95 By New Jersey Council On Affordable Housing, 390 N.J. Super. 1, 914 A.2d 348, 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 20 (App.Div., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, 22 municipalities, challenged the validity of revised rules of respondent, the New Jersey Council on Affordable Housing (COAH), adopted under the Fair Housing Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 52:27D-301 to 52:27D-329.19, which establish the obligations of municipalities to provide affordable housing during a third round period from 1999 to 2019. The court had previously invalidated substantial portions of the third round rules.


OVERVIEW: The court had remanded the case to COAH for the adoption of revised rules in conformity with the court's prior opinion. The revised rules were the subject of the underlying appeal. The court held that the growth share methodology for determining a municipality's share of the prospective regional need for affordable housing set forth in the revised third round rules were invalid. The court also invalidated N.J.A.C. 5:97-3.2(a)(4)(iv), which authorizes a municipality to obtain substantive certification of a compliance plan that proposes to construct municipally-funded affordable housing without any specifics regarding the location of the site or source of funding; those parts of the third round rules that fail to provide sufficient incentives for the construction of inclusionary developments. Likewise, N.J.A.C. 5:97-3.5, which governs rental bonuses for prior round obligations was invalidated as was N.J.A.C. 5:97-3.18, which authorizes compliance bonuses for affordable housing units approved during the period from December 20, 2004 to June 2, 2008.


OUTCOME: The court invalidated substantial portions of the rules and remanded the case to the COAH to adopt new third round rules that use a methodology for determining prospective need similar to the methodologies used in the first and second rounds. The court noted that the determination should be made on the basis of the most up-to-date available data and that the remand shall be completed within five months.

Borough of Sayreville v. 35 Club, L.L.C.


DOCKET NO. A-3537-08T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


416 N.J. Super. 315; 3 A.3d 1268; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 192


February 4, 2010, Argued 
September 17, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication September 17, 2010.
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Borough of Sayreville v. 35 Club, L.L.C., 2012 N.J. LEXIS 12 (N.J., Jan. 19, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Middlesex County, Docket No. C-247-07.
D. Russo, Inc. v. Romankow, 2010 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2272 (App.Div., Sept. 17, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant club challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Middlesex County, which granted plaintiff borough's application to permanently enjoin it from operating its sexually oriented business at a particular location. The borough had filed a complaint alleging that the location and the nature of the club's activities violated N.J.S.A. § 2C:34-7 and the licensing requirements of its ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The club operated a sexually oriented business featuring live nude erotic dancing. Applying N.J.S.A. § 2C:34-7 and the licensing requirements of the borough's local ordinance, the trial court permanently enjoined the club from operating that business at its location. The trial court also ordered that the injunction be recorded in the office of the county registrar of deeds as a restriction on the use of the property in perpetuity. The court identified a Supreme Court of New Jersey case applicable to evaluating an as-applied challenge to § 2C:34-7. The court found that the trial court erred by concluding that the borough had met its burden of identifying the club's relevant market area since the two experts that testified did not address regional marketing patters or available public transportation and other factors. The court further held that the internet was not a reasonably viable alternative forum for the constitutionally protected form of expression at issue. The court also determined that the trial court had no authority to impose the deed restriction on the use of the property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for it to reconsider its ruling by applying all of the relevant case law factors. The court held that regardless of how the trial court ruled on remand, there was no legal ground for sustaining the order imposing a judicially crafted restriction on the use of the property that ran with the land in perpetuity. The court rejected the borough's cross-appeal.

State v. Badr


DOCKET NO. A-1975-08T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


415 N.J. Super. 455; 2 A.3d 436; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 157


November 12, 2009, Argued 
August 5, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 5, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, Municipal Appeal No. 31-2008.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A municipal court found defendant guilty of four counts of violating the New Jersey Smoke-Free Air Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 26:3D-55 to 26:3D-55-64. He appealed; the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, convicted defendant on each of the violations and imposed the same sentences as had been imposed in municipal court. Defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: A health inspector issued four summons alleging that defendant violated the Act in his hookah bar. Defendant's wife testified that there was no tobacco in any of the products and that they did not permit smoking of any tobacco on the premises. The instant court held that the Act was neither unconstitutionally vague nor overbroad under N.J. Const. art. I, § 1, para. 1 as applied to defendant's hookah bar. The Act provided "fair warning" by requiring prior written notification of prohibited conduct under N.J.S.A. § 26:3D-62(b). No one of common intelligence had to guess at the Act's meaning. The Act did not deprive defendant of the right to acquire, possess, and protect property under N.J. Const. art. I, § 1, para. 1, but merely denied him the option of permitting smoking within his premises. In the absence of constitutional infirmity, the question whether the Act had to be amended to explicitly include or exclude defendant's conduct was left to the legislature. As there was no indication that the written notification required by § 26:3D-62(b) was provided to defendant before the first summons was issued, the record was insufficient to support a conviction under that summons.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction on the first count was reversed, but the other convictions were affirmed.

New Jersey Ass'n of School Adm'rs v. Schundler


DOCKET NO. A-2101-08T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


414 N.J. Super. 530; 999 A.2d 535; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 150


March 2, 2010, Argued 
August 3, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 3, 2010.
Certification granted by New Jersey Ass'n of Sch. Adm'rs v. Schundler, 205 N.J. 519, 16 A.3d 384, 2011 N.J. LEXIS 526 (2011)
Reversed by New Jersey Ass'n of Sch. Adm'rs v. Schundler, 2012 N.J. LEXIS 511 (N.J., May 3, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Agency Decision by the Commissioner of Education.
N.J. Ass'n of Sch. Adm'rs v. Davy, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 96056 (D.N.J., Nov. 25, 2008)
New Jersey Ass'n of School Business Officials v. Davy, 409 N.J. Super. 467, 978 A.2d 295, 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 215 (App.Div., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, school superintendents, an assistant superintendent, and an association of school administrators, sued defendant New Jersey Commissioner of Education, challenged regulations adopted by the Commissioner in 2008 entitled "Fiscal Accountability, Efficiency and Budgeting Procedures," N.J.A.C. 6A:23A-1.2 to -22.15.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged N.J.A.C. 6A:23A-3.1(e)(1), (3), (4), (5), (6), (7), (8), (9) and (11) and certain provisions of N.J.A.C. N.J.A.C. 6A:23A-5.2(a). The appellate court rejected the argument that the regulations were an impermissible taking, unconstitutionally vague, a violation of equal protection, and ultra vires. Pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:7-8(j), the Commissioner had the authority to promulgate the challenged regulations. The appellate court agreed, however, that certain of the regulations violated the tenure statute, N.J.S.A. § 18A:28-5, and were thus invalid. While superintendents had no property rights in future employment contracts, and untenured assistant superintendents had only contingent rights in such contracts, under § 18A:28-5, tenured assistant superintendents could not be dismissed or reduced in compensation except for cause. Section 6A:23A-3.1(e)(3), (4), (5), and (6) improperly served to deprive certain administrators of vested rights and to reduce the compensation of tenured assistant superintendents. As § 6A:23A-5.2(a)(2)(iv) and (a)(4) affected school districts, not plaintiffs, they lacked standing to challenge these provisions.


OUTCOME: The appellate court upheld the authority of the Commissioner to adopt the challenged regulations but found that § 6A:23A-3.1(e)(3), (4), (5), and (6) violated the vested rights of certain school employees. It rejected pfs' challenges to the other regulations.

S.D. v. M.J.R.


DOCKET NO. A-6107-08T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


415 N.J. Super. 417; 2 A.3d 412; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 143


March 24, 2010, Argued 
July 23, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication July 23, 2010.
Related proceeding at S.D. v. M.J.R., 2014 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 172 (App.Div., Jan. 28, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Hudson County, Docket No. FV-09-1792-09.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Hudson County, found that defendant husband had assaulted and harassed plaintiff wife, in violation of the New Jersey Prevention of Domestic Violence Act (PDVA), N.J.S.A. §§ 2C:25-17 to 2C:25-35. It dismissed the wife's PDVA complaint, vacated a prior temporary restraining order, and denied her request to issue a permanent restraining order. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: On three occasions, the husband physically abused his wife, leaving multiple bruises; he also had nonconsensual sex with her several times. The trial court found that the nonconsexual sex did not constitute sexual assault (N.J.S.A. § 2C:14-2) or criminal sexual contact (N.J.S.A. § 2C:14-3) because the husband did not have the requisite criminal intent, as he believed his conduct was permitted by his religion. The appellate court held that this was error. As neither crime specified a mental state, the husband's knowing conduct was sufficient to establish the elements of both offenses. The Free Exercise Clause of the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I, did not require the trial court to exempt the husband, a practicing Muslim, from a finding that he committed the predicate acts of sexual assault and criminal sexual contact and thus violated the PDVA. The trial court erred in refusing to issue a final restraining order, as it inappropriately relied on restraints that may or may or may not have issued in the parallel criminal proceeding, and it failed to give sufficient consideration to the parties' future contact with each other due to the imminent birth of their child.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for entry of a final restraining order.

CASE SUMMARY:

Plaintiffs sought a declaration that N.J.S.A. §§ 18A:36A-10 and 18A:36A-12, regarding charter school funding, violated their equal protection rights.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged N.J.S.A. § 18A:36A-10, which barred charter schools from receiving state or local funding for facilities, and N.J.S.A. § 18A:36A-12, which provided only 90 percent per pupil funding for operational costs to charter schools as opposed to 100 percent of eligible facilities costs provided to traditional public schools. Plaintiffs contended that the funding disparity violated their equal protection rights under N.J. Const. art. I, para. 1. As a result, plaintiffs failed to demonstrate how they were deprived of the equal opportunity to attend the fully funded traditional public schools available to them in their city.

Bayer v. Township of Union


DOCKET NO. A-1482-07T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


414 N.J. Super. 238; 997 A.2d 1118; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 116


May 11, 2009, Submitted 
July 7, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication July 7, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, Docket No. L-4448-04.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestee sued defendants, a township and police officers, alleging false arrest and false imprisonment under the New Jersey Tort Claims Act (TCA), N.J.S.A. §§ 59:1-1 to 12-3, and asserting a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim for violation of his constitutional rights. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, dismissed the TCA claim and granted defendants summary judgment on the § 1983 claim. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was arrested based upon a mistaken identification. The appellate court held that the trial court properly dismissed plaintiff's § 1983 claim on summary judgment because a careful review of the undisputed facts revealed that a reasonable police officer would have believed there was probable cause to arrest plaintiff. That was a determination appropriately made by the trial court. As plaintiff showed no link between the township's alleged absence of valid procedures and the asserted § 1983 violation, the township was entitled to summary judgment. The trial court also properly dismissed plaintiff's TCA claim because plaintiff failed to provide timely notice pursuant to N.J.S.A. § 59:8-8. His receiving wrong advice from an attorney about the accrual date of his false arrest claim, and his desire not to aggravate police, were not "extraordinary circumstances" under N.J.S.A. § 59:8-9 justifying his failure to file a notice of claim within 90 days of its accrual. After reviewing in camera the certain documents plaintiff requested in discovery, as the trial court concluded they were not relevant to his claims against the township, it properly denied his discovery request.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

New Jersey Law Enforcement Supervisors Ass'n v. State


DOCKET NO. A-2839-08T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


414 N.J. Super. 111; 997 A.2d 1043; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 106


March 8, 2010, Argued 
June 21, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication June 21, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Governor's Office of Employee Relations.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The New Jersey Governor's Office of Employee Relations (OER) rejected the request of appellant, an independent police union, for paid leave for some of its members and trustees to attend a convention. Appellant sued respondent, the State of New Jersey, seeking a declaration that N.J.S.A. § 11A:6-10 violated the ban on special legislation set forth in N.J. Const. art. IV, § 7, para. 7, as well as the equal protection rights of its members.


OVERVIEW: Appellant represented law enforcement officers holding the rank of captain or its equivalent. OER denied its request for paid leave for its members and trustees to attend as delegates a state convention hosted by appellant and another union, on grounds appellant was not affiliated with any of the unions named in § 11A:6-10 or N.J.A.C. 4A:6-1.13. Appellant argued that § 11A:6-10 was special legislation as its limitation to four unions was arbitrarily exclusive, and, for the same reason, violated the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. The court held that the police and firefighters paid convention leave statute, § 11A:6-10, was not unconstitutional as special legislation and did not violate the equal protection rights of members of employee organizations not affiliated with the unions designated in the statute. As the vast difference in size and diversity sufficiently distinguished the groups excluded, the statutory classification was at least "fairly debatable." And as the classification rested on a rational basis relevant to the statute's educational purpose, § 11A:6-10 passed the rational basis test and therefore defeated appellant's equal protection claim.


OUTCOME: OER's ruling was affirmed.

 

279 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Perth Amboy Bd. of Educ. v. Christie


DOCKET NO. A-3361-09T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


413 N.J. Super. 590; 997 A.2d 262; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 100


May 18, 2010, Argued 
June 14, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication June 14, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Executive Order 14, February 11, 2010.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a board of education, filed a notice of appeal, pursuant to R. 2:2-3(a)(2), challenging the withholding of New Jersey state aid payments to school districts as a result of Executive Order 14 (EO14), which was signed by respondent, the Governor of the State of New Jersey. The board also sought an emergent application for injunctive relief. The court denied the motion for emergent relief, but accelerated the appeal.


OVERVIEW: EO14 froze State aid to school districts for the remainder of Fiscal Year 2010 in an amount equal to each district's anticipated surplus funds, but allowed transfers from the surplus to meet a school district's current year's operating costs. The board alleged that EO14 constituted gubernatorial lawmaking in violation of the constitutional principle of separation of powers because it conflicted with the legislative mandate of N.J.S.A. § 18A:7F-7, that excess surplus be appropriated to the school district's subsequent fiscal year's budget. The court held that EO14 was authorized both statutorily and constitutionally, despite § 18A:7F-7's command that such excess surplus funds be used for the next year's school budget. As a result, the court held that EO14 did not violate the separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

280 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jefferson


DOCKET NO. A-1945-06T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


413 N.J. Super. 344; 994 A.2d 1067; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 87


January 12, 2010, Submitted 
May 21, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication May 21, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, Indictment No. 05-12-1371.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, which denied his motion to suppress evidence. Defendant entered a conditional plea of guilty to second-degree possession of cocaine with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of a school, in violation of N.J.S.A. § 2C:35-5(a)(1) and (b)(2).


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose from warrantless police searches of his person and his residence. Evidence of crack cocaine was found on defendant's person following his arrest and, after his wife consented to the search of their apartment, additional contraband was found. The court held that the evidence seized from the apartment should have been suppressed because in the absence of a warrant or a recognized exception from the warrant requirement under U.S. Const. amend. IV, the police could not lawfully enter defendant's home to conduct a Terry-type detention and investigation of him. The court found that a police officer's wedging herself in the doorway to prevent defendant from closing his front door was entry into the home and that the police failed to show either hot pursuit exigent circumstances or a community caretaking exception from the warrant requirement. Although the police entry was unlawful, defendant had no right to resist physically, and the search of his person incident to his arrest was lawful. However, consent to search defendant's apartment, given by his wife, was tainted by the unconstitutional police conduct and was not shown to be voluntary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Powerhouse Arts Dist. Neighborhood Ass'n v. City Council of City of Jersey City


DOCKET NO. A-4570-08T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


413 N.J. Super. 322; 994 A.2d 1054; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 81


April 13, 2010, Argued 
May 17, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication May 17, 2010.
Certification denied by Powerhouse Arts Dist. Neighborhood Ass'n v. City Council of Jersey City, 2011 N.J. LEXIS 162 (N.J., Jan. 14, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, Docket No. L-2756-08.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff neighborhood association sued defendants, a city council and developers, challenged a redevelopment plan amendment relaxing height and density requirements that was proposed by the developers and adopted by the council. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, dismissed the complaint with prejudice; plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The council had designated an area as in need of redevelopment under New Jersey's Local Redevelopment and Housing Law (LRHL), N.J.S.A. §§ 40A:12A-1 to 40A:12A-1-73. The appellate court held that the trial court properly applied the arbitrary and capricious standard. It rejected plaintiff's claim that as the redevelopment plan was successful, it could not be amended; the LRHL neither precluded amendment of a successful redevelopment plan or required that it forever depend upon the initial impetus for the blight designation. The council's adoption of the amendment was not arbitrary or capricious, as it had adequate support in the record. Plaintiff's claim that the blight designation was stale when certain lots were included in the plan 29 years later failed. As approval of an amendment to a redevelopment plan was governed by N.J.S.A. § 40A:12A-7, not N.J.S.A. § 40A:12A-5, which governed only an initial blight designation, the council need not have reevaluated any of the properties under the criteria of § 40A:12A-5 while it adopted a redevelopment plan under § 40A:12A-7. And plaintiff's four-year acquiescence to the inclusion of those lots estopped it from challenging it later.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Communications Workers of America, AFL-CIO v. Christie


DOCKET NO. A-2871-09T2, A-2996-09T2, A-2997-09T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


413 N.J. Super. 229; 994 A.2d 545; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 77; 188 L.R.R.M. 2664; 159 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,991


April 8, 2010, Argued 
May 7, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication May 7, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Executive Order 7, January 20, 2010.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant labor unions brought suit against respondents, the Governor of New Jersey and others challenging Executive Order Number 7 (EO 7), signed by the Governor, which attempted to extend labor unions and labor organizations certain pay-to-play restrictions on political campaign contributions.


OVERVIEW: Appellants consisted of six labor unions that were representatives of more than 300,000 public employees. Appellants asserted that EO 7 was unconstitutional in numerous respects in that it conflicted with the terms of existing legislation and thereby infringed upon principles of separation of powers, in violation of N.J. Const. art. III, para. 1. The court held that paragraph one of EO 7 violated principles of separation of powers and invalidated it to the extent that it was written or intended to be construed to cover labor unions and collective bargaining agreements. The court concluded that paragraph one of EO 7, at least insofar as it was intended to treat collective bargaining agreements as contracts and labor unions as business entities, was so fundamentally incompatible with existing laws and statutes that it impaired the essential integrity of the constitutional powers of the New Jersey Legislature. The court held that an executive order could not bypass the Legislature and carry out what would be, in effect, an implied repealer of existing legislation addressing pay-to-play restrictions.


OUTCOME: The court vacated paragraph one of EO 7 as exceeding the Governor's executive power. The court held that in the interests of accommodating potential review by the New Jersey Supreme Court, its determination was effective July 1, 2010, unless the Governor filed a timely notice of appeal or petition for certification, in which event the effective date shall be stayed pending further order of the Supreme Court.

Committee to Recall Robert Menendez from the Office of U.S. Senator v. Wells


DOCKET NO. A-2254-09T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


413 N.J. Super. 435; 995 A.2d 1109; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 40


March 2, 2010, Argued 
March 16, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication March 16, 2010.
Certification granted by Committee to Recall Robert Menendez from Office of U.S. Senator v. Wells, 201 N.J. 498, 992 A.2d 793, 2010 N.J. LEXIS 414 (2010)
Reversed by, Vacated by Comm. to Recall Robert Menendez from the Office of United States Senator v. Wells, 2010 N.J. LEXIS 1223 (N.J., Nov. 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Division of Elections and decision of the Secretary of State.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff recall committee appealed the final administrative determination of defendant, the New Jersey Secretary of State, declining to accept its notice of intention to recall a particular United States Senator. N.J. Const. art. I, para. 2 and the Uniform Recall Election Law, N.J.S.A. § 19:27A-2, permitted such a petition, but the Secretary declined to accept the filing. Defendant, the Director of the Division of Elections, was also a party.


OVERVIEW: The particular Senator at issue was made an indispensible party and various amicus curiae participated in the case. The Secretary's decision was based on her determination that the qualifications and election of a member of the United States Senate was a matter of exclusive jurisdiction of federal authority and that neither the United States Constitution nor federal statute provided for a recall proceeding for a federally-elected official. The court acknowledged the overwhelming margin that the recall provision set forth in N.J. Const. art. I, para. 2 was approved by New Jersey voters. The court determined that the recall measures approved by the citizens of New Jersey, and implemented via N.J.S.A. § 19:27A-2, were clear and unambiguous and authorized the recall of a United States Senator in New Jersey. The court found no federal constitutional provision precluding States from adopting legislation for the recalling of a United States Senator and that the New Jersey recall process was not so clearly invalid under federal law as to require a drastic, preemptive judicial declaration thwarting the will of the voters.


OUTCOME: The court ordered the Secretary to accept and file the petition and to proceed under the statute. The court noted that in ordering that ministerial act, it was not passing on the ultimate validity of the recall process at issue. The court stayed its decision until such time as defendants or the Senator filed a timely notice of appeal or petition for certification.

Jenkins v. New Jersey Dep't of Corr.


DOCKET NO. A-1220-08T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


412 N.J. Super. 243; 989 A.2d 854; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 35


January 4, 2010, Submitted 
March 5, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication March 5, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Department of Corrections.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the final decision of respondent, the New Jersey Department of Corrections, finding him guilty of disciplinary infraction *.011, which was defined in N.J.A.C. 10A:4-4.1 as possession or exhibition of anything related to a security threat group (STG).


OVERVIEW: On September 23, 2008, three handwritten letters were seized during a search of the inmate's cell. At the disciplinary hearing, the letters were received in evidence. An intelligence investigator who had received training as a gang investigator prepared a report, which stated that two of the three letters contained STG related material. The hearing officer found the inmate guilty of *.011, and he received a sanction of 15 days detention, 180 days administrative segregation, and 180 days loss of commutation time. On appeal, the inmate asserted that the regulation was unconstitutionally vague. The court reviewed disciplinary infraction *.011, as defined in N.J.A.C. 10A:4-4.1, and determined that it was neither facially vague nor unconstitutionally vague as applied. The court found that, at a minimum, the regulation provided proper notice of the prohibited conduct and what constituted prohibited literature related to STGs. In response to the inmate's challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence, the court found that the evidence relied upon by the hearing officer provided the required substantial evidence to support the disciplinary violation against him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the final decision.

New Jersey Educ. Ass'n v. State


DOCKET NO. A-4460-07T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


412 N.J. Super. 192; 989 A.2d 282; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 33


December 15, 2009, Argued 
March 4, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication March 4, 2010.
Certification denied by New Jersey Educ. Ass'n v. State, 202 N.J. 347, 997 A.2d 232, 2010 N.J. LEXIS 761 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, Docket No. L-81-04.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a teachers union and some of its members, sued defendants, the State of New Jersey, its legislature, and its current and former treasurers, seeking to redress shortfalls in the State's statutorily-mandated contributions to the New Jersey Teachers' Pension and Annuity Fund (TPAF). After a bench trial, the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, dismissed the complaint. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged, inter alia, that the legislature's failure to fund TPAF in the amounts certified by the TPAF actuary violated the Contracts, Due Process, and Unlawful Taking Clauses of the New Jersey and U.S. Constitutions; violated the Uniformity of Taxation and Debt Limitation Clauses of the New Jersey Constitution; and violated the New Jersey Teachers' Pension and Annuity Fund Law, N.J.S.A. §§ 18A:66-1 to -93, -3 (TPAF Act). The appellate court held that members of TPAF, although entitled by law to the receipt of vested benefits upon retirement, possessed no constitutionally protected contract right to the particular level, manner, or method of State funding provided by statute. The New Jersey Constitutional created no contractual right to retirement benefits or to future legislative appropriations. Moreover, granting members the contract rights they claimed would run afoul of the Appropriations Clause, N.J. Const. art. VIII, § 2, para. 2, and the Debt Limitation Clause, N.J. Const. art. VIII, § 2, para. 3, which granted the legislature exclusive powers of appropriation and precluded one legislature from binding future legislatures regarding prospective appropriations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lake Valley Associates, LLC v. Township Of Pemberton


DOCKET NO. A-4040-07T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


411 N.J. Super. 501; 987 A.2d 623; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 15


November 18, 2009, Argued 
February 1, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication February 1, 2010.
Certification denied by Lake Valley Assocs. v. Twp. of Pemberton, 2010 N.J. LEXIS 443 (N.J., May 4, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County, Docket No. L-2669-06.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a limited liability company, appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County, which dismissed its action in lieu of prerogative writs challenging the constitutionality and statutory validity of an ordinance adopted by defendant township, which imposed certain registration obligations and other regulatory requirements on landlords within the township.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff owned and operated a 450-unit apartment complex located within the township. Plaintiff facially challenged the constitutionality and statutory validity of the ordinance, and argued that the ordinance was not for a valid public purpose; violated due process and separation-of-powers principles of the United States Constitution and the New Jersey Constitution; and that it was preempted by the Hotel and Multiple Dwelling Law, N.J.S.A. §§ 55:13A-1 to - 28, and by other state statutes. The court upheld the dismissal of plaintiff's claims, essentially for the same reasons as the trial court. The court, quoting much of the trial judge's opinion, held that N.J.S.A. § 55:13A-25(b) was clear and contained an explicit expression that preemption was never intended. The court held that not only did the Hotel and Multiple Dwelling Law not preempt municipal action, but that none of the rules or regulations promulgated pursuant to it could preempt a municipality from acting in the field. The court further found that plaintiff failed to provide any extrinsic evidence of an invalid purpose for enactment of the ordinance, therefore, the presumption of its validity remained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Bernstein v. State


DOCKET NO. A-1601-08T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


411 N.J. Super. 316; 986 A.2d 22; 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 7


December 8, 2009, Submitted 
January 11, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication January 11, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, Docket No. L-2922-06.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a deceased inmate's estate, sued defendants, New Jersey Department of Corrections officials and prison administrators and employees, alleging common law tort and federal civil rights claims based on defendants' alleged delayed response to another prisoner's attack on the inmate, resulting in his death. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, granted defendants summary judgment; plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff claimed the attack was delayed by a prison policy dictating supervision of the mess hall from protective cages above the floor rather than direct floor patrol, and by assembling two emergency response teams rather than one before interceding. Plaintiff also sought to hold defendants liable for failing to remove the attacking inmate from the prison's general population, as he suffered from psychological problems. The appellate court approved the summary judgment dismissal of plaintiff's complaint, finding the individual state defendants immune from state tort claims under N.J.S.A. § 59:5-2(b)(4) in the absence of any evidence of willful misconduct. As to the federal civil rights claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, the appellate court also found no proof of a constitutional violation, that is, no evidence defendants acted with a deliberate indifference to a substantial risk to decedent in violation of the "cruel and unusual punishment" ban of the Eighth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VIII. Moreover, because it discerned no violation of a clearly established constitutional right, it held the individual state defendants had a qualified immunity from liability under § 1983.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

J.S. v. J.F.


DOCKET NO. A-2552-08T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


410 N.J. Super. 611; 983 A.2d 1151; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 251


November 12, 2009, Submitted 
December 10, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication December 10, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Essex County, Docket No. FV-07-1485-09.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed a domestic violence complaint against defendant. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Essex County, entered a final restraining order in favor of plaintiff pursuant to the New Jersey Prevention of Domestic Violence Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 2C:25-17 to -35. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the parties were in a dating relationship and that defendant made terroristic threats and harassed plaintiff. Defendant argued that plaintiff did not qualify as a domestic violence victim because he paid for her company. The appellate court examined the factors relevant to determining whether a dating relationship existed for purposes of the Act and concluded that plaintiff was not automatically disqualified from claiming a dating relationship solely because defendant may have paid plaintiff for her company. Defendant testified that his payments to plaintiff were meant to help her out financially and were not necessarily in exchange for her time. In response to questioning by the trial court, he agreed that he and plaintiff dated. Further, plaintiff testified she and defendant were girlfriend and boyfriend. The trial court's findings that defendant committed acts of domestic violence, in that his communications constituted terroristic threats or were otherwise acts of harassment, were supported by credible evidence. The legislature was not constitutionally required to impose a clear-and-convincing standard for adjudication of domestic violence matters.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Williams


DOCKET NO. A-4530-07T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


410 N.J. Super. 549; 983 A.2d 1114; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 248


October 6, 2009, Argued 
November 23, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication November 23, 2009.
Certification denied by N.J. v. Robert E. Williams A/K/A Robert Love, 2010 N.J. LEXIS 269 (N.J., Mar. 2, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, Indictment No. 06-11-1044.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. IV. and N.J. Const. art. I, para. 7, defendant moved to suppress drugs seized after an investigatory stop. After the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, denied the motion, defendant pled guilty to possession of cocaine. He then appealed the denial of his suppression motion.


OVERVIEW: After a recent homicide at a housing complex, police went to the complex to deter a possible retaliatory shooting. When defendant recognized the officers as police, he pedaled away on a bicycle despite their commands to stop. After two officers grabbed him, he threw away a box of cocaine. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that the officers did not have a reasonable suspicion that defendant was engaged or about to engage in criminal activity. However, the trial court erred in ruling that defendant's apparent violation of the obstruction statute, N.J.S.A. § 2C:29-1, provided sufficient grounds to justify the stop. Flight from an unconstitutional investigatory stop that could justify an arrest for obstruction did not automatically justify admission of evidence revealed during that flight. For such evidence to be admissible, there had to be a "significant attenuation" between the unconstitutional stop and seizure of evidence. As only four or five seconds elapsed between the order to stop and defendant's discarding the cocaine, and there were no significant "intervening circumstances" between the two events, the State failed to show significant attenuation.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's motion to suppress was reversed and the judgment of conviction was vacated.

United Consumer Financial Services Co. v. Carbo


DOCKET NO. A-5501-06T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


410 N.J. Super. 280; 982 A.2d 7; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 230


May 19, 2009, Argued 
October 22, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication October 22, 2009.
On remand at United Consumer Fin. Servs. Co. v. Carbo, 2010 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2311 (Law Div., Jan. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, Docket No. L-3438-02.
United Consumer Fin. Servs. Co. v. Carbo, 2004 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 5 (Law Div., Apr. 8, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a financial company, appealed various orders of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, which awarded injunctive relief and a civil penalty to defendant consumers, pursuant to the Truth-in-Consumer Contract, Warranty and Notice Act (TCCWNA), N.J.S.A. §§ 56:12-14 to -18. Plaintiff's suit sought collection of amounts due under retail installment contracts.


OVERVIEW: The award to defendants was based upon violations of consumer rights provided in the Retail Installment Sales Act (RISA), N.J.S.A. §§ 17:16C-1 to -61, and the Door-to-Door Retail Installment Sales Act (DDRISA), N.J.S.A. §§ 17:16C-61.1 to -61.9. Plaintiff accepted assignments of retail installment contracts entered into by defendants for vacuum cleaners sold door-to-door. The court rejected plaintiff's claim that class certification was improper in the case because only one of the several sellers was involved in the purchase made by the class representative. The court found that the common nucleus of fact in the action was the content and form of the contract and notices by plaintiff and used in each transaction. Thus, class certification was held proper. The court affirmed the TCCWNA penalty because the contract violated a consumer right provided by RISA and the aggregate award was neither unconstitutionally excessive nor a basis for decertification of the class. The court did modify the injunctive relief to conform the same with federal regulations, which preempted and precluded enforcement of several but not all of the provisions of the DDRISA.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, in part, the orders of the trial court with regard to finding a violation of the DDRISA based upon the typeface included in the contracts and the attorney fee award in favor of defendants' counsel. The court further ordered modification of the injunction. The court otherwise affirmed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

In re Dubov


DOCKET NO. A-0832-08T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


410 N.J. Super. 190; 981 A.2d 87; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 227


September 15, 2009, Argued 
October 19, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication October 19, 2009.
Appeal after remand at In re Dubov, 2012 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1957 (App.Div., Aug. 14, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of a police chief's denial of his application for a permit to purchase a firearm pursuant to to N.J.S.A. § 2C:58-3. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, affirmed the denial of the application. The applicant appealed; respondent State opposed the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not hear testimony, but based its ruling solely on documentary evidence, including letters from the applicant's references and the report of his psychiatrist. The appellate court ruled that the U.S. Supreme Court's decision in District of Columbia v. Heller, which held that the Second Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. II, protected an individual right to keep and bear arms, had no effect upon the constitutionality of § 2C:58-3, which required a permit to purchase a firearm. The trial court's failure to conduct a hearing on the appeal from the denial of the application for a firearms purchaser permit within the 30-day period allowed by § 2C:58-3(d) did not require automatic approval of the application. The trial court erred in failing to conduct an evidentiary hearing on an appeal from the denial of the application for a firearms purchaser permit and instead deciding the appeal based on evidence submitted to the trial court ex parte in the form of telephone calls by the trial court to the applicant's former employers and an unsolicited letter submitted after argument of the appeal that commented negatively upon the applicant's fitness to possess a firearm.


OUTCOME: The trial court's affirmance of the denial of the application was reversed and the case was remanded for an evidentiary hearing.

County of Warren v. State


DOCKET NO. A-4591-07T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


409 N.J. Super. 495; 978 A.2d 312; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 217


May 6, 2009, Submitted 
September 4, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication September 4, 2009.
Certification denied by County of Warren v. State, 201 N.J. 153, 988 A.2d 1176, 2010 N.J. LEXIS 102 (2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Shope v. New Jersey, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 5393 (U.S., June 28, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, Docket No. L-1021-07.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff farmers appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, which dismissed their declaratory judgment action against defendants, the State of New Jersey, the Department of Environmental Protection, the Highlands Water Protection and Planning Council (Council), and the New Jersey Water Supply Authority. The farmers alleged statutory violations involving preserved areas.


OVERVIEW: The farmers all owned tracts of land created by the Highlands Water Protection and Planning Act (Highlands Act), N.J.S.A. §§ 13:20-1 to -35. In lieu of an answer, defendants moved to dismiss the farmers' complaint. The trial court upheld the Highlands Act on due process and other grounds, dismissed the challenge to the Council's action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, finding that the issue was a final decision of a state administrative agency, and that there was no legal merit to the remaining claims. The court held that the Council's failure to adopt a Master Plan within the statutory 18-month time period set forth in N.J.S.A. § 13:20-8(a) did not invalidate any subsequent adoption of the plan. The court further upheld the trial court's finding that the economic activity of farming did not fall within a protected right or economic or suspect classification. The court rejected the farmers' equal protection arguments and held that the farmers failed to articulate how the Highlands Act impeded their right or ability to farm and noted that the farmers had the opportunity to seek waivers. The court further upheld the constitutionality of the Highlands Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
