Township of Readington v. Solberg Aviation Co.


DOCKET NO. A-3083-07T3, A-1537-08T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


409 N.J. Super. 282; 976 A.2d 1100; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 205


April 27, 2009, Argued 
August 19, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 19, 2009.
Certification denied by Twp. of Readington v. Solberg, 2010 N.J. LEXIS 123 (N.J., Jan. 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hunterdon County, Docket No. L-468-06.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hunterdon County, granted summary judgment to plaintiff township and entered a condemnation judgment granting it title to a portion of defendant condemnee's property. While the condemnee's appeal was pending, the trial court allowed the township to withdraw money from its trust fund in order to pay post-taking real estate taxes on the property; the condemnee appealed this order as well.


OVERVIEW: The property the township condemned included an airport. The appeal raised two critical issues of law. The first was the preemptive effect of state aviation statutes, specifically the New Jersey Air Safety and Zoning Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 6:1-80 to 84, -88, and the New Jersey State Aviation Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 6:1-20 to -44, and regulations on land use authority. The second was the application of the principles enunciated in Mount Laurel Twp. v. MiPro Homes. The condemnee claimed that the taking was pretextual in an attempt to limit the use of airport property. As to this claim, the appellate court concluded that the condemnee presented a sufficient factual basis to overcome a motion for summary judgment; it further concluded that state statutes preempted certain aspects of local land use, constraining a municipality's exercise of its condemnation authority (Garden State Farms, Inc. v. Bay). In a consolidated appeal, the appellate court further concluded that under the New Jersey Eminent Domain Act of 1971, N.J.S.A. §§ 20:3-1 to -50, title passed to the township upon the filing of the declaration of taking, and the township improperly assessed taxes against the condemnee.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the summary judgment and remanded for trial on the issues raised by its opinion, including which, if any, of the parcels named in the township's condemnation action fell outside of the airport facilities area and safety zone, and the condemnee's arbitrariness claim. The order for withdrawal of funds was vacated; the trial court was to ensure that the condemnee was reimbursed for any money paid from the trust fund.

Presbyterian Home at Pennington, Inc. v. Borough of Pennington


DOCKET NO. A-6061-06T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


409 N.J. Super. 166; 976 A.2d 413; 25 N.J. Tax 249; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 196


October 29, 2008, Argued 
August 10, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:
Approved for Publication August 10, 2009.
Certification denied by Presbyterian Home at Pennington v. Borough of Pennington, 201 N.J. 143, 988 A.2d 563, 2010 N.J. LEXIS 78 (N.J., Jan. 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey, Docket Nos. 2348-2002; 4027-2003; 5159-2004; 7504-2005, whose opinion is published at 23 N.J. Tax 473 (Tax 2007).
Presbyterian Home at Pennington, Inc. v. Pennington Borough, 23 N.J. Tax 473, 2007 N.J. Tax LEXIS 10 (Tax Ct., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an assisted living facility, challenged the judgment of the Tax Court of New Jersey, which upheld respondent borough's denial of the facility's application for real estate property tax exemption under N.J.S.A. § 54:4-3.6 and granted the borough's motion for summary judgment. Three complaints had been filed in the action, challenging the denial of the exemption for tax years 2002, 2003, and 2004.


OVERVIEW: The borough contended that the facility was not organized exclusively for hospital purposes, was not used actually and exclusively for hospital purposes, and was designed to generate at profit. The borough also asserted that the facility made no provisions to provide for charitable care and provided none. In interpreting § 54:4-3.6, the Tax Court found that nursing homes and assisted living facilities were eligible for exemption from local property taxes, even if not part of or integrated into a hospital facility, but only if those facilities provide some measure of charitable care. The court held that the Tax Court judge erroneously inserted an additional qualification in § 54:4-3.6 that did not exist by imposing the charitable care component upon an assisted living facility for it to qualify for tax exemption under that hospital purposes provision. The court found that there was no ambiguity in the statute and that its plain language did not require an assisted living facility to provide charity care in order to qualify for the exemption.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying the facility's tax exemption for tax year 2002 and remanded the case to the Tax Court for a determination of when the facility was substantially completed. The court further reversed the orders denying the facility's tax exemption for tax years 2003 and 2004.

Thigpen v. City of East Orange


DOCKET NO. A-0456-07T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


408 N.J. Super. 331; 974 A.2d 1126; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 172


March 25, 2009, Submitted 
July 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication July 29, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, L-10090-94.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officers sued defendants, a city and others. Officer one alleged a N.J.S.A. § 40A:9-6 violation; officer two alleged malicious prosecution and invasion of privacy. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, dismissed officer two's non-economic damages claims as barred by the New Jersey Tort Claims Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 59:1-1 to 14-4. A jury returned a verdict for the officers. Defendants and officer two appealed.


OVERVIEW: Officer one alleged he was not compensated for his service as a de facto police sergeant or lieutenant. The appellate court held that the trial court was mistaken when it determined as a matter of law that defendants were liable in damages to officer one on his claim for service as the de facto supervisor of the traffic unit, because the proofs conflicted as to whether he held that office on a de facto basis. It rejected defendants' argument that his damages had to be limited to back pay, determining that if past and future pension benefits were found to be owing on retrial, defendants, not the New Jersey Division of Pensions, would be responsible for payment. Officer two sought economic and non-economic damages for malicious prosecution pursuant to N.J.S.A. § 2A:47A-1 and non-economic damages for invasion of privacy. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's determination that the claims were subject to the Tort Claims Act's injury threshold. Since that threshold was not met, officer two was entitled only to economic damages for malicious prosecution. It affirmed the dismissal of his non-economic damage claims based on malicious prosecution and invasion of privacy.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of officer two's cause of action for invasion of privacy and his claim for non-economic damages arising from his malicious prosecution cause of action was affirmed. The judgment in favor of officer one was reversed and the matter was remanded for a new trial as to whether he was the de facto supervisor of the traffic unit, utilizing the standards expressed in Jersey City v. Dept. of Civil Service.

State v. Moran


DOCKET NO. A-3810-07T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


408 N.J. Super. 412; 975 A.2d 480; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 171


February 9, 2009, Argued 
July 28, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication July 28, 2009.
Certification granted by, Stay granted by State v. Moran, 200 N.J. 547, 985 A.2d 645, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 1477 (2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Moran, 2010 N.J. LEXIS 588 (N.J., July 13, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County, Municipal Appeal No. 07-108.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County, which convicted her of reckless driving, in violation of N.J.S.A. § 39:4-96. In addition to a fine and costs, the municipal judge imposed a 45 day driver's license suspension pursuant to N.J.S.A. § 39:5-31. At issue in the case was the continued viability and constitutionality of § 39:5-31.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal that the evidence was insufficient to find her guilty of reckless driving and that if her conviction was sustained, the portion of her sentence imposing the 45-day driver's license suspension should be vacated. Defendant contended that § 39:5-31 was antiquated and should be given no effect, and that it should be declared unconstitutional because it is vague, overbroad, provided insufficient notice to the public, and was capable of widely disparate application in that it gave judges unbridled discretion. The court found that the evidence supported the municipal judge's findings and conclusions that defendant was guilty of reckless driving, particularly based on the testimony of an officer, who observed her passing in a left turn lane in an intersection. The court rejected defendant's constitutional and repeal by implication challenges to § 39:5-31. The court held that § 39:5-31, and the point system under the Motor Vehicle Code set forth in N.J.S.A. §§ 39:5-30 to -30.11, harmoniously coexisted, with each given effect. The court addressed the overbreath and vagueness arguments asserted by defendant and found no merit to either.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Hand v. Philadelphia Ins. Co.


DOCKET NO. A-1957-07T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


408 N.J. Super. 124; 973 A.2d 973; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 146


November 6, 2008, Argued 
July 1, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication July 1, 2009.
Certification denied by Hand v. Philadelphia Ins. Co., 200 N.J. 506, 983 A.2d 1113, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 1394 (2009)
Certification denied by Hand v. Philadelphia Ins. Co., 200 N.J. 506, 983 A.2d 1113, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 1378 (2009)
Subsequent appeal at Hand v. Phila. Ins. Co., 2012 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1787 (App.Div., July 25, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, Docket No. L-1738-07.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an insured's employee, sued defendant insurer to compel arbitration of her claim for underinsured motorist (UIM) benefits. Third-party defendant, plaintiff's personal auto insurance carrier, was made a party. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, applying the so-called "Scutari Amendment," N.J.S.A. § 17:28-1.1(f), enacted after the suit was filed, granted summary judgment to plaintiff. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was a passenger in her employer's car when she was injured in a collision caused by another motorist. She settled with the motorist for policy limits and then made a claim for UIM benefits under her employer's policy. Defendant denied the claim, contending that as her personal policy had a UIM limit of $ 100,000, the step-down provision in the employer's policy became operational. As a result, the available UIM limit under the policy was $ 100,000; thus, the motorist's vehicle was not underinsured, and plaintiff had no claim for UIM benefits. The trial court held that the Scutari Amendment, which required a business entity's insurer to provide the same UIM coverage to its insured's employees as it did to the named insureds, applied retroactively. Contrary to the result reached by its colleagues in Olkusz v. Brown, the appellate court concluded that the legislature implicitly intended the Scutari Amendment to be applied retroactively. However, under the facts of this case, to do so would have resulted in a manifest injustice to defendant, as prior law gave it a reasonable basis to believe that the policy provisions at issue were enforceable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings to resolve the issue of whether plaintiff was covered by third-party defendant's policy.

Affirmed by In re Civil Commitment of W.X.C., 204 N.J. 179, 8 A.3d 174, 2010 N.J. LEXIS 1213 (2010)

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, Docket No. SVP-458-07.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, which committed him to the Special Treatment Unit, pursuant to the Sexually Violent Predator Act (SVPA), N.J.S.A. §§ 30:4-27.24 to -27.38. Prior to appellant's release from prison, the State filed a petition to civilly commit him under the SVPA.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had been incarcerated for various crimes, including sexual offenses. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Davanne Realty v. Edison Tp.


DOCKET NO. A-0333-08T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


408 N.J. Super. 16; 972 A.2d 1164; 25 N.J. Tax 203; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 134


April 21, 2009, Argued 
June 15, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:
Approved for Publication June 15, 2009.
Certification granted Davanne Realty v. Edison Twp., 200 N.J. 371, 982 A.2d 458, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 1127 (2009)
Affirmed by Davanne Realty v. Edison Twp., 201 N.J. 280, 990 A.2d 639, 2010 N.J. LEXIS 231 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey, Docket No. 5066-2008.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of defendant township's assessed value of its commercial property. In conformity with L. 1979, c. 91, N.J.S.A. § 54:4-34, the Tax Court of New Jersey dismissed the action. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: As the taxpayer did not respond to the township's request for information on income derived from its property, the tax assessor valued the property using the information available to him. To show it was overtaxed, the taxpayer did not challenge the assessor's methodology but submitted to the tax court a valuation based on income it derived from leasing its property. The tax court held that under § 54:4-34, the taxpayer forfeited its right to appeal the assessment by failing to respond to the request for information within 45 days. The taxpayer contended that its tax bill was a fine, forfeiture, or penalty imposed in violation of the Excessive Fines Clause of the Eighth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VIII, and N.J. Const. article I, para. 12. The appellate court concluded that the tax court properly rejected this claim. The appeal-dismissal sanction of § 54:4-34 was not punishment because it was rationally related to the need to efficiently assess and collect property taxes based on property value; therefore, it did not implicate the Excessive Fines Clause. Further, the taxpayer had the right to challenge the assessor's methodology at a reasonableness hearing, but failed to do so.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Dragon v. New Jersey Dep't of Environmental Protection


DOCKET NO. A-5743-06T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


405 N.J. Super. 478; 965 A.2d 209; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 45


January 29, 2009, Argued 
March 6, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication March 6, 2009.
Certification denied by Dragon v. N.J. Dep't of Envtl. Prot., 2009 N.J. LEXIS 661 (N.J., May 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Department of Environmental Protection, 0103-02-0046.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection (DEP) entered into a settlement agreement that authorized respondent homeowner to tear down and reconstruct his oceanfront home without a permit otherwise required under the New Jersey Coastal Area Facility Review Act (CAFRA), N.J.S.A. §§ 13:19-1 to -21, and the DEP's Coastal High Hazard Areas Rule, N.J.A.C. 7:7E-3.18. Appellant neighbors sought review.


OVERVIEW: The homeowner proposed to expand the size and footprint of his home. At issue was whether an administrative agency, through its dispute resolution process, could effectively override statutory, as well as its own regulatory requirements. Here, after initially denying a CAFRA coastal general permit for the tear down and reconstruction of an oceanfront home nine feet closer to the ocean, the DEP, finding a "litigation risk," settled the homeowner's challenge to the DEP's denial by issuing a letter of authorization "in lieu of permit," approving the development subject to conditions designed to meet several of the environmental concerns underlying the regulation's development ban. On the neighbors' challenge to the DEP's authorization, the appellate court held that, given the express language of the exception to the regulatory development ban, which the homeowner clearly did not meet, the DEP did not correctly assess its "litigation risk," and that, in any event, the DEP could not use its settlement process to circumvent CAFRA's substantive permitting requirements to allow regulated development in a coastal region governed exclusively by CAFRA and its implementing regulations.


OUTCOME: The DEP's decision was reversed.

Dempsey v. Alston


DOCKET NO. A-4975-06T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


405 N.J. Super. 499; 966 A.2d 1; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 47


September 15, 2008, Argued 
March 5, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication March 5, 2009.
Certification denied by Dempsey v. Interim, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 570 (N.J., May 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Atlantic County, Docket No. C-121-06.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, parents and their son, sued defendants, a school district superintendent, an assistant principal, and a board of education. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Atlantic County, granted defendants summary judgment, rejecting plaintiffs' challenge to the constitutionality of N.J.S.A. § 18A:11-8, which authorized boards of education to adopt school dress code policies. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The board denied the parents' request that their son be allowed to opt out from the dress code policy based on their "constitutional rights"; this suit followed. Plaintiffs claimed that § 18A:11-8 was facially unconstitutional because it did not require school boards to adopt an opt-out provision, and violated privacy and freedom of expression rights. The appellate court found § 18A:11-8 constitutional on its face and as applied to the parents' son, a student in a public school district which had adopted a school dress code policy five years before the suit was filed. Section 18A:11-8 was rationally related to the State's legitimate interests in protecting and preserving the quality of its educational system. As there was no fundamental right to be exempt from a school dress code policy, § 18A:11-8's absence of a mandatory opt-out policy was constitutional. Dressing as one liked was not expressive conduct protected under the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I. Section 18A:11-8 was neither overbroad nor vague. The record showed that the board complied with the requirements of § 18A:11-8(a) in adopting the dress code policy; plaintiffs presented no evidence to the contrary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Raymour and Flanigan Furniture


DOCKET NO. A-4622-07T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


405 N.J. Super. 367; 964 A.2d 830; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 43; 157 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,760


January 6, 2009, Argued 
March 2, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication March 2, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a final decision of the Commissioner of the Department of Labor and Workforce Development, GE-851-0306-ZAY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged the final decision of the Commissioner of the New Jersey Department of Labor and Workforce Development, which determined that the employer did not qualify as a trucking industry employer and, consequently, was not exempt from paying certain employees overtime at the statutory rate, pursuant to the New Jersey Wage and Hour Law, N.J.S.A. §§ 34:11-56a to -56a38.


OVERVIEW: The case arose from an employee complaint that the employer was not paying its delivery employees the statutory overtime rate. The Commissioner held that the employer did not qualify as a trucking industry employer under the exemption set forth in N.J.S.A. § 34:11-56a4, allowing such employers to pay certain employees an overtime rate of not less than 1½ times the minimum wage, rather than the statutorily required overtime rate of 1½ times the employee's regular wage. The employer asserted that although it was in the retail industry, its facilities for delivery operations qualified as a trucking industry employer, as that term was defined under § 34:11-56a4 as any business or establishment primarily operating for the purpose of conveying property from one place to another. The court upheld the decision of the Commissioner, concluding that the employer's facilities in which it conducted its trucking operations were not separate establishments so as to qualify for the trucking industry employer exemption. As a result, the employer was required to pay all employees 1½ times the employee's regular hourly wage for each hour the employee worked in excess of 40 in any week.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commissioner's decision.

In re Disciplinary Action Against Gonzalez


DOCKET NO. A-1392-07T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


405 N.J. Super. 336; 964 A.2d 811; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 36


October 29, 2008, Argued 
February 25, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication February 25, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Waterfront Commission of New York Harbor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Waterfront Commission of New York Harbor, an instrumentality of New York State and New Jersey, determined that appellant employee violated the Commission's media and public relations policy by contacting a reporter without permission, and imposed a penalty of a 10-day suspension without pay. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a Commission detective, told a superior about a rat-infested dirt pile on Commission property near the employee's office building. Unsatisfied with the Commission's response, he contacted the federal Occupational Safety and Health Administration and the New Jersey Environmental Protection Agency. Since no regulatory action was taken, he contacted a television reporter, which led to the disciplinary proceedings. On appeal, he argued that his rights under the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I, had been violated. The appellate court held that the Commission's media relations policy, which prohibited employees from contacting the media without prior approval of the Commission's Executive Director, was overbroad and thus an unconstitutional prior restraint upon speech. It also held the that the policy had been unconstitutionally applied to the employee, who was disciplined for contacting the media to report a potentially toxic pile of dirt that had remained on the Commission's property for three years and the presence of dead rats in and around the dirt pile. He spoke to the reporter not only as an employee but also as a citizen on a matter of public concern.


OUTCOME: The Commission's media and public relations policy was declared unconstitutional, the disciplinary sanction imposed on the employee was vacated, and reimbursement of forfeited pay, with interest, was awarded to him.

 

309 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Horsnall v. Washington Tp. (Mercer County) Div. of Fire


DOCKET NO. A-0655-07T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


405 N.J. Super. 304; 964 A.2d 341; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 35; 28 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1775


October 20, 2008, Argued 
February 24, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication February 24, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, Docket No. L-418-07.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a captain in a township's former fire district, sued defendants, township officials and the township division of fire, seeking reinstatement and alleging denial of due process and violations of N.J.S.A. §§ 40A:14-19, -25. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, denied defendants' motion to dismiss, ordered reinstatement of plaintiff with back pay, but denied his request for counsel fees. Both sides appealed.


OVERVIEW: The township council adopted a resolution authorizing the dissolution of the fire district and applied to the local finance board of the department of county affairs, pursuant to N.J.S.A. § 40A:5A-20, to create the division of fire within the department of public safety. The township notified all fire district employees that they had to apply for employment with the township to serve in the division. Plaintiff filed a timely application, but was not offered employment. The appellate court held that plaintiff's right of review did not accrue when he received a letter notifying him that his employment would cease, but on the first day that he did not have a job. Therefore, his action in lieu of prerogative writs was filed within R. 4:69-6(a)'s 45-day time-limit. N.J.S.A. § 40A:14-19 gave firefighters a constitutionally protected property interest in their tenure and conferred a reasonable expectation of continued employment unless just cause was established for termination. The creation of the division of fire to replace the previously existing fire district did not eliminate fire district firefighters' statutory tenure protections under §§ 40A:14-19 and 40A:14-25.


OUTCOME: The judgment, including the denial of counsel fees, was affirmed.

 

310 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


R.R. v. New Jersey Dept. of Corrections


DOCKET NO. A-0508-07T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


404 N.J. Super. 468; 962 A.2d 563; 2009 N.J. Super. LEXIS 7


October 2, 2008, Submitted 
January 12, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication January 12, 2009.
Certification denied by R.R. v. New Jersey Dept. of Corrections, 198 N.J. 474, 968 A.2d 1190, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 369 (2009)
Related proceeding at Roberts v. Conway, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 78453 (D.N.J., Aug. 3, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Agency Decision of the New Jersey Department of Corrections.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After he served the maximum term of a sentence imposed for kidnapping and other crimes, appellant inmate was civilly committed to a Special Treatment Unit (STU) as a sexually violent predator, as defined by N.J.S.A. § 30:4-27.26. Respondent New Jersey Department of Corrections (DOC) denied his request for "marital privacy" and conjugal visitation. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that N.J.S.A. § 30:4-27.34(d) of New Jersey's Sexually Violent Predator Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 30:4-27.24 to -27.38, required the DOC to adopt less restrictive regulations than those for prisons. He also argued that he was being denied his protected liberty interest in marital privacy and conjugal visitation. The appellate court that a sexually violent predator who was civilly committed to an STU had no constitutional right to marital privacy and conjugal visitation, and that DOC regulations that did not establish such a right were properly promulgated and in accord with legislative intent. Both the New Jersey Department of Human Services and the DOC participated in establishing N.J.A.C. 10:36A-1.1 to -4.6 and engaged in the appropriate rulemaking process. The regulations' prohibition of conjugal visits was not unreasonable, as it protected visitors from persons found likely to commit acts of sexual violence. His liberty interest in conjugal relations was outweighed by the State's interest in security and rehabilitation. As the State had a rational basis for treating repetitive-compulsive sex offenders differently than others, his equal protection claim failed.


OUTCOME: The DOC's decision was affirmed.

Riverside Chiropractic Group v. Mercury Ins. Co.


DOCKET NO. A-3034-07T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


404 N.J. Super. 228; 961 A.2d 21; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 267


November 13, 2008, Argued 
December 17, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication December 17, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, Docket No. L-8691-07.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff chiropractic group filed a demand for arbitration of its claim against defendant insurer for personal injury protection (PIP) costs incurred by a patient. Pursuant to N.J.S.A § 2A:23A-13(a), plaintiff filed suit to vacate the arbitrator's decision. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, affirmed the arbitration award. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was an assignee of the insurance contract. The insurer denied plaintiff's pre-certification requests for payment for the treatments it had provided to the patient. The insurer's policy allowed, but did not require, plaintiff to arbitrate its PIP claims. The arbitrator found that the insurer's reasons for the pre-certification denials were sufficient, denied plaintiff most of the payments it sought, and awarded the insurer costs and counsel fees. On appeal, plaintiff challenged N.J.S.A. § 2A:23A-18(b) of the New Jersey Alternative Procedure for Dispute Resolution Act (APDRA), N.J.S.A. §§ 2A:23A-1 to -19, which barred appellate review, arguing that § 2A:23A-18(b) was unconstitutional as applied. The appellate court held that the statutory bar to appellate review was not unconstitutional as applied because the applicable insurance contract did not require the insured to file any claims it had in arbitration. The fact that plaintiff opted to arbitrate instead of sue amounted to a voluntary waiver of the right to appellate review. Plaintiff's claims did not involve a matter of public policy that warranted review under the appellate court's special supervisory function.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Mountain Hill, L.L.C. v. Township Comm. of Tp. Middletown


DOCKET NO. A-2404-06T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


403 N.J. Super. 146; 958 A.2d 1; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 197


January 22, 2008, Argued 
September 10, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication September 10, 2008.
Certification denied by Mountain Hill, L.L.C. v. Twp. Comm. of Middletown, 199 N.J. 129, 970 A.2d 1046, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 456 (2009)
Certification denied by Mountain Hill, L.L.C. v. Twp. Comm. of Middletown, 199 N.J. 129, 970 A.2d 1046, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 482 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Civil Part, Monmouth County, Docket Nos. L-2378-04, L-5591-04 and L-0296-05.
Mountain Hill, L.L.C. v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment of Tp. of Middletown, 403 N.J. Super. 210, 958 A.2d 42, 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 196 (App.Div., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer appealed the orders of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Civil Part, Monmouth County, which declared that defendants, a township planning board and the township committee, properly approved two ordinances, determined that the township mayor was not precluded from voting on them, and that a third permit application was subject to one of the ordinances. Defendants cross-appealed the dismissal of three complaints.


OVERVIEW: The parties had been embroiled in litigation for a decade with regard to plaintiff's development, which involved the filing of various complaints and prerogative writ actions on plaintiff's part with regard to defendants' attempts to stop the development. The appeal at issue concerned the events occurring after the denial of plaintiff's first and amended second as-of-right applications for a development permit. The main issue addressed by the court was the propriety of the township mayor's voting on the enactment of the ordinances at issue since she owned a title company that had done work for plaintiff over the years. The court concluded that a direct financial involvement existed on the part of the township mayor under the Local Government Ethics Law, N.J.S.A. §§ 40A:9- 22.1 to -22.25, which required her disqualification from voting on the ordinances and the master plan. The court noted that the termination of the involvement in 2000 was not so remote in time that she was permitted to participate in the municipal actions in 2001 and 2004 involving the ordinances and the master plan to have freed her of any conflict of interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders, in part, and remanded the case to the trial court for entry of judgments in two related cases invalidating the 2004 Master Plan and, in another case, invalidating the 2004 ordinance.

 

313 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Quezada


DOCKET NO. A-6472-05T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


402 N.J. Super. 277; 953 A.2d 1206; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 183


January 28, 2008, Argued 
August 13, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 13, 2008.
Related proceeding at Basauri v. AG of the United States, 2011 U.S. App. LEXIS 22067 (3d Cir., June 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County, Indictment No. 04-07-1027.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County, of official misconduct (N.J.S.A. 2C:30-2(a)), setting false fire alarms ( N.J.S.A. 2C:33-3), and committing a pattern of official misconduct (N.J.S.A. 2C:30-7). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a volunteer firefighter, admitted to making false fire alarms on three occasions. He argued that his convictions for misconduct and pattern of misconduct had to be reversed because as a matter of law, his conduct was not related to his office and he did not derive a benefit from his conduct. The appellate court held that when a volunteer firefighter called in a false alarm it was misconduct related to a public office or position, and defendant received a "benefit" by the joy or gratification of participating in the response or even by giving the unit work to keep it in existence. Although he was unpaid, he was a "public servant" under § 2C:30-2, Thus, a volunteer fireman who called in false alarms and responded to the scene of the reported fires could be convicted of official misconduct under § 2C:30-2. However, his conviction for setting false fire alarms, § 2C:33-3, merged into official misconduct because the false alarm constituted the official misconduct. There was no insufficiency with the proofs as defendant was identified as the caller, independent of his statement or admission, and the reasonable inferences warranted a finding that he received a "benefit."


OUTCOME: The appellate court ordered merger of the false alarm convictions with the official misconduct conviction and remanded for the correction of judgment. The judgment of conviction and sentences for official misconduct and pattern of misconduct were affirmed.

In re Attorney General's "Directive on Exit Polling: Media and Non-Partisan Public Interest Groups"


DOCKET NO. A-0543-07T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


402 N.J. Super. 118; 952 A.2d 1127; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 174


March 12, 2008, Argued 
August 6, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 6, 2008.
Certification granted by In re Attorney General's "Directive on Exit Polling: Media and Non-Partisan Public Interest Groups", 196 N.J. 599, 960 A.2d 395, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 1511 (2008)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by In re Atty General's "Directive on Exit Polling: Media & Non-Partisan Pub. Interest Groups", 2009 N.J. LEXIS 991 (N.J., Sept. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Agency Decision of the Department of Law and Public Safety, Office of the Attorney General.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a civil liberties organization, challenged the final agency decision of defendant, the Department of Law and Public Safety, Office of the Attorney General of the State of New Jersey, which upheld a Directive issued by defendant, the Attorney General of the State of New Jersey, with respect to exit polling activities on election days. The organization brought suit asserting various objections to the Directive.


OVERVIEW: The Directive, issued to County Boards of Election and County Superintendents of Election, set forth various guidelines to adhere to with regard to exit polling. The organization specifically challenged the Directive's prohibition against distribution of voters' rights cards within 100 feet of the polls. The organization asserted that the Directive was not statutorily authorized and, even if it was, it was not adopted in compliance with the Administrative Procedures Act (APA), N.J.S.A. §§ 52:14B-1 to -25. The court upheld the Directive as a formal position of the Attorney General that was consistent with conduct allowed at exit polling. The court found that the Directive was an effort to improve procedures and was an attempt to provide greater access to entities such as the organization. The court rejected the organization's challenges regarding the failure of the Directive to comply with the APA since it did not constitute improper rule-making.


OUTCOME: The court denied the organization's application to invalidate those portions of the Directive that barred the distribution of voters' rights cards within 100 feet of the entrance to a polling place and which required notification to an election board two weeks in advance of an election of those sites at which a non-partisan public interest group intended to conduct exit polling.

State ex rel. X.B.


DOCKET NO. A-3053-06T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


402 N.J. Super. 23; 952 A.2d 521; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 168


April 9, 2008, Submitted 
July 31, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication July 31, 2008.
Certification denied by In re X.B., 196 N.J. 601, 960 A.2d 395, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 1648 (N.J., Oct. 30, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Somerset County, Docket No. FJ-18-948-06.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Somerset County, adjudicated appellant juvenile delinquent of offenses that would have constituted the following crimes if committed by an adult: third-degree resisting arrest (N.J.S.A.§ 2C:29-2(a)), fourth-degree aggravated assault (N.J.S.A. § 2C:12-1(b)(5)(a)), and the petty disorderly persons offense of defiant trespass (N.J.S.A. § 2C:18-3(b)). Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for trespassing on public housing property, despite being notified that he was on a list prohibiting him from being on the housing complex property. Following his adjudication as a delinquent, appellant argued his inclusion on the list was unconstitutional as applied to him. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's finding of delinquency and found no constitutional infirmity as applied to him. Appellant did not contest the adjudication of delinquency for possession of a weapon that led to his being placed on the list, and made no effort to remove his name from the list. The appellate court did, however, caution public entities who maintained such lists to consider adopting regulations regarding one's placement on and removal from the list and establishing a procedure whereby one could challenge placement on the list. An officer's testimony that when he told appellant he was going to arrest him, appellant pulled back and struck the officer in the chest with his elbow; and that appellant refused to be handcuffed during a lawful arrest, was sufficient evidence to support appellant's adjudication for the resisting arrest and aggravated assault charges.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

New Jersey Shore Builders Ass'n v. Township of Jackson


DOCKET NO. A-5805-06T3, A-1563-07T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


401 N.J. Super. 152; 949 A.2d 312; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 139


May 13, 2008, Argued 
June 23, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication June 23, 2008.
Certification granted New Jersey Shore Builders Ass'n v. Township of Jackson, 197 N.J. 14, 960 A.2d 744, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 1747 (2008)
Certification granted Builders League of South Jersey v. EGG Harbor Tp., 197 N.J. 14, 960 A.2d 744, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 1725 (2008)
Affirmed by N.J. Shore Builders Ass'n v. Township of Jackson, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 666 (N.J., June 25, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, L-1823-03PW (Docket No. A-5805-06T3); and the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, L-0307-05PW (Docket No. A-1563-07T2).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent builders association sued appellant Jackson Township, challenging an ordinance requiring land set-asides. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, declared the ordinance unenforceable. Appellant builders association sued respondent Egg Harbor Township, raising a similar claim; the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, found the ordinance valid. The cases were consolidated for appeal.


OVERVIEW: Jackson Township's ordinance provided that at least 10 to 40 percent of a tract of land proposed for development, depending on the zoning district, had to set aside for open space. Egg Harbor Township's ordinance required a residential developer to set aside one-half acre for recreation and open space for each 1000 persons expected to reside in a proposed development. The issue was the authority of a municipality to require developers to set aside land for common open space or recreation, or make payments in lieu of those set-asides, as a condition of a development application. The Jackson Township trial court determined that the municipality's authority to make these exactions was limited to planned developments as defined in the New Jersey Municipal Land Use Law (MLUL), N.J.S.A. §§ 40:55D-1 to -163. The Egg Harbor Township trial court concluded that the exactions were justified in other than planned developments. The appellate court concluded that the MLUL did not empower municipal governments to require developers to set aside land for common open space or recreational areas, except with regard to applications for planned developments as defined in the MLUL.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order of the trial court in the Jackson Township case, and reversed the order of the trial court in the Egg Harbor Township case.

McGovern v. Borough of Harvey Cedars


DOCKET NO. A-0043-07T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


401 N.J. Super. 136; 949 A.2d 302; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 131


May 19, 2008, Argued 
June 19, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication June 19, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, L-3222-06.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, which dismissed his complaint in lieu of prerogative writs against defendants, a borough, its board of commissioners, and its zoning officer. The suit arose after plaintiff's application for a zoning permit was denied.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought to construct a ten-by-sixty foot lap pool between his oceanfront house and the ocean in the borough, but he was unable to get permission due to the building line ordinance enacted decades ago as a result of a disastrous storm. The building line ordinance precluded any construction east of a defined geographic line adjacent to the ocean-side perimeter of the borough. The zoning officer denied plaintiff's application for a zoning permit, because it would violate the building line ordinance as well as a setback portion of the zoning ordinance. The court found no impropriety with regard to the denial of the zoning permit since plaintiff was told from the beginning that his proposed pool project violated the building line ordinance. The court further found no due process violation and that CAFRA did not preempt the building line ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

State v. Fortin


DOCKET NO. A-3579-07T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


400 N.J. Super. 434; 948 A.2d 160; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 121


May 19, 2008, Argued 
June 4, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication June 4, 2008.
Appeal granted by State v. Fortin, 196 N.J. 340, 953 A.2d 760, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 901 (2008)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Fortin, 198 N.J. 619, 969 A.2d 1133, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 261 (N.J., May 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, Indictment No. 95-9-1197.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was granted leave to appeal the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, which determined that defendant was only eligible for a maximum sentence of life imprisonment with 30 years of parole ineligibility, the maximum authorized sentence at the time of his offense. The State had moved to sentence defendant under the new law, codified at N.J.S.A. § 2C:11-3(b)(4), to life imprisonment without parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder, which was committed in 1994. On August 22, 2000, six years after the offense occurred, and six months before the penalty phase proceedings in defendant's trial, the New Jersey Legislature amended § 2C:11-3 to permit a life sentence without parole in certain capital cases. Defendant endeavored to waive his rights under the ex post facto clause and asked that the new life-without-parole alternative be applied to him so that he could argue its application before the jury at the penalty phase. The trial court rejected the request and ruled that defendant could not waive an ex post facto objection to the new law. The court agreed and held that defendant was not subject to be sentenced to life-without-parole because, at the time of offense, the maximum parole ineligibility term was 30 years and under the December 17, 2007, amendments to the murder statute defendant was no longer able to present mitigating factors to reduce the sentence to such term if not outweighed by aggravating factors. The court noted that its holding was narrow in its application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order and remanded the case to the trial court for sentencing.

State v. Hewitt


DOCKET NO. A-5939-06T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


400 N.J. Super. 376; 947 A.2d 674; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 109


March 11, 2008, Submitted 
May 19, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication May 19, 2008.
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Hewitt, 2013 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 523 (App.Div., Mar. 8, 2013)
Related proceeding at Hewitt v. AG of the United States, 2017 U.S. App. LEXIS 6443 (3d Cir., Apr. 14, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County, Indictment No. 06-06-0777.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted the State's motion for leave to appeal from the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Burlington County, which granted defendants' motion to suppress. Defendants were indicted on various drug-related charges as a result of 1,400 pounds of marijuana being found in the truck-trailer they were operating.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' truck was stopped for an administrative search of the commercial vehicle, pursuant to federal and state law. The trooper conducting the search noticed the nervousness of one defendant and several irregularities existing with the trailer. After making those observations, the troopers arrested defendants. Thereafter, defendants' tractor-trailer was towed, and the troopers gained access to the secret compartment containing the marijuana. The trial court concluded that the safety inspection of defendants' truck was transformed into a search for evidence of a crime when the trooper discovered what appeared to be a hidden compartment at the front of the trailer, and therefore, the troopers should have obtained a warrant before taking steps to confirm the existence of the compartment and its contents. On appeal, the State argued that the troopers' search of the hidden compartment did not exceed the scope of the regulatory inspection of defendants' trailer. The court agreed and held that the warrantless search of the trailer, including the search of the hidden compartment, was during the course of a routine safety inspection and constituted a valid administrative search.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order suppressing the evidence obtained in that search.

Milford Mill 128, LLC v. Borough of Milford


DOCKET NO. A-5508-06T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


400 N.J. Super. 96; 946 A.2d 75; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 94


April 7, 2008, Argued 
May 2, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication May 2, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hunterdon County, Docket No. L-99-07.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant joint planning board and zoning board of adjustment declined to act on plaintiff developer's variance application. The developer filed an action in lieu of prerogative writs against the board and defendant borough, alleging various constitutional and statutory claims. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hunterdon County, dismissed the complaint without prejudice. The developer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The borough designated a defunct paper mill as an area in need of redevelopment under the New Jersey Local Redevelopment and Housing Law, N.J.S.A. §§ 40A:12A-1 to -49. The borough adopted a redevelopment plan for the site, calling for both commercial and residential uses and large areas set aside for open space and wetlands. The plan required a party seeking to develop the site to obtain from the borough council a determination of consistency with the plan before submitting its proposal to the board. The developer wished to develop the site with much higher densities and more expansive uses than allowed by the plan. If the variances were granted, the area's permitted residential density would vastly increase. The appellate court noted that pursuant to the plan, the developer had to obtain from the borough council a determination of consistency with the plan as a precondition of having its development project considered by the board. Its proposal was not a "minor exception" to the plan, but rather an attempt to rezone, de facto, the entire redevelopment area. Further, the challenge to the merits of the plan, filed over two years after its adoption, was untimely under R. 4:69-6(a).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. However, the dismissal was without prejudice to future proceedings, including a potential inverse condemnation action if the existing plan ultimately deprived the developer, or the title owner, of all economically beneficial uses of the property.

State v. Krause


DOCKET NO. A-3737-06T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


399 N.J. Super. 579; 945 A.2d 116; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 88


December 4, 2007, Submitted; April 8, 2008, Resubmitted 
April 17, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication April 17, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: December 4, 2007, Submitted
On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Warren County, A-30-06-YO9.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted and fined in the municipal court for violating a town's noise ordinance. He appealed. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Warren County, reversed on the ground that the noise ordinance was preempted by a state statute and administrative regulations to the extent that it regulated noise emanating from a commercial entity. The town appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant operated a roller skating rink; a neighbor, who lived 100 feet from the rink, complained that the music was too loud. The town's ordinance prohibited the making of loud, unnecessary noises likely to disturb others. The operation of a machine that was clearly audible 100 feet from the building in which it was located was prima facie evidence of a violation. Defendant failed to present evidence in the municipal court or in the intermediate appellate court indicating that the ordinance was not more stringent than the pertinent state regulation, N.J.A.C. 7:29-1.2(a), or that the ordinance had not been approved by the New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection. The instant court held that based on defendant's failure to meet his burden of proving facts that would establish that the town's noise ordinance was preempted by the New Jersey Noise Control Act of 1971, N.J.S.A. §§ 13:1G-1 to -23, the ordinance was valid. However, local noise ordinances could require DEP approval to be enforceable at least with respect to certain facilities, such as commercial and industrial sites.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed and the conviction was reinstated.

Leang v. Jersey City Bd. of Educ.


DOCKET NO. A-5777-05T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


399 N.J. Super. 329; 944 A.2d 675; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 77; 27 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1042


December 17, 2007, Argued 
April 2, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication April 2, 2008.
As Corrected April 25, 2008.
Certification granted by Leang v. Jersey City Bd. of Educ., 196 N.J. 87, 951 A.2d 1040, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 809 (2008)
Certification granted by Leang v. Jersey City Bd. of Educ., 196 N.J. 87, 951 A.2d 1040, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 808 (2008)
Certification denied by Leang v. Jersey City Bd. of Educ., 196 N.J. 598, 960 A.2d 393, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 1642 (2008)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Leang v. Jersey City Bd. of Educ., 198 N.J. 557, 969 A.2d 1097, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 167 (N.J., Apr. 16, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, Docket Nos. L-2732-03 and L-3422-04.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a teacher and her husband, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, which granted summary judgment dismissing all of their claims against defendants, a board of education, a supervising teacher, a principal, a superintendent, a medical center, and a mobile crisis unit. Plaintiffs asserted claims of false imprisonment, assault, and other torts arising from her employment termination.


OVERVIEW: The cause of action arose from the teacher making a comment to the supervising teacher that she was under a lot of stress, and the supervising teacher accused her of threatening to kill students and faculty. The teacher was detained for several hours and transported against her will to a crisis center where she was discharged later that same day. The trial court dismissed all of plaintiffs' claims upon concluding that they were barred by qualified immunity. The court found that the trial court erred in finding that the supervising teacher and the principal were immune from liability for any of the intentional tort claims asserted and the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim since both of those individuals participated in the detention of the teacher. The court held that the medical center and the mobile crisis unit were not public entities and did not enjoy the immunities of the Tort Claims Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 59:1-1 to 12-3. The school board was properly found to be immune on the intentional tort claims since it had no liability for the willful misconduct of its employees but the breach of contract claim against it should not have been dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, the dismissal of all claims against the superintendent and the dismissal of all of the intentional tort claims asserted against the school board. The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the supervising teacher and the principal as to all of the intentional tort claims and the federal civil rights claim as well as reversed the grant of summary judgment to the school board on the breach of contract claim.

In re Petition of S.D.


DOCKET NO. A-3427-06T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


399 N.J. Super. 107; 943 A.2d 188; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 65


December 19, 2007, Argued 
March 20, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication March 20, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Casino Control Commission, Docket No. PRN 40605.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant gambler challenged the decision of respondent, the New Jersey Casino Control Commission, which denied his petition for removal from the voluntary lifetime self-exclusion list (SEL). Following a series of letters and phone calls, the gambler filed his formal petition with the Commission seeking an order removing him from the SEL. The SEL was part of the New Jersey Casino Control Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 5:12-1 to 210.


OVERVIEW: The gambler had placed himself on the SEL. The gambler acknowledged that he voluntarily requested his placement on the SEL and understood that he would be under a lifetime ban from New Jersey casinos. The gambler sought removal from the SEL upon becoming aware that some out-of-state casinos affiliated with those in New Jersey would also exclude him from their gaming facilities. The Commission denied the application, concluding that the potential extra-territorial consequences of placement on New Jersey's SEL were collateral and do not negate the applicant's voluntary actions and that the harm was minimal when balanced against the statutory aims of the SEL. The Commission also determined that its revision of its form to include reference to that potential consequence after being informed of it by the gambler did not demonstrate an acknowledgement of a duty to disclose that information or the insufficiency of the prior form signed by him. The court found no discernible basis to second-guess the agency's decision and upheld the same and deferred to the Commission's expertise and experience in assessing the gambler's unique circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's decision.

New Jersey Citizens Underwriting Reciprocal Exchange v. Kieran Collins, D.C., LLC


DOCKET NO. A-3705-06T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


399 N.J. Super. 40; 942 A.2d 864; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 61


February 11, 2008, Argued 
March 18, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication March 18, 2008.
Certification denied by N.J. Citizens Underwriting Reciprocal Exch. v. Keiran, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 911 (N.J., July 11, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, Docket No. L-3394-06.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent insurer filed suit to upset an arbitrator's ruling in favor of appellant chiropractor, who treated an insured and his wife and child. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, noting that two arbitrations involving the same policy were decided at different times by different arbitrators, held that the first arbitrator's ruling in favor of the insurer applied to the second arbitration. The chiropractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insured's policy application stated he was single, and the only operator of the insured vehicle; in fact, he was married and his wife drove the vehicle. The insured, his wife, and child were injured in two separate accidents; the insurer refused coverage based on the insured's misrepresentations, and the matter was submitted to arbitration. Exercising its limited supervisory jurisdiction to review a trial judge's review of an arbitration award rendered under the New Jersey Alternative Procedure for Dispute Resolution Act (ADPRA), N.J.S.A. §§ 2A:23A-1 to -30, the appellate court concluded that the trial judge acted within his statutory jurisdiction in finding the arbitrator's failure to consolidate two related arbitrations, which resulted in inconsistent awards, constituted "prejudicial error" as defined by N.J.S.A. § 2A:23A-13(c)(5), thus permitting the trial judge's intervention. And, since the trial judge acted within his jurisdiction, the appellate court was precluded by N.J.S.A. § 2A:23A-18(b), which declared that "there shall be no further appeal or review" of a trial court's review of an ADPRA award, from examining the correctness of the trial judge's determination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The chiropractor's appeal of the order that reversed the arbitration award was dismissed pursuant to § 2A:23A-18(b).

Bacon v. New Jersey State Dep't of Educ.


DOCKET NO. A-2460-05T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


398 N.J. Super. 600; 942 A.2d 827; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 57


December 3, 2007, Argued 
March 14, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication March 14, 2008.
Certification denied by Bacon v. New Jersey State Dept. of Educ., 210 N.J. 218, 42 A.3d 890, 2012 N.J. LEXIS 530 (2012)
Related proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Bacon v. New Jersey State Dep't of Educ., 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 190 (App.Div., Nov. 6, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the State Board of Education, OAL Docket Nos. EDU 2637-00, EDU 2638-00, EDU 2639-00, EDU 2640-00, EDU 2641-00, EDU 2642-00, EDU 2643-00, EDU 2644-00, EDU 2645-00, EDU 2646-00, EDU 2649-00, EDU 2650-00, EDU 2651-00, EDU 2652-00, EDU 2654-00, EDU 2655-00, and EDU 2656-00.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, eight rural and poor school districts, challenged the final decision of respondent, the New Jersey State Board of Education, which initiated a process to systematically remedy the deficiencies that were found to have existed by the implementation of a school funding statute, the Comprehensive Educational Improvement and Financing Act of 1996, N.J.S.A. §§ 18A:7F-1 to -42. The suit was initiated via a declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The Board found that appellants' circumstances mirrored those of urban school districts receiving remedial relief in accordance with a series of New Jersey Supreme Court decisions, yet declined to require the same relief for appellants. The Board instead directed its Commissioner to design and conduct a needs assessment of each appellant, which the Commissioner failed to do, opting to await the fate of pending legislative proposals, which had since been enacted into law. The court, in recognizing the judiciary's stated preference for legislative and executive solutions to remedy constitutional violations, found no warrant to interfere with the approach ordered by the Board. The court also found no inconsistency in ordering the Commissioner to promptly proceed with a particularized needs assessment of appellants as a integral step in the Board's ultimate determination, on remand. The court noted that in making such an assessment, the Commissioner must determine whether the new funding formula, set forth in the School Funding Reform Act of 2008, L. 2007, c. 260, would afford appellants' students the thorough and efficient education to which they were constitutionally entitled.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the Board for further proceedings, including the necessity of conducting a needs assessment of appellants.

Harrison Redevelopment Agency v. DeRose


DOCKET NO. A-0958-06T2, A-0382-07T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


398 N.J. Super. 361; 942 A.2d 59; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 38


February 4, 2008, Argued 1


1 A-0958-06T2 was previously argued on November 5, 2007, without the amicus curiae, before this same panel, and was then reargued, along with A-0382-07T2, with the participation of the amicus curiae.

 
February 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication February 25, 2008.
Companion case at Harrison Redevelopment Agency v. Harrison Eagle, LLP, 2008 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2910 (2008)
Companion case at Harrison Redevelopment Agency v. Amaral Auto Ctr., Inc., 2008 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2301 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, Docket Nos. L-2001-06 and L-2744-07.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two consolidated cases, appellant landowner challenged the orders of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, which upheld the condemnation of his property by appellees, a town and its redevelopment agency, and that dismissed his counterclaim and third-party complaint. The property owner's claims were dismissed as untimely, pursuant to the Local Redevelopment and Housing Law (LRHL), N.J.S.A. §§ 40A:12A-1 to -49.


OVERVIEW: There were also two consolidated companion cases involved, for a total of four cases before the court. The property owner contested the blight designation of his property under the LRHL. The trial court ruled that the property owner's defense was time-barred, because he had not filed a timely action in lieu of prerogative writs under R. 4:69-6 after the town designated his property for redevelopment. Although the property owner had received notice by mail of the town's preliminary investigation of the proposed blight designation under N.J.S.A. § 40A:12A-6 of the LRHL, he and others in the proposed redevelopment zone were not individually notified when the town approved that designation. The court held that several deficiencies existed under § 40A:12A-6, but upheld its constitutionality. The court set forth three mandates necessary in providing notice to a property owner to satisfy due process. The court noted that the trial court failed to consider N.J. Const. art. VIII, § 3, para. 1, the Eminent Domain Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 20:3-1 to -50, and other applicable court rules in making its decision.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the final orders and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings. On remand, the trial court was directed to consider the merits of the property owner's contention that the proposed taking of his property for redevelopment was invalid, both in general and specifically.

DEG, LLC v. Township of Fairfield


DOCKET NO. A-5181-06T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


398 N.J. Super. 59; 939 A.2d 261; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 29


October 2, 2007, Argued 
January 31, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication January 31, 2008. As Corrected.
Certification granted by DEG, LLC v. Township of Fairfield, 195 N.J. 421, 949 A.2d 850, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 429 (2008)
Reversed by DEG, LLC v. Township of Fairfield, 198 N.J. 242, 966 A.2d 1036, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 94 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, Docket No. L-6984-05.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent lessee sued appellant township, alleging N.J.S.A. § 2C:34-7 and a zoning ordinance were unconstitutional. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, ordered the township to issue lessee the required permits. The parties then settled. Later, the lessee moved to enforce the consent judgment, and the township moved for relief from it under R. 4:50-1. The trial court granted the lessee's motion; the township appealed.


OVERVIEW: N.J.S.A. § 2C:34-7 barred sexually-oriented businesses in some locations, but could be constitutionally applied only if they were allowed elsewhere in the relevant market area. After the trial court ruled the ordinance banning such businesses anywhere in the township was facially unconstitutional, the parties entered into a settlement allowing the lessee to operate its business, but requiring it to apply for a nonconformity permit if the ordinance was amended to allow such businesses in other zones. The township enacted such an ordinance, and denied the lessee's permit application. The appellate court held that a governmental body had authority to enter into a settlement of a case challenging the constitutionality of a statute under which it agreed to an injunction against enforcement of the statute if it reasonably concluded there was a substantial question concerning the statute's constitutionality and the costs of the statute's defense were not justifiable. The governmental body could seek to vacate or modify the judgment memorializing such a settlement where it could show that enforcement of the judgment would no longer be equitable due to changes in the law or facts.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's the order granting the lessee's motion for enforcement of the consent judgment. It vacated paragraph two of the consent judgment, which required the lessee to apply for a nonconformity permit if the zoning ordinance was amended to allow sexually-oriented businesses in other zones, and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Read


DOCKET NO. A-1751-03T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


397 N.J. Super. 598; 938 A.2d 953; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 21

January 24, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication January 24, 2008.
Certification denied by N.J. v. Read, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 827 (N.J., June 11, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County, Indictment No. 02-01-0101.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was then 17 years old, was charged with acts of juvenile delinquency which, if committed by an adult, would have constituted armed robbery, and various other offenses. The prosecutor's motion to waive the charges to the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County, from the Family Part, was granted under the 2000 amendment to N.J.S.A. § 2A:4A-26, L. 1999, c. 373, § 1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant moved for reconsideration of the order waiving the charges against him to the Law Division. In support of his motion, defendant submitted a report by a psychiatrist which concluded that he had various psychological impairments that contributed to his poor judgment and lack of impulse control caused by a traumatic brain injury suffered in an auto accident. Defendant also had a severe drug dependency problem. The Family Part concluded that defendant's psychological impairments were not encompassed by the Attorney General's Guidelines for determining whether a Chart 1 charge against a juvenile over the age of 16 should be waived to the Law Division and that the prosecutor's decision to waive the charges against him did not constitute a patent and gross abuse of discretion. The court agreed and held that the Family Part was not required to consider the juvenile's alleged psychological impairments as they were not included in the factors that the guidelines required a prosecutor to consider. The court noted that defendant could not prevent the waiver of the charge to the adult court under the amendment to § 2A:4A-26(e).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the prosecutor's motion to waive the charges and the sentencing imposed against defendant.

People For Open Government v. Roberts


DOCKET NO. A-4926-05T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


397 N.J. Super. 502; 938 A.2d 158; 2008 N.J. Super. LEXIS 10


December 3, 2007, Argued 
January 9, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication January 9, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, L-2876-05.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, four individuals and an organization, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, which dismissed their suit against defendants, a city, its mayor, and three of its councilmen. By their cause of action, plaintiffs challenged the asserted lack of enforcement of an ordinance adopted by the city designed to curtail awarding municipal contracts to political contributors.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance at issue restricted certain political contributors from negotiating or entering into certain contracts with the city. The trial court dismissed the action upon determining that plaintiffs lacked standing to challenge the asserted lack of enforcement of the ordinance. The court found error, concluding that plaintiffs had a sufficient particularized interest in the enforcement of the ordinance, beyond their status as mere taxpayers, to afford them standing to pursue the lawsuit. By seeking to compel defendants to enforce the anti-pay-to-play ordinance enacted as a result of an initiative effort in which all plaintiffs were heavily involved, the court determined that the individual plaintiffs had that slight additional private interest coupled with the great public interest in seeking the enforcement of the ordinance to establish standing. The court also determined that plaintiffs did not need to demonstrate any additional special damages. Further, because the four individual plaintiffs had standing, the organizational plaintiff had standing as well.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Mercer County, No. C-14-06.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

State v. Emmons


DOCKET NO. A-5689-05T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


397 N.J. Super. 112; 936 A.2d 459; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 358


September 18, 2007, Argued 
December 7, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication December 7, 2007.
Certification denied by State v. Emmons, 195 N.J. 421, 949 A.2d 849, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 505 (2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Emmons, 2012 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 760 (App.Div., Apr. 10, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, Indictment No. 04-02-328.
State v. Emmons, 186 N.J. 601, 897 A.2d 1056, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 579 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for failure to appear in court without lawful excuse, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:29-7. He moved to dismiss the indictment on grounds § 2C:29-7 was unconstitutional. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, granted the motion. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 2C:29-7 was unconstitutional because it shifted the burden of proving the "without lawful excuse" and "knowing" mental culpability elements of the offense to the defendant. The appellate court noted that as § 2C:29-7 did not describe the requisite mens rea, under the "gap filler" provision of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:2-2(c)(3), the State had to show that defendant's failure to appear was "knowing." N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:29-7 was constitutional. Although a jury instruction in the language of the second sentence of § 2C:29-7 would impose an unconstitutional burden upon defendant to disprove the "knowing" mental culpability element of the offense, this constitutional defect could be avoided by a jury instruction that omitted any reference to defendant's having the burden to prove that his failure to appear was "not knowingly." Section 2C:29-7 was not unconstitutionally vague. A criminal defendant who had been directed to appear at a specified time and place was prohibited from failing to appear at that time and place. No person of ordinary intelligence would have any difficulty knowing what was prohibited by § 2C:29-7, so that he or she could act accordingly.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.
