State v. A.O.


DOCKET NO. A-5388-04T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


397 N.J. Super. 8; 935 A.2d 1202; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 349


September 24, 2007, Argued 
November 27, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication November 27, 2007.
Certification granted by State v. A.O., 194 N.J. 446, 945 A.2d 1289, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 321 (2008)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by, Remanded by State v. A.O., 2009 N.J. LEXIS 51 (N.J., Mar. 4, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, Indictment No. 01-12-1411.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, which convicted defendant for first-degree aggravated sexual assault on a child. Defendant was sentenced to 18 years imprisonment with a nine-year parole bar.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted based on the uncorroborated testimony of a child witness who had recanted her accusation and then withdrew the recantation. Prior to his arrest, defendant entered into a polygraph stipulation without advice of counsel. He failed the test, and the test result was admitted at his trial. The court determined that defendant's conviction required reversal because inducing an uncounseled defendant to sign a stipulation agreeing that polygraph results will be admissible at trial, violated an accused's Sixth Amendment right to trial counsel. In so holding, the court determined that State v. Reyes, 237 N.J. Super. 250, 567 A.2d 287 (App. Div. 1989) was no longer good law. The court further found that the trial court should have held a N.J.R.E. 104 hearing before barring defendant from introducing evidence that a few months after accusing him, the victim-witness accused another man of molesting her and then recanted her accusation. Because the polygraph evidence may well have made the difference between conviction and acquittal in the case, the court held that the conviction required reversal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case to the trial court for retrial. The court directed that, prior to retrial, the trial judge must conduct further proceedings to determine whether defendant was entitled to question witnesses about a subsequent incident in which the victim-witness accused another man of molesting her and then recanted that accusation.

 

333 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dixon


DOCKET NO. A-2419-04T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


396 N.J. Super. 329; 933 A.2d 978; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 331


October 1, 2007, Submitted 
October 24, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication October 24, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, Indictment No. 03-10-1325-I.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, which convicted her, following a jury trial, for second-degree conspiracy to commit both second-degree robbery and first-degree bias intimidation based on the victim's handicap, in violation of N.J.S.A. § 2C:5-2. Defendant also appealed from the sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from her attempt to collect back rent from the victim. The victim worked at a grocery store as a cart retriever and the evidence established that defendant and her two cohorts had visited the grocery store and attempted to retrieve money from the victim. In instructing the jury, the trial judge charged that to prove bias intimidation, the State had to prove that defendant committed the underlying crime of robbery and that she committed the crime with the purpose to intimidate the victim because of his handicap. The court held that the trial court erred in the jury instruction by not properly defining the term handicap because the trial court's instruction in no way connected the victim's disadvantage to his physical or mental disability as the victim could have been disadvantaged because he was outnumbered two to one by large assailants. In failing to properly define the term handicap, the trial court, in effect, relieved the State of its burden of proving a key element of the case. Since the verdict sheet required a separate verdict on the conspiracy to commit robbery charge, that conviction was sustained.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, in part, the aspect of the conspiracy conviction that was based on bias intimidation as a predicate offense and vacated the associated seven-year sentence. The court affirmed, in part, defendant's conviction for second-degree conspiracy to commit second-degree robbery and affirmed the imposition of the sentence for that conviction. The case was remanded to the trial court for correction of the judgment of conviction.

State v. DeAngelo


DOCKET NO. A-4229-05T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


396 N.J. Super. 23; 930 A.2d 1236; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 304; 182 L.R.R.M. 2743; 154 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,484


March 21, 2007, Argued 
September 13, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication September 13, 2007.
Certification granted by State v. DeAngelo, 193 N.J. 276, 937 A.2d 978, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1521 (2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Deangelo, 2009 N.J. LEXIS 10 (N.J., Feb. 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, 44-2005.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his conviction in municipal court, defendant had a trial de novo in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County. He was again convicted of violating Lawrence, N.J., Municipal Ordinance § 535(L)(2), which banned the display of balloon signs. He appealed, contending the ordinance was preempted by the National Labor Relations Act (NLRA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 151-69, and was otherwise invalid.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a senior union official. As part of a labor action, he authorized the union to display a balloon in the shape of a rat, as a symbol of protest against unfair labor practices. There was evidence that a rat was a well-known symbol of a labor dispute and a signal to third parties that there was an invisible picket line they should not cross. The focus of the appeal was the enforceability of the ordinance, which prevented the display of certain signs, including balloon signs. The appellate court rejected defendant's contention that an inflatable rat was not prohibited by the ordinance; "balloon signs or other inflated signs" designed to attract the attention of pedestrians and motorists were expressly banned. The ordinance, which did not affect the parties' rights in the labor dispute, was not preempted by the NLRA, nor did it abridge any party's freedom of expression. The ordinance's exemption for balloon signs for business grand openings did not violate the First Amendment. The ordinance was not void for vagueness. It was content-neutral and the record did not support a claim that it was selectively enforced against labor unions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

335 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Hetsberger v. Department of Corrections


DOCKET NO. A-4813-05T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


395 N.J. Super. 548; 929 A.2d 1139; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 295


March 27, 2007, Submitted 
August 24, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication August 24, 2007.
Appeal after remand at, Dismissed by Hetsberger v. Dep't of Corr., 2010 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1799 (App.Div., July 28, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, L-5546-04.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 suit against defendants, the New Jersey Department of Corrections (DOC) and its Commissioner, alleging they imposed a substantial burden on his religious exercise, in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000cc-1 of the Religious Land Use and Institutionalized Persons Act of 2000 (RLUIPA). The New Jersey Superior Court, Law Division, Middlesex County, granted defendants summary judgment; the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate became a member of a group -- which he claimed was a religious group -- that was perceived by DOC officials to be a security threat, and he was disciplined administratively for possessing the group's materials. The trial court, in granting defendants summary judgment, made no mention of RLUIPA but relied solely case law addressing claims of First Amendment violations. The appellate court held that the inmate had standing to file the suit, as he suffered detention, loss of commutation time, and confiscation of items under the policy he challenged. The trial court erred by limiting its analysis to Turner v. Safley First Amendment standards; the inmate was entitled to a summary judgment evaluation by the separate standards of RLUIPA. The appellate court did not reject the DOC's contention that prison security was a compelling state interest. But in order to apply RLUIPA standards, a determination had to be made, not only that a compelling state interest was involved, but also as to whether the DOC's policies represented the least restrictive means of furthering that compelling governmental interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a determination whether genuine issues of material fact existed in respect of the standards of RLUIPA, and for such proceedings as might be necessary to resolve those issues.

Jones v. Department of Community Affairs, Div. of Codes and Standards, Bureau of Rooming and Boarding House Standards


DOCKET NO. A-0701-05T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


395 N.J. Super. 632; 930 A.2d 477; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 296


April 17, 2007, Submitted 
August 24, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 24, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Civil Part, Burlington County, BUR-C-000141-05.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was transferred from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Civil Part, Burlington County. Defendant, the Bureau of Rooming and Boarding House Standards in the Division of Codes and Standards in the Department of Community Affairs, moved for a final remand and to supplement the record in the contested case involving plaintiffs, an individual tenant and a corporation.


OVERVIEW: The case was transferred to the court due to jurisdictional considerations. The court found that the issues between the parties dated back to 2001, when they entered a settlement agreement in respect of alleged violations of the Rooming and Boarding House Act of 1979, N.J.S.A. §§ 55:13B-1 to -21, regarding property in which the individual plaintiff resided. The Bureau, based on an investigation, determined that the property was being used as a boarding house and that plaintiffs were violating N.J.S.A. § 55:13B-7. When plaintiffs resisted the citation, the case was transmitted to the Office of Administrative Law (OAL) as a contested case. Plaintiffs raised a series of constitutional questions, and the Administrative Law Judge (ALJ) determined that it had no jurisdiction to hear and decide the constitutional issues raised by plaintiffs. The court disagreed and held that it was unable to consider the constitutional issues without a well-developed record isolating the essential factual issues. The court clarified that constitutional questions necessary to complete resolution of a contested case may be considered in an administrative proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the Bureau for re-transmittal to the OAL for a contested-case hearing and initial decision on all issues and for reference, in turn, to the Bureau head for a final decision. The court dismissed the Bureau's pending motion to supplement the record, without prejudice, subject to such determinations as the ALJ made in the conduct of the hearing regarding the record and the receipt of evidence and argument.

 

337 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fisher


DOCKET NO. A-3026-05T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


395 N.J. Super. 533; 929 A.2d 1130; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 290


November 8, 2006, Submitted 
August 14, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 14, 2007.
Certification denied by State v. Fisher, 192 N.J. 593, 934 A.2d 636, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1333 (N.J., Oct. 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Salem County, Indictment No. 05-04-00124.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Salem County, which denied his motion to declare N.J.S.A. § 2C:11-5.1 unconstitutional. Defendant had entered a conditional plea of guilty to a third degree charge of knowingly leaving the scene of a motor vehicle accident resulting in death, in violation of N.J.S.A. § 2C:11-5.1.


OVERVIEW: While driving in the early morning hours, defendant ran over what he thought was the carcass of a deer. The next day, he learned that he had hit a person but did not report the accident. While his car was at a dealership for repairs, it was identified as the vehicle involved in the accident. Because the decedent had been sitting or crouching down in the center of the road, defendant was not charged with an offense for causing death or injury. Defendant argued that the reporting requirements of § 2C:11-5.1 forced a driver involved in an accident that resulted in serious injury or a fatality to either abide by the statute and report his involvement, facing prosecution under other laws; or he could exercise his Fifth Amendment right to silence, facing prosecution under § 2C:11-5.1 and potentially other laws as well. The court disagreed and held that compliance with the reporting requirements would preclude prosecution under § 2C:11-5.1 and that compliance with those requirements would not violate a driver's privilege against self-incrimination as disclosure of one's name and address was essentially a neutral act and most accidents occurred without creating criminal liability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court denying defendant's motion to have the statute declared unconstitutional.

OFP, L.L.C. v. State


DOCKET NO. A-3190-05T1

August 10, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 10, 2007.
Related proceeding at Castle Rock Estates, LLC v. State, 2007 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2007 (2007)
Certification granted OFP, L.L.C. v. State, 193 N.J. 277, 937 A.2d 979, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1518 (2007)
Affirmed by OFP, L.L.C. v. State, 197 N.J. 418, 963 A.2d 810, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 1793 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County, Docket No. L-160-05.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County, which dismissed its complaint against respondent, the State of New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection (DEP), via summary judgment. The property owner's suit challenged the constitutionality of the Highlands Water Protection and Planning Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 13:20-1 to -35, as it applied to its property.


OVERVIEW: The property owner had a 93 acre tract of undeveloped land located within the preservation area in the Highlands region. The property owner asserted that the Highlands Act was unconstitutional, as applied to its property, because it operated to bar its planned development as otherwise permitted by law and resulted in a taking of its property without compensation. Based on the alleged retroactive application of the Act to the property owner's subdivision approval, the complaint also asserted that the Act violated the equal protection and due process guarantees of the United States and New Jersey Constitutions. The court agreed with the trial court's determination that the property owner had yet to exhaust all of its administrative remedies before bringing suit. Specifically, the administrative hardship waiver remedy of the Act had to be exhausted before the property owner was entitled to assert a claim that the Act's restrictions upon development in the preservation area of the Highlands Region had resulted in a regulatory taking. The court also upheld the validity of the retroactive application of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court rejected the property owner's challenges and affirmed the summary judgment dismissal of its complaint.

Pryor v. Department of Corrections


DOCKET NO. A-1707-04T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


395 N.J. Super. 471; 929 A.2d 1091; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 286


November 2, 2005, Submitted; December 20, 2006, Resubmitted 
August 9, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication August 9, 2007.
Certification denied by Pryor v. N.J. Dep't of Corr., 2008 N.J. LEXIS 371 (N.J., Mar. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a final agency decision of the Department of Corrections. November 2, 2005, Submitted April 27, 2006, Decided.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a final agency decision of respondent, the Department of Corrections, which upheld the following three regulations: N.J.A.C. 10A:18-9.6, N.J.A.C. 10A:16-4.4, and N.J.A.C. 10A:4-4.1. Appellant was incarcerated at the Adult Diagnostic and Treatment Center (ADTC) serving an aggregate sentence of life imprisonment with 25 years parole ineligibility for aggravated sexual assault and other crimes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged N.J.A.C. 10A:18-9.6, which allowed the ADTC administrator to prohibit ADTC inmates from receiving, possessing, distributing, or displaying not sexually oriented material that impeded the rehabilitation of inmates, as being unconstitutional because it restricted inmates' rights under common law and the First Amendment and the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The court held that the regulation was facially constitutional and was within the deference courts should give to the professional judgment of prison administrators obligated to further legitimate prison objectives dealing with rehabilitation. The court upheld the constitutionality of N.J.A.C. 10A:16-4.4, regulating exceptions to statutorily privileged inmate-therapist communications, as the regulation did not demonstrate deliberate indifference to serious medical needs of prisoners, as required to find an Eighth Amendment violation. The court summarily rejected appellant's challenge to N.J.A.C. 10A:4-4.1, since the Supreme Court of New Jersey recently upheld its constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court rejected appellant's challenges and held that all three regulations complied with the federal and New Jersey Constitutions. The court remanded the case to permit appellant to challenge the withholding of specific magazines, periodicals, and other material from him under the standards set forth in the case.

Quarto v. Adams


DOCKET NO. A-3904-06T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


395 N.J. Super. 502; 929 A.2d 1111; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 287


May 23, 2007, Argued 
August 9, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication August 9, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from a Final Agency Decision of the Division of Taxation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a same-sex couple, challenged the final agency decision of the Acting Director of the New Jersey Department of the Treasury, Division of Taxation, which denied appellants' request to file a joint State of New Jersey tax return for their 2006 earnings. The couple were residents of New Jersey and were married in Canada on July 28, 2003.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that the case really presented a timing issue, namely the transitional issue presented that was compelled by certain case law and the subsequent enactment of New Jersey's Civil Union Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 37:1-28 to -36, which permitted a same-sex couple, married in another jurisdiction before the statute's February 19, 2007, effective date, to file a joint New Jersey gross income tax return. The court held that appellants were entitled to declaratory relief concerning future tax years, which the Division did not oppose. However, the court held that the Division was not required to treat appellants' 2006 income as joint income. In contrast to appellants' assertion that they were entitled to full parity with married heterosexual couples on matters of taxation the moment that the case decision recognizing same-sex marriages and civil unions from other states and foreign jurisdictions was issued, the Division was entitled to a reasonable transition period to conform its forms and procedures to the equal protection constitutional and statutory principles espoused in the case law as to same-sex couples.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Acting Director of the Division.

Vineland Constr. Co., Inc. v. Township of Pennsauken


DOCKET NO. A-3136-05T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


395 N.J. Super. 230; 928 A.2d 856; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 272


March 6, 2007, Argued 
July 27, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication July 27, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, L-2223-04.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff construction company sued defendant township in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, contesting the township's designation of intervenor/defendant developer as master redeveloper for the township's redevelopment plan. The trial court dismissed the company's unconstitutional taking claim and its claim based on alleged political impropriety. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The township determined that approximately 600 acres of waterfront property, including 137 acres owned by the company, were in need of redevelopment. The township designated a master redeveloper for the entire area. The company did not contest the township's determination that the area was in need of redevelopment or the township's redevelopment plan. The company said it should be permitted to develop its own property as part of the redevelopment project and not be subject to eminent domain proceedings to turn its property over to the master redeveloper. The appellate court held the company did not have a constitutional right to redevelop its own property, and, once it was determined that the property was in need of redevelopment, thus establishing a public purpose, the township had the authority under the Local Redevelopment and Housing Law, N.J.S.A. §§ 40A:12A-1 to -73, to condemn the property and designate a master redeveloper to execute the redevelopment plan if the township reasonably concluded that such action was necessary or convenient. The record established a reasonable basis for the township's decision, and the court owed judicial deference to that legislative decision.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Seigel v. New Jersey Dept. of Environmental Protection


DOCKET NO. A-4109-05T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


395 N.J. Super. 604; 930 A.2d 461; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 291


May 31, 2007, Argued 
July 26, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication August 16, 2007.
Certification denied by Seigel v. N.J. Dep't of Envtl. Prot., 193 N.J. 277, 937 A.2d 978, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1539 (N.J., Dec. 5, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from State of New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection, Docket No. 1327-04-0014.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowner appealed from the final agency decision of respondent, the Department of Environmental Protection (DEP), which denied her application for a coastal general permit under the Coastal Area Facility Review Act (CAFRA), N.J.S.A. §§ 13:19-1 to -21. Consistent with the surrounding properties, petitioner sought to build a second home that faced the ocean on the portion of the property behind the current house.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner intended to occupy the oceanfront home with her aged and ailing mother. The DEP concluded that the entirety of petitioner's property was a primary frontal dune and denied the permit. The court determined that it was called upon to interpret the regulations promulgated by the DEP that defined a dune under N.J.A.C. 7:7E-3.16(a) and a primary frontal dune under N.J.A.C. 7:7-7.8(d)(1)(ii). The court interpreted the regulatory definitions and concluded that petitioner's entire property was not a primary frontal dune as well as determined that the proposed construction area was not on a dune. As a result, the court held that petitioner's property was not subject to the regulatory restrictions the DEP used to deny the application. The court also concluded that the DEP's interpretation of the regulatory language resulted in a fundamental unfairness to petitioner, whose surrounding neighbors had constructed similar homes on their adjacent properties.


OUTCOME: We reverse and remand the matter to DEP for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.

In re Civil Commitment of J.M.B.


DOCKET NO. A-6458-03T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


395 N.J. Super. 69; 928 A.2d 102; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 260


September 13, 2006, Argued 
July 20, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication July 20, 2007.
Certification granted In re Civil Commitment of J.M.B., 193 N.J. 222, 936 A.2d 969, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1433 (2007)
Affirmed by In re Civil Commitment of J.M.B., 2009 N.J. LEXIS 67 (N.J., Feb. 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, SVP-358-04.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a committee under the Sexually Violent Predator Act (SVPA), N.J.S.A. §§ 30:4-27.24 to -.38, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, which imposed his initial commitment. The committee was serving a state prison term of five years for tampering with a witness, in violation N.J.S.A. § 2C:28-5(a)(1), and an additional one year consecutive term for a probation violation.


OVERVIEW: The committee asserted on appeal that he was wrongfully committed because none of his convictions were sexually violent offenses as defined by N.J.S.A. § 30:4-27.26. The trial judge identified several convictions that established the committee as a sexually violent offender, including his last conviction for tampering with a witness. The trial judge underscored the circumstances involving that witness, which included the fact that the witness was an underage boy whom the committee had forced into bondage. The court upheld the commitment, concluding that § 30:4-27.26(b) was a catchall provision permitting the psychiatric experts and the trial court to consider the factual circumstances of the offenses in making the determination of whether sexually violent offenses were committed and whether the committee was a sexual predator under the SVPA. The court held that the use of force, coercion, threats of physical harm, lack of knowing consent, exploitation of underage victims, and grooming them with drugs or alcohol to satisfy his compulsive sexual gratification presented sufficient circumstances for the trial judge to have found the committee's offenses were sexually violent offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of commitment.

Owens v. Feigin


DOCKET NO. A-1074-06T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


394 N.J. Super. 85; 925 A.2d 106; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 188


February 15, 2007, Telephonically Argued 
June 21, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved For Publication June 21, 2007.
Appeal granted by Owens v. Feigin, 192 N.J. 473, 932 A.2d 25, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1085 (2007)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by, Remanded by Owens v. Feigin, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 564 (N.J., June 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, Docket No. L-1318-06.
Owens v. Feigin, 188 N.J. 344, 907 A.2d 1006, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1358 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents of a deceased child, sued respondent county medical examiner and others, alleging he violated N.J.S.A. § 10:6-2 of the New Jersey Civil Rights Act of 2004 (CRA). The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, dismissed the suit against the medical examiner on grounds the parents failed to file a notice against him under the New Jersey Tort Claims Act (TCA), N.J.S.A. § 59:1-1 et seq. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The medical examiner performed an autopsy on the 13-year-old child and concluded that he died due to cardiac arrhythmia resulting from a congenital heart defect. The parents alleged he "botched" the autopsy to help a state trooper avoid liability for the child's death. They never filed a notice of claim against the medical examiner under the TRA. The appellate court held that the notice requirements of the TCA did not apply to a claim based on the CRA. The broad remedial purposes of the CRA were not the sort of claims to which the TCA was a legislative response. The TCA was not designed to vindicate societal interests or to rectify public or governmental misconduct or to protect any individual constitutional interest or civil right, all matters that were addressed by the CRA. The appellate court did not express any view on whether the parents' claim against the medical examiner came within the CRA.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

State v. Morgan


DOCKET NO. A-5969-05T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


393 N.J. Super. 411; 923 A.2d 359; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 173


April 18, 2007, Argued  
June 6, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 6, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Criminal Part, Sussex County, Docket No. 46-08-05.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction entered by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Criminal Part, Sussex County, finding him guilty of speeding, in violation of N.J.S.A. § 39:4-98. The municipal court judge fined defendant $ 400 and imposed $ 39 in court costs. Though defendant's license was originally suspended for 60 days, such suspension was vacated after a de novo review of the record by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from an officer observing defendant driving at a high rate of speed, specifically 66 miles per hour (m.p.h.) in a 40 m.p.h. zone. The officer testified that she lost sight of defendant's vehicle for 30 seconds. On appeal, defendant contended that the State failed to demonstrate what the lawful speed was along that portion of the road because the officer's testimony, which was the only evidence adduced on the issue, was legally insufficient to meet the State's burden. Defendant cited case law precedent to support his argument on appeal, but the court distinguished such case law as involving issues wherein no evidence of the applicable speed limit was offered. Contrary to defendant's assertion, the court held that the sworn testimony of the officer was admissible and was sufficient proof of the lawful speed limit in the area in question. The court noted that the State was not obligated to prove the applicable speed limit through the introduction of a certified copy of an ordinance or regulation. The court refused to address defendant's challenge to the suspension of his license since that issue was moot based on the suspension being vacated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

CSX Transp., Inc. v. Director, Div. of Taxation


DOCKET NO. A-6102-04T3, A-6104-04T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


393 N.J. Super. 235; 923 A.2d 252; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 156


February 28, 2007, Argued  
May 24, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication May 24, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey, 4036-2000, 3779-2002, 5545-2002, 6337-2003 (CSX), and 4026-2000, 5594-2002, 6364-2003 (Norfolk Southern) which opinion is published at 22 N.J. Tax 399 (Tax 2005).
CSX Transp., Inc. v. Director, Div. of Taxation, 22 N.J. Tax 399, 2005 N.J. Tax LEXIS 13 (Tax Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two railroads, appealed the decision of the Tax Court (New Jersey), which affirmed the assessments imposed by defendant, the Director of the New Jersey Division of Taxation, of the Railroad Franchise Tax (RFT), pursuant to N.J.S.A. §§ 54:29A-13 to -15. One railroad appealed the RFT assessments against it for tax years 2000, 2001, 2002, and 2003, and the other challenged the assessments for tax years 2000, 2002, and 2003.


OVERVIEW: The Tax Court affirmed the assessments by granting the Director's motion for summary judgment. The tax was based on a calculation of each railroad's New Jersey-derived net operating income as a percentage of the net income the railroad derived operating world-wide. To compute the percentage of each railroad's net income attributable to its operations in New Jersey, the Director multiplied a fraction against each railroad's nationwide net income and then applied the statutory 10 percent tax rate to the railroad's income attributed to its New Jersey operations. On appeal, plaintiffs asserted that the Director's formula was facially unconstitutional and unconstitutional as applied to their operations and that genuine issues of material fact remained in dispute. The court held that the 10 percent RFT tax rate did not violate the 4-R Act, 49 U.S.C.S. § 11501, and that the Director's apportionment formula was not unconstitutional on its face. The court agreed that summary judgment in favor of the Director was inappropriate since plaintiffs presented sufficient evidence to establish a genuine issue of fact as to whether the formula was unconstitutional as applied to their operations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, the decision of the Tax Court upholding the constitutionality of the RFT. The court reversed, in part, the Tax Court decision affirming the tax assessments for the challenged tax years. The court remanded the case to the Tax Court for plaintiffs to have the opportunity to make a showing that the RFT was unconstitutional as applied to them.

In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 19:3, 19:4, 19:5 & 19:6


DOCKET NO. A-4174-03T3, A-3107-04T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


393 N.J. Super. 173; 922 A.2d 852; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 153


April 24, 2007, Argued  
May 21, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication May 21, 2007.
Certification denied by In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 19:3, 19:4, 19:5 and 19:6 ex. rel New Jersey Meadowlands Com'n, 194 N.J. 267, 944 A.2d 28, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 156 (2008)
Certification denied by In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 19:3, 19:4, 19:5 and 19:6 ex rel. New Jersey Meadowlands Com'n, 194 N.J. 268, 944 A.2d 28, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 178 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Meadowlands Commission and on transfer from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, L-14374-04.
In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 5:94 & 5:95 By New Jersey Council On Affordable Housing, 390 N.J. Super. 1, 914 A.2d 348, 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 20 (App.Div., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, plaintiffs, a fair housing center and a builders association, challenged the implementation of N.J.A.C. 19:4-3.8, and corresponding interim rules, by defendants, the New Jersey Meadowlands Commission (NJMC), the New Jersey Sports and Exposition Authority, and local entities. One case was transferred to the court directly from the NJMC, and the other came from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


OVERVIEW: The fair housing center sought invalidation of the master plan and zoning regulations adopted by the NJMC and wanted to ensure development of requisite affordable housing within its district. The builders association sought a judgment declaring that the NJMC and the Sports Authority had a constitutional obligation under the Mount Laurel Doctrine to provide low income housing opportunities. The builders association sought to have the regulations of both the NJMC and the Sports Authority declared unconstitutional. The court confirmed that under the New Jersey Constitution, as interpreted by the Mount Laurel cases, the NJMC was responsible for affirmative zoning and planning for affordable housing in its 21,000 acre district but that it had to act in consultation with the Council on Affordable Housing (COAH), with the NJMC's planning and zoning being based on municipal responsibilities for affordable housing as established by COAH. As such, the court held that the interim rules were held reasonable. The Sports Authority was held not to be responsible under the New Jersey Constitution for affordable housing within its portion of the Meadowlands District.


OUTCOME: The appeal as to the Sports Authority was dismissed and remanded to the trial court as to the local entities. Both appeals against the NJMC were remanded to the NJMC for further proceedings.

 

348 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Cruz v. Central Jersey Landscaping, Inc.


DOCKET NO. A-3843-04T1, A-3844-04T1, A-4379-04T1, A-4878-04T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


393 N.J. Super. 34; 922 A.2d 770; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 144


November 14, 2006, Argued  
May 14, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication May 14, 2007.
Reversed by, Remanded by Cruz v. Cent. Jersey Landscaping, Inc., 2008 N.J. LEXIS 567 (N.J., June 9, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Division of Workers' Compensation, Department of Labor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Four cases were consolidated on appeal that raised a common question with regard to petitioner dependents' claims for death benefits under the Workers' Compensation Act, N.J.S.A. §§ 34:15-1 to -142. In two cases, the dependents appealed and in the other two cases, respondent employers appealed the respective decision of the Division of Workers' Compensation, Department of Labor (New Jersey).


OVERVIEW: There was no dispute that each of the four dependents were eligible for death benefits as a result of the death of a worker. The common question in each case was whether the revised formula set forth in N.J.S.A. § 34:15-13(a), as amended by L. 2003, c. 253, §§ 1 and 4, should be applied to determine the amount of the benefit on a claim that arose prior to the effective date of the amendment. The two judges of compensation that decided the four cases answered that question differently. Under the revised formula, N.J.S.A. § 34:15-13(a) was amended to provide a benefit based on 70 percent of wages for one or more dependents, as opposed to the prior amount of 50 percent of wages for one dependent. The court held that the revised formula applied in pending cases to calculate death benefits for dates on and after the effective date of the amendment, namely January 14, 2004. In making its decision, the court found that the legislative history suggested that the New Jersey Legislature intended to extend the enhanced benefit to the dependents of eligible workers who died before the effective date of the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders entered by the judge of compensation with regard to the two petitions wherein the employers appealed. The court reversed the orders with regard to the petitions of the two appealing dependents and remanded those two cases to the Division for further proceedings.

In re Taylor


DOCKET NO. A-5522-05T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


393 N.J. Super. 213; 923 A.2d 239; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 140


March 20, 2007, Submitted  
May 9, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 9, 2007.
Certification granted by In re Taylor, 192 N.J. 294, 927 A.2d 1292, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 945 (2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by In re Taylor, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 891 (N.J., July 28, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cape May County, Docket No. CPM-L-156-06.
In re Taylor, 393 N.J. Super. 425, 923 A.2d 368, 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 353 (Law Div., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent county prosecutor filed a complaint under N.J.S.A. § 2A:158-7, seeking an order directing appellant county board of chosen freeholders to appropriate funds for the prosecutor's office. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cape May County, directed the freeholders to appropriate monies necessary to fund salary increases for certain employees of the prosecutor's office. The prosecutor and freeholders appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered the freeholders to appropriate funds for salary increases to prosecutor's office employees whose increases were not governed by existing collective negotiations agreements, but not for employees whose increases were governed by those agreements. The appellate court noted that when acting under § 2A:158-7, a trial judge was obliged to make his own original evaluation of a prosecutor's request for funds. His obligation was to determine what ought to be, as opposed to whether the action or inaction of the board of freeholders was arbitrary or unreasonable. He did not exercise judicial power; rather, § 2A:158-7 constituted him a legislative agent, and he exercised a delegated legislative function. Therefore, the appellate court's review was limited to whether the trial judge's decision was arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable. The appellate court found that it was not.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

350 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burr


DOCKET NO. A-4603-04T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


392 N.J. Super. 538; 921 A.2d 1135; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 137



May 8, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 8, 2007.
Certification granted by State v. Burr, 192 N.J. 478, 932 A.2d 28, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1077 (2007)
Affirmed by, Modified by, Remanded by State v. Burr, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 606 (N.J., June 11, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Argued September 26, 2006 - Remanded November 16, 2006. Resubmitted March 23, 2007. On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County and on remand from the Supreme Court, Indictment No. 04-05-0726.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, of second-degree sexual assault and third-degree endangering the welfare of a child. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of fondling his seven-year-old piano student through her clothing. He asserted that as he suffered from Asperger's Disorder, a form of autism, he did not know it was inappropriate to have the child sit on his lap. He was precluded from offering expert evidence about this disorder as an explanation for some of his arguably inappropriate behavior with the child. The appellate court held that it was not necessary for this disorder to be a "mental disease or defect" under the diminished capacity statute, N.J.S.A. § 2C:4-2, for the evidence to be admissible; it was sufficient if it had probative value on an issue in the case. The prosecutor strongly argued that defendant's behavior constituted "grooming" as a prelude to a sexual assault. Hence, the error was not harmless. N.J. R. Evid. 803(c)(27), the so-called "tender years" exception to the hearsay rule, did not run afoul of Crawford v. Washington and its progeny, insofar as it permitted introduction of evidence of a "testimonial" out-of-court statement of the victim (her videotaped interview by an investigator), because the victim testified in court and was able to be fully cross-examined on her allegations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

Raab v. Borough of Avalon


DOCKET NO. A-6028-04T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


392 N.J. Super. 499; 921 A.2d 470; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 132


December 20, 2006, Argued  
April 30, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication April 30, 2007.
Certification denied by, Appeal dismissed by Raab v. Borough of Avalon, 192 N.J. 475, 932 A.2d 26, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1159 (2007)
Subsequent appeal at, Motion denied by Raab v. Borough of Avalon, 2009 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1951 (App.Div., July 28, 2009)
Related proceeding at Raab v. Borough of Avalon, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 183837 (D.N.J., Dec. 30, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cape May County, Docket No. L-257-02.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cape May County, which granted summary judgment dismissal of their claims against defendant borough. Plaintiffs sought compensation for the physical taking of their property by the borough, together with damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' complaint concerned vacant oceanfront property that the parties stipulated was not capable of development, because it was situated directly between the borough's dune line established in 1968, and the ocean high-water line. The borough had previously rejected a proposed exchange of property by letter dated April 29, 2965, which was requested by plaintiffs' predecessors. The entire suit required a determination as to the applicable limitation period within which a private party must commence an action to challenge the taking of private property by a public entity, as an exercise of its police power, where the public entity's actions failed to comply with any of the statutory provisions governing the use of eminent domain and, therefore, presented an inverse condemnation matter. The court held that there was no question that the borough's actions in physically appropriating plaintiffs' property constituted a taking by inverse condemnation since no legal process was followed. The court also held that plaintiffs' cause of action accrued on or about April 26, 1965, and was, therefore, time-barred by the application of the six-year period set forth in N.J.S.A. § 2A:14-1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

 

352 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Todaro v. County of Union


DOCKET NO. A-2077-05T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


392 N.J. Super. 448; 920 A.2d 1243; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 118; 25 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1841


December 13, 2006, Argued  
April 19, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 19, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, L-4177-02.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sued defendants, a county and its director of public safety, alleging political discrimination. A jury returned a verdict in her favor, finding that her political affiliation was the reason she was not promoted. Ruling on her equitable claims, the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, granted a "rightful place" remedy but denied her request for instatement or front pay. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: A jury found that the employee was denied promotion to county superintendent of weights and measures solely due to her political affiliation, contrary to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The jury awarded compensatory damages and found that the employee was entitled to punitive damages. The parties reached a post-verdict settlement that resolved all issues except the official's claim for equitable relief, which they agreed to submit to the trial court. At the hearing, the trial court ordered that the employee receive salary and benefits comparable to what the incumbent superintendent was receiving at the time of the hearing. The appellate court concluded this "rightful place" remedy, which did not include front pay, failed to make the employee whole. As there was only one superintendent, instatement should have been viewed as a priority, even at the expense of the incumbent. The record did not support the trial court's findings that the incumbent was an "innocent party" who would be substantially harmed if demoted. Even assuming he was an "innocent party," he was not vested with a greater entitlement to the position than the employee, the victim of illegal discrimination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further fact-finding and reconsideration of the equitable remedies of instatement or, alternatively, front pay.

New Jersey Citizen Action, Inc. v. County of Bergen


DOCKET NO. A-4901-05T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


391 N.J. Super. 596; 919 A.2d 170; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 103


March 13, 2007, Argued  
April 9, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication April 9, 2007.
Certification denied by New Jersey Citizen Action, Inc. v. County of Bergen, 192 N.J. 597, 934 A.2d 639, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1321 (2007)
Certification denied by New Jersey Citizen Action, Inc. v. County of Bergen, 192 N.J. 597, 934 A.2d 639, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1292 (2007)
Certification denied by New Jersey Citizen Action, Inc. v. County of Bergen, 192 N.J. 597, 934 A.2d 639, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1369 (2007)
Appeal after remand at N.J. Citizen Action v. County of Bergen, 2011 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2092 (App.Div., Aug. 3, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, L-60902-05.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a citizen action group, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, which dismissed its complaint against defendants, a county improvement authority, a health care group, and others, for failure to state a claim. Plaintiffs filed a declaratory judgment action challenging the validity of two loans made by the authority to the health care group as violating N.J. Const. art. VIII, § 3, para. 2.


OVERVIEW: The county to whom the authority belonged decided to have its hospital managed by a private entity, the health care group. In establishing that contractual relationship in 1997, a lease was entered into which transferred operation of the hospital to the health care group for 19 years. Subsequently, the authority provided two loans to the health care group. One was a working capital loan of $ 6 million and the other was an accounts receivable loan of $ 27 million. The complaint alleged that the cash flow from the management fee and patient services established by the lease were sufficient for the operation of the hospital and that the loans were not needed for the public purpose of operating the hospital. Plaintiffs' complaint also alleged that the loans lacked consideration or lacked adequate consideration. In reviewing the complaint, the court was satisfied after viewing the lease and other documents to which the complaint referred, that it stated a cause of action for which relief can be granted. The court noted that factual findings were necessary as to plaintiffs' allegations as to no or inadequate consideration.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the complaint and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings, including the resolution of the factual issues as to whether any consideration was provided for with regard to the loans or, in the alternative, whether the consideration was inadequate.

State v. Bradshaw


DOCKET NO. A-4731-02T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


392 N.J. Super. 425; 920 A.2d 1228; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 93


February 6, 2007, Submitted  
April 2, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication May 1, 2007. As Amended May 1, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, Ind. No. 01-02-0155.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, of first-degree aggravated sexual assault, second-degree sexual assault, and second-degree robbery. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Trial evidence showed that defendant tackled and punched a woman, unsuccessfully tried to find her money, and raped her. After his arrest, defendant admitted having consensual intercourse with the victim. Although his DNA matched DNA recovered from the victim's vagina and underwear, there was some evidence that the semen samples were contaminated. Defendant testified that he had never met or had sex with the victim, and denied telling the police otherwise. The appellate court held that application of the notice of alibi rule, R. 3:12-2, to bar defendant's own testimony as to his whereabouts at the time of the crime, because of his failure to comply with R. 3:12-2, unconstitutionally infringed on defendant's state and federal right to testify, a right emanating from the due process and compulsory process guarantees. The appellate court disagreed with its contrary rulings in State v. Francis, 128 N.J. Super. 346, 320 A.2d 173 (App. Div. 1974), and State v. Gonzalez, 223 N.J. Super. 377, 538 A.2d 1261 (App. Div. 1988). Combined with a highly objectionable prosecutor summation in which he vouched for the victim's credibility with evidence outside the record, the error was not harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Kent


DOCKET NO. A-3137-05T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


391 N.J. Super. 352; 918 A.2d 626; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 83


January 31, 2007, Argued  
March 22, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 22, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Criminal Part, Passaic County, Municipal Appeal No. 4582.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Criminal Part, Passaic County, which upheld his conviction of a first-time Driving While Intoxicated (DWI) offense, in violation of N.J.S.A. § 39:4-50(a)(1)(i). Defendant was sentenced to serve 12 hours in treatment center; received a three-month driving suspension; and was ordered to pay fines, penalties and costs. Defendant's sentence was stayed pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended on appeal that the trial court erred by admitting into evidence a laboratory report prepared by a State Police chemist and a blood test certificate prepared pursuant to N.J.S.A. § 2A:62A-11 by a hospital employee who had extracted blood from defendant at the request of a police officer. The court agreed that the blood sample certification in the case at bar was not prepared to assist police with an ongoing emergency. Additionally, the primary purpose of the blood certificate was to preserve evidence for a future anticipated DWI prosecution and the samples were not extracted for purposes of medical treatment. As a result, because defendant was deprived of his constitutional rights of confrontation, the chemist's report and the hospital worker's blood test certificate were improperly admitted as part of the State's evidence at trial. Nevertheless, the court sustained defendant's DWI conviction under N.J.S.A. § 39:4-50 on independent grounds, based upon the arresting police officer's numerous field observations of intoxication that were not contradicted by competing proofs at the municipal trial and were ratified by the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and lifted the stay of his sentence.

Weeden v. City Council of the City of Trenton


DOCKET NO. A-2200-05T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


391 N.J. Super. 214; 917 A.2d 815; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 75


February 13, 2007, Argued  
March 19, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication March 19, 2007.
Certification denied by Weeden v. City Council of Trenton, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 757 (N.J., June 19, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a historical committee and eight others, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, which upheld the grant of a variance by defendants, a city council and its zoning board of adjustment, that permitted defendant applicant to construct a 60-seat restaurant with a drive-thru window in a designated redevelopment area of the city. Plaintiffs had filed a complaint in lieu of prerogative writs.


OVERVIEW: The city council had adopted a redevelopment plan seeking to achieve various objectives such as preserving historic significance of the area and providing new retail opportunities. Plaintiffs challenged the city council's decision granting the variance, contending that the zoning board of adjustment had no jurisdiction to grant variances from the requirements of the redevelopment plan, which prohibited drive-in restaurants. The complaint also challenged the zoning board of adjustment's decision as unreasonable, arbitrary, and capricious in that the city council did not make an independent determination and did not make sufficient findings to support its decision. The court agreed with the trial court that the the redevelopment plan was adopted as overlay zoning. As such, the court held that where a municipality adopts a redevelopment plan as overlay zoning in a zoning district, the zoning board of adjustment has jurisdiction to grant a variance from the provisions of the plan. The court noted that its opinion did not address applications from designated redevelopers that have covenanted with a municipality to carry out a redevelopment plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Mastondrea v. Occidental Hotels Management S.A.


DOCKET NO. A-6412-05T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


391 N.J. Super. 261; 918 A.2d 27; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 67


December 6, 2006, Argued telephonically  
March 9, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication March 9, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, L-704-04.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a Mexican hotel corporation, appealed, by leave granted, from an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, which denied the hotel's motion to dismiss the complaint of plaintiff guest for lack of personal jurisdiction, finding New Jersey law applicable to the guest's personal injury action and declining to dismiss her action on the ground of forum non conveniens. Defendant, a travel agency, was also a party.


OVERVIEW: While staying at the hotel located in Quintana Roo, Mexico, the guest slipped and fell on a wet exterior staircase and broke her ankle. Upon her return to New Jersey, she filed suit. The court agreed with the trial court's determination that the guest had sufficiently demonstrated that the hotel had contacts with New Jersey, consisting of a tour operator contract and marketing activities, which established that a causal relationship existed between those activities and the guest's vacation booking at the hotel to support the assertion of specific personal jurisdiction over the hotel. Traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice were not offended since the hotel was part of a world-wide travel empire well-equipped to defend litigation within the United States, which chose to market itself, through the travel agency, in New Jersey, and, thus, was deemed to have foreseen, and indeed to have induced, the presence of New Jersey guests at its Mexican facility. Though the court upheld the guest's forum choice, it disagreed with the trial court's choice of law decision since the law of Quintana Roo applied to the issues of apportionment of liability and damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying the hotel's motion to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction and on grounds of forum non conveniens. The court reversed the order on choice of law, determining that the law of Quintana Roo, Mexico, applied to the issues raised.

Rente v. Rente


DOCKET NO. A-2887-05T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


390 N.J. Super. 487; 915 A.2d 1099; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 48


January 17, 2007, Submitted  
February 15, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 15, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division - Family Part, Passaic County, FD-16-2072-05.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff paternal grandparents filed a petition seeking visitation with their grandson. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division-Family Part, Passaic County, granted the grandparents unsupervised weekly visitation pursuant to the New Jersey Grandparent Visitation Statute, N.J.S.A. § 9:2-7.1, and denied the mother's motion for reconsideration. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The child's mother had sole legal and physical custody; his father had supervised visitation on alternate weekends, monitored by the grandparents. The appellate court reversed the trial judge's grant of unsupervised weekly visitation to the grandparents under the grandparent visitation statute, § 9:2-7.1, as the grandparents' sole proof was that they babysat the toddler on occasion, and the mother was amenable to supervised visitation, possibly once a month. The grandparents' proofs were clearly insufficient to satisfy the high burden of proof of harm required under Moriarty v. Bradt to rebut the presumption in favor of parental decisionmaking. The trial judge made no finding, and the record was devoid of evidence to support a finding, that visitation was necessary and the monthly supervised visitation schedule offered by the mother was inadequate to avoid harm to the child. The trial judge also violated R. 5:3-3 by admitting his appointed expert's report into evidence without offering the mother an opportunity to obtain her own expert, providing a copy to her before the hearing, giving her a reasonable opportunity to depose him, or making him available for cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 5:94 & 5:95 By New Jersey Council On Affordable Housing


DOCKET NO. A-1960-04T3, A-2665-04T3, A-2674-04T3, A-2706-04T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


390 N.J. Super. 1; 914 A.2d 348; 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 20


October 25, 2006, Argued  
January 25, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at In re Grant of Third Round Substantive Certification to Pennsville Twp., 2007 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1844 (App.Div., Jan. 25, 2007)
Related proceeding at In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 19:3, 19:4, 19:5 & 19:6, 393 N.J. Super. 173, 922 A.2d 852, 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 153 (App.Div., 2007)
Certification denied by In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 5:94 & 5:95 by the New Jersey Council on Affordable Housing, 192 N.J. 71, 926 A.2d 856, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 890 (2007)
Certification denied by In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 5:94 & 5:95 by the New Jersey Council on Affordable Housing, 192 N.J. 72, 926 A.2d 856, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 891 (2007)

Related proceeding at Fair Share Housing Center, Inc. v. New Jersey State League of Municipalities, 413 N.J. Super. 423, 995 A.2d 865, 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 88 (App.Div., 2010)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by, Stay denied by In re Adoption of N.J.A.C. 5:96 and 5:97, 416 N.J. Super. 462, 6 A.3d 445, 2010 N.J. Super. LEXIS 201 (App.Div., 2010)
Related proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by In re Plan for Abolition of Council on Affordable Housing, 424 N.J. Super. 410, 38 A.3d 620, 2012 N.J. Super. LEXIS 33 (App.Div., 2012)
Related proceeding at In re Failure of the Council on Affordable Hous. to Adopt Trust Fund Commitment Regulations, 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 51 (App.Div., Apr. 9, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Council on Affordable Housing.
In re Adoption of Uniform Housing Affordability Controls, 390 N.J. Super. 89, 914 A.2d 402, 2007 N.J. Super. LEXIS 19 (App.Div., 2007)
In re Failure of New Jersey Council on Affordable Housing, 180 N.J. 148, 849 A.2d 182, 2004 N.J. LEXIS 538 (2004)
In re Six Month Extension of N.J.A.C. 5:91-1 et seq., 372 N.J. Super. 61, 855 A.2d 582, 2004 N.J. Super. LEXIS 344 (App.Div., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; remanded for regulatory action consistent with this opinion. We do not retain jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a builders association and others, challenged the decision of respondent, the New Jersey Council on Affordable Housing (COAH). In the appeal, the court addressed appellants' multifaceted challenge to the validity of the substantive rules of the COAH for the third round that calculated affordable housing needs from 1999 to 2014 and established criteria for satisfaction of the need between 2004 and 2014.


OVERVIEW: Appellants' challenges focused on several rules that governed the calculation of housing need, the allocation of that need, and compliance mechanisms. Appellants contended that COAH's methodology was contrary to, and ill-designed to respond to the constitutional mandate to provide affordable housing to the residents of the State of New Jersey as required by the Mount Laurel doctrine. The court found merit in COAH's methodology for calculating a municipality's rehabilitation share; its decision to no longer reallocate present need; its continued use of regional contribution agreements; and its regulations awarding credits, bonus credits, and vacant land adjustments. The court directed that the subtraction of tax credit developments from statewide and regional housing need must be further addressed by COAH in its rule making and that COAH's use of filtering in calculating statewide and regional housing need was unsupported by the record and required reconsideration. COAH's reliance on unissued data was invalidated as were the regulations that permitted municipalities to provide affordable housing without offsetting benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, certain portions of COAH's methodology but reversed, in part, other portions. The court remanded the case to COAH for promulgation of regulations in conformance with the Mount Laurel doctrine and the FHA within six months. The court also stayed the applications for substantive certification pending the amendment process on the part of COAH.

 

360 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Regency Sav. Bank, F.S.B. v. Southgate Corporate Office Center


DOCKET NO. A-1757-05T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


388 N.J. Super. 420; 908 A.2d 854; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 289


October 4, 2006, Argued  
October 25, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication October 25, 2006.
Certification denied by Regency Sav. Bank v. Southgate Corporate Office Ctr., 2007 N.J. LEXIS 163 (N.J., Jan. 29, 2007)
Certification denied by Regency Sav. Bank v. Southgate Corporate Office Ctr., 2007 N.J. LEXIS 164 (N.J., Jan. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Morris County, F-3943-04.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriff and respondent bank cross-appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Morris County, which awarded the sheriff a percentage fee of $ 5,050 based upon N.J.S.A. § 22A:4-8. The bank was a mortgagee and had obtained a judgment in foreclose on certain real property and issued a writ of execution to the sheriff. However, the bank settled with defendant mortgagors before the sheriff's sale.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff sought the amount of $ 730,000, which was based on the amount of the foreclosure judgment of almost $ 36 million. He asserted that sum was the settlement received by the bank from the mortgagors in consideration of the cancellation of the sheriff's sale. Alternatively, the bank argued that the sheriff was only entitled to the $ 50 minimum statutory fee or, at most, application of the statutory percentages to the $ 250,000 in cash it received from the mortgagors to cancel the sale, which sum, it asserted, was the settlement. Under that theory, the fee was $ 5,050, which the trial court had awarded. The court found N.J.S.A. § 22A:4-8 less than clear in that it did not indicate who paid the fee due to the sheriff, what sum the percentage fee was to be based upon, nor whether the percentage should be applied to the value of the property or to the amount of the settlement. The court determined that legislative intent and common sense required the fee for a cancelled mortgage foreclosure judgment to be based on the amount of the settlement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order awarding the sheriff a fee of $ 5,050, based on the settlement amount of $ 250,000.

 

361 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Oberhand v. Director, Div. of Taxation, Dept. of Treasury


DOCKET NO. A-3886-04T2, A-4243-04T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


388 N.J. Super. 239; 907 A.2d 428; 23 N.J. Tax 431; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 274


September 12, 2006, Argued  
September 29, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Approved For Publication September 29, 2006. Approved for Publication in the New Jersey Tax Court Reports.
Certification granted by Oberhand v. Director, Dep't of the Treasury, Div. of Tax., 190 N.J. 255, 919 A.2d 849, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 355 (2007)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Oberhand v. Director, Div. of Taxation, 2008 N.J. LEXIS 110 (N.J., Feb. 27, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Tax Court of New Jersey, 004150-03 and 006267-03.
Oberhand v. Director, Div. of Taxation, 22 N.J. Tax 55, 2005 N.J. Tax LEXIS 4 (Tax Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two decedents executed wills before N.J.S.A. § 54:38-1(a)(2)(a) was enacted and died after it went into effect. Respondents, the executor and executrix of the decedents' estates, sued appellant, the Director of the New Jersey Division of Taxation, challenging estate taxes imposed under § 54:38-1(a)(2)(a). The Tax Court of New Jersey held that the assessments had to be vacated because they were manifestly unjust. The Director appealed.


OVERVIEW: Section 54:38-1(a)(2)(a) imposed a tax on the estate of every New Jersey resident who died after December 31, 2001 that would have been subject to an estate tax under the version of the Internal Revenue Code in effect on December 31, 2001. Section 54:38-1(a)(2)(a) was enacted to preserve the New Jersey estate tax as it existed before sweeping changes were made to the federal estate tax laws. The tax court held that applying § 54:38-1(a)(2)(a) retroactively would be manifestly unjust under the circumstances. The appellate court held that this retroactive estate tax law, which was adopted on July 1, 2002, by L. 2002, c. 31, § 1, applied without exception to all resident decedents dying after December 31, 2001, including those who, like the decedents in question, drafted their wills before the statute was adopted to avoid federal and state taxes in a manner then permitted by law and who died after December 31, 2001, and before the adoption of the statute. The tax court opinion erred in granting the estates exemption from the tax due under the new law by application of the equitable doctrine of manifest injustice because that doctrine had no place in retroactive-taxation cases.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

362 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rountree


DOCKET NO. A-2043-02T1, A-5014-02T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


388 N.J. Super. 190; 906 A.2d 1124; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 270


September 28, 2005, Argued  
September 21, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 21, 2006.
Certification denied by State v. Rountree, 192 N.J. 66, 926 A.2d 852, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 850 (2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by, Certificate of appealability denied Rountree v. Balicki, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 93856 (D.N.J., Nov. 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, 93-10-2162-I and from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, 94-04-1187-I.
State v. Hawkins, 316 N.J. Super. 74, 719 A.2d 689, 1998 N.J. Super. LEXIS 437 (App.Div., 1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from two separate orders, one from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, and one from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, which each denied his petition for post-conviction relief (PCR). Defendant's appeals were argued before the court on the same date, and the court consolidated its opinion.


OVERVIEW: In Camden County, a jury found defendant guilty of first-degree robbery and third-degree hindering prosecution. That trial judge found that defendant used a real gun and sentenced him as a second offender under the Graves Act, N.J.S.A. § 2C:43-6(c), (d), (g), and (h) and N.J.S.A. § 2C:44-3(d). In Essex County, defendant entered a guilty plea to two second-degree Graves Act crimes: aggravated assault and possession of a firearm for an unlawful purpose. The court held that applying Apprendi to second-offender Graves Act mandatory extended-term sentences did not apply retroactively in the context of a collateral review. As to defendant's claim that counsel in both counties were ineffective for failing to move, pursuant to R. 3:25A-1, for consolidation of the indictments for purposes of plea negotiations and sentencing, the court agreed that counsel should have moved for consolidation. However, such failure only established the first prong of defendant's ineffective assistance claims as defendant failed to prove that his counsels' failures would have made a difference since he had rejected a plea offer that was as favorable as any he could have expected in a consolidated plea offer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both orders denying defendant's petition for PCR.

Salem Management Co. v. Township of Lopatcong


DOCKET NO. A-5981-04T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


387 N.J. Super. 573; 904 A.2d 839; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 259


March 7, 2006, Submitted  
August 21, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 21, 2006.
Certification denied by Salem Mgmt. Co. v. Twp. of Lopatcong, 188 N.J. 579, 911 A.2d 70, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1684 (N.J., Nov. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Civil Part, Warren County, WRN-L-92-04 and DC-1212-04 (consolidated).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord filed an action in lieu of prerogative writs against respondents, a township, its mayor and council, and some of the landlord's tenants, claiming the township's rent control ordinance was unconstitutional. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Civil Part, Warren County, granted respondents summary judgment; the landlord appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landlord owned more than 90 percent of the apartments in the township. The township rent leveling board ordered it to refund overcharges to tenants pursuant to the rent control ordinance. The landlord argued that ordinance was unconstitutional on its face and as applied and could not be extended to vacant apartments. The trial court disagreed. The monopolistic conditions of the rental market provided a rational basis for the ordinance under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:48-2. It interpreted the ordinance as allowing an increase on rents on apartments, occupied or vacant, by no more than three percent per annum per apartment. The appellate court rejected the landlord's constitutionally-based attack on the ordinance and upheld as well its application to vacant apartments. The landlord did not meet its burden to establish a lack of rational basis for the ordinance and failed to show it was denied a just and reasonable return on its investment because of the manner in which the ordinance was interpreted or applied. Its attack on the ordinance as applied for being unconstitutionally vague and overly burdensome was properly rejected as it failed to exhaust its remedies with the board.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Plemmons v. Blue Chip Ins. Services, Inc.


DOCKET NO. A-0414-04T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


387 N.J. Super. 551; 904 A.2d 825; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 256


March 14, 2006, Argued  
August 21, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 21, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, Docket No. L-5769-00.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a former real property owner, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, which dismissed his Consumer Fraud Act (CFA), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 56:8-1 to -20, claim against defendants, an insurance company and its agent. The owner also appealed the summary judgment dismissal of his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims against defendants, a borough, a chairperson, and his secretary.


OVERVIEW: The owner had purchased property in the borough with the intent to convert it from residential to commercial. Before the initial closing date, the owner contacted the agent to obtain insurance coverage for the property, paid a premium, and received a declaration sheet for a homeowner's policy. The policy was voided due to a delay in the closing date, and the agent allegedly never informed the owner that a commercial policy was required. Property damage occurred from a storm and allegedly from contractors for which the owner had no coverage. The court held that insurance brokers were semi-professionals who were excluded from liability under the CFA for the services they rendered within the scope of their professional licenses. Therefore, the trial court properly dismissed the CFA claims. The court further held that the owner's constitutional rights were not violated by any stop work orders issued, an alleged failure to give the owner a construction permit, nor for any delay in the borough issuing a resolution memorializing its approval of the owner's application for site plan approval since the owner failed to pursue any administrative and judicial remedies regarding such actions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
