Thurber v. City of Burlington


DOCKET NO. A-5382-04T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


387 N.J. Super. 279; 903 A.2d 1079; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 226


May 15, 2006, Submitted  
August 3, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 3, 2006.
Certification granted Thurber v. City of Burlington, 188 N.J. 579, 911 A.2d 70, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1679 (2006)
Certification granted Thurber v. City of Burlington, 188 N.J. 579, 911 A.2d 70, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1707 (2006)
Affirmed by Thurber v. City of Burlington, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 701 (N.J., June 20, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff municipal court employee sought review before the Merit System Board (New Jersey) of the termination of her employment, and the Board substituted a six-month suspension. Defendant city appealed, the employee cross-appealed, and the Judiciary and the assignment judge who ordered the employee's termination were allowed to intervene.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a deputy municipal court administrator, was arrested after a motor vehicle stop during which she caused damage to a police vehicle. Soon thereafter, the assignment judge directed the employee's employer, the city, to terminate her relationship with the municipal court. The city also terminated the employee from employment altogether. The employee's appeal to the Merit System Board resulted in a determination that a portion of her misconduct during the police encounter was brought about by a panic attack, although the Board did find that she engaged in conduct unbecoming of a public employee. The Board also found termination was unreasonable, directing instead that she be suspended without pay for six months. The appellate court held N.J. Ct. R. 1:33-4 did not give the assignment judge jurisdiction over this personnel decision and, if it did, principles of comity required deferral to the Merit System Board. The Board's findings and the six-month suspension were reasonable, in light of lesser sanctions imposed on municipal judges for similar conduct. The New Jersey Supreme Court did not intend N.J. Ct. R. 1:33-4 to envelop this case.


OUTCOME: The lower tribunal's decision was affirmed.

State v. Martinez


DOCKET NO. A-6115-02T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


387 N.J. Super. 129; 903 A.2d 457; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 225


October 18, 2005, Argued  
August 2, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication August 2, 2006.
Certification denied by State v. Martinez, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1693 (N.J., Nov. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, 02-01-0075-I.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County, which convicted him of various crimes, including possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, possession of a weapon while engaged in a drug activity, and child neglect. Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to convict him of child neglect and that the anti-merger provision of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-4.1(d) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Officers, acting pursuant to a search warrant, raided defendant's home and obtained evidence against him. On appeal from defendant's convictions, the court held that (1) the failure to give Hampton and Kociolek charges instructing the jury to disregard the alleged oral admission by defendant to a detective that he possessed weapons found in the bedroom unless they found the admission credible did not constitute plain error since two detectives testified that they found the weapons in the room occupied by defendant, within easy reach; (2) that defendant's motion to suppress evidence was properly denied because mistaken or incorrect statements in a search warrant affidavit were insufficient to grant a motion to suppress unless they were intentionally false or made with reckless disregard of the truth; (3) that filthy conditions in defendant's residence were an insufficient basis for a conviction for child neglect; and (4) that the anti-merger provision of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-5(a), requiring separate, consecutive sentences for possession with intent to distribute and possession of a weapon while engaged in drug activity, was constitutional under N.J. Const. art. I, para. 11.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for child neglect but affirmed the remainder of defendant's convictions. The court remanded the case for resentencing.

New Jersey State Bar Ass'n v. State


DOCKET NO. A-6188-04T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


387 N.J. Super. 24; 902 A.2d 944; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 216


April 5, 2006, Argued  
July 26, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication July 26, 2006.
Certification denied by N.J. State Bar Ass'n v. State, 188 N.J. 491, 909 A.2d 726, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1594 (N.J., Oct. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Union County, No. UNN-C-1-05.
N.J. State Bar Ass'n v. State, 382 N.J. Super. 284, 888 A.2d 526, 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 358 (Ch.Div., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an attorney and the New Jersey State Bar Association, sued defendants, the State of New Jersey and state officials, arguing that §§ 5, 6, 7, and 27 (2004 N.J. Laws 17, §§ 5, 6, 7, and 27) of the New Jersey Medical Access and Responsibility and Patient's First Act, 2004 N.J. Laws 17, were unconstitutional. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Union County, granted defendants summary judgment. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that certain provisions of the Act violated the Fourteenth Amendment's Equal Protection Clause; N.J. Const. art. I, para. 1; N.J. Const. art. VI, § 2, para. 3 (separation of powers); N.J. Const. art. IV, § 7, para. 9 (special legislation); and N.J. Const. art. VIII, § 3, paras. 2 and 3 (public spending for private purposes). The appellate court disagreed. The Act, (1) imposing a $ 75 tax on persons licensed to practice law in New Jersey; (2) directing complementary dispute resolution of certain medical malpractice actions; (3) authorizing the dismissal of a malpractice action upon a party filing an affidavit of non-involvement; and (4) specifying credentials of individuals executing an affidavit of merit or testifying as an expert witness, was constitutional. 2004 N.J. Laws 17, § 27, imposing the tax on attorneys, was rationally related to a legitimate state interest in providing access to medical care. The Act's "affidavit of noninvolvement" procedure and its provisions for complementary dispute resolution in certain cases did not invade the judiciary's role of creating procedural rules. The Act did not authorize spending public funds on private purposes.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Menorah Chapels at Millburn v. Needle


DOCKET NO. A-3499-03T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


386 N.J. Super. 100; 899 A.2d 316; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 165


November 9, 2005, Argued  
June 8, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication June 8, 2006.
Certification denied by Menorah Chapels at Millburn v. Needle, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1601 (N.J., Oct. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Special Civil Part, Essex County, DC-8636-02.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant customer challenged the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Special Civil Part, Essex County, which granted summary judgment on the complaint and dismissal of the customer's counterclaim. The customer also appealed from the award of counsel fees against him. Respondent, a funeral home, had brought a collection action demanding full payment for funeral services rendered.


OVERVIEW: The customer's counterclaim alleged that the failure to provide the required funeral services contracted for constituted negligence and breach of warranty resulting in emotional distress to the family. The cause of action arose from the customer contracting with the funeral home for the services involving his father-in-law, an orthodox Jew. Watchers, or shomerim, were to have conducted a continuous vigil over the body of the deceased until the time of the funeral. However, it was discovered that only three of the six shifts contracted for appeared. The customer asserted that he was entitled to a substantial discount due to the funeral home's failure to provide the full contracted-for services. The court found no evidential support for the motion judge's conclusion that the contract provisions regarding the enumerated goods and services was severable as such an intent clearly was not manifested by the parties at the time that the contract for services was executed. The court further found that the customer's counterclaim for emotional distress was dismissed in error as caselaw supported the recovery of damages for emotional distress arising out of a breach of contract.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment entered in favor of the funeral home, reversed the dismissal of the customer's counterclaim for breach of contract, and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial. The court also vacated the award of attorney's fees for further determination upon retrial.

State v. Walker


DOCKET NO. A-3632-02T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


385 N.J. Super. 388; 897 A.2d 411; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 145


February 6, 2006, Submitted  
March 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 12, 2006.
Certification denied by State v. Walker, 187 N.J. 83, 899 A.2d 305, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 977 (N.J., May 23, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, Indictment No. 01-12-1429.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, which convicted defendant of third degree possession of a controlled dangerous substance (CDS), third degree possession of a CDS with intent to distribute, and third degree maintaining a fortified premises. Following merger of the first two counts, defendant was sentenced to consecutive four-year terms of imprisonment on the second and third counts.


OVERVIEW: The police executed a warrant to search an apartment that did not authorize a no-knock entry. Upon a look-out warning of the approaching officers, a detective admittedly attempted to gain access to the apartment using a battering ram, without first knocking and announcing his presence. Because the front and rear doors were barricaded, the officers were unable to gain access. The police eventually searched the apartment and seized several vials of cocaine. Defendant asserted on appeal that the evidence seized should have been suppressed because the police violated the knock and announce terms of the warrant. The court disagreed and held that, due to the circumstances, the police acted reasonably to disregard those terms as the look-out created the exigent circumstances by alerting defendant. No due process nor double jeopardy rights of defendant were violated as to the imposition of the consecutive four-year terms of imprisonment since the plain language of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:35-4.1(c) prohibited merger and ordered consecutive terms for fortifying or maintaining a fortified structure and also for possessing drugs with intent to distribute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

In re Commitment of M.C.


DOCKET NO. A-2770-04T2, A-3221-04T5

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, CASC-1738-04 (A-2770-04T2); Gloucester County, GLSC-492-04 (A-3221-04T5).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two patients, challenged the respective orders with regard to each of them issued by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, which placed the two patients on continued extension pending placement (CEPP). The court consolidated the appeals to address the legal standards that governed a trial judge's discretion to extend CEPP under N.J. Ct. R. 4:74-7(h)(2).


OVERVIEW: The patients were each released but the court did not find the issues involving each matter moot since the issues raised were likely to arise again in other cases. The first patient sought release but received extended CEPP, despite that patient's mother being willing to have him return home temporarily for a maximum of 90 days. The questions the trial judge was required to resolve were limited, after finding that the person was not in need of commitment, to whether there was evidence that supported imposition of continued restrictions under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4-27.15(c) and N.J. Ct. R. 4:74-7(h)(1), or a delay of release pursuant to Rule 4:74-7(h)(2).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the respective orders placing the two patients on CEPP.

State v. Pineiro


DOCKET NO. A-4764-02T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


385 N.J. Super. 129; 896 A.2d 480; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 111


March 28, 2006, Submitted  
April 19, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Approved for Publication April 19, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cape May County, Indictment No. 02-04-00269-I.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pled guilty to absconding from parole (N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:29-5(b)), he moved to withdraw his guilty plea, to relieve assigned counsel, and to proceed pro se. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Cape May County, denied the motions and sentenced him to five years' imprisonment with a two and one-half year parole bar, to be served concurrent to any sentence imposed for violation of parole. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant maintained on appeal that his guilty plea lacked a factual basis. During the plea colloquy, he admitted violating § 2C:29-5(b) by leaving his assigned residence and by failing to contact his parole officer or to notify him of his new address. However, in response to the trial court's further questioning, he denied that he left his assigned residence for the purpose of hiding. He claimed he did so and became homeless because he was penniless and did not have his psychiatric medication. He also claimed that he called his parole officer "a couple times," but he was never in the office. The appellate court held that his subsequent admission, that he knew that by not telling his parole officer that he had moved, the officer would not be able to find him, was not sufficient to overcome the exculpatory information he had already placed on the record. When it became clear that he denied an essential element of the crime - hiding with the intent to avoid parole supervision -- the trial court should have refused to accept the plea as it lacked a factual basis.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Affirmed by State v. Elkwisni, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 438 (N.J., Apr. 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, Indictment No. S-1280-03.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, which convicted defendant after a jury trial of second-degree robbery, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:15-1, and third-degree possession of a weapon without a permit, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from a convenience store robbery. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court improperly permitted the State to introduce a statement he made about the location of the gun used in violation of his Miranda rights and that the prosecutor's cross-examination and comments in summation violated his privilege against self-incrimination. The court held that the record developed before the trial court at a N.J. R. Evid. 104 hearing was insufficient, as a matter of law, to determine beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant voluntarily and knowingly waived his constitutional rights under Miranda when he told the arresting officer where the gun was in the store. The court determined that reversal was not the appropriate remedy to correct the error but, rather, remand to the trial court for it to conduct a new hearing on voluntariness was required. The court further discerned no legal basis to reverse defendant's conviction based on an alleged Muhammad violation since defendant testified concerning statements he made to the police when he was arrested in support of his affirmative defense of duress, which the State was entitled to cross-examine him regarding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and remanded the case to the trial court to conduct a new hearing with respect to the admissibility of defendant's statements to the police.

A.A. v. State


DOCKET NO. A-2153-04T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION

December 12, 2005, Argued  
April 6, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication April 6, 2006.
Certification denied by, Appeal dismissed by A.A. v. State, 188 N.J. 346, 907 A.2d 1007, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1449 (2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by A. A. v. New Jersey, 127 S. Ct. 1169, 166 L. Ed. 2d 996, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 1199 (U.S., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, MER-L-20-04.
A. A. v. New Jersey, 341 F.3d 206, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 16853 (3d Cir. N.J., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed a class action suit against defendants, the State of New Jersey and state officials, challenging a constitutional amendment, N.J. Const. art. IV, § VII, para. 12, and its implementing legislation, the New Jersey Internet Registry Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:7-12 to -19. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, found the amendment and Act constitutional and dismissed the complaint. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The amendment authorized, and the Act implemented, the posting of identifying information and the whereabouts of sex offenders on the Internet. Plaintiffs alleged the amendment violated their rights under the federal Equal Protection, Ex Post Facto, and Double Jeopardy Clauses and the Act violated the ex post facto, double jeopardy, and privacy provisions of the N.J. Constitution. The appellate court disagreed. The amendment by its clear terms trumped "any other provision" of the N.J. Constitution. Therefore, although it applied to offenders convicted before its effective date, it was not invalidated by state constitutional provisions concerning retroactive impact. As the purpose of the amendment was not to punish, but to protect the public, it did not violate the federal Ex Post Facto and Double Jeopardy Clauses. As it served a legitimate state interest in public safety and did not irrationally target an unpopular group, it did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. It did not violate the federal right to privacy. Challenges to the Act under the ex post facto, double jeopardy, and privacy provisions of the state constitution failed since the amendment was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

International Union of Operating Engineers Local # 68 Welfare Fund v. Merck & Co., Inc.


DOCKET NO. A-0450-05T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


384 N.J. Super. 275; 894 A.2d 1136; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 95


January 31, 2006, Argued  
March 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 31, 2006.
Appeal granted by, Motion granted by International Union of Operating Engineers # 68 Welfare Fund v. Merck & Co., Inc., 188 N.J. 215, 902 A.2d 1232, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1159 (2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by International Union of Operating Engineers Local No. 68 Welfare Fund v. Merck & Co., Inc., 192 N.J. 372, 929 A.2d 1076, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1055 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, Docket No. L-3015-03.
Int'l Union v. Merck & Co., 2005 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 805 (Law Div., July 29, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a pharmaceutical corporation, filed an interlocutory appeal of the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, which certified a nationwide class in the case, found that the common issues among all members of the class predominated, and that New Jersey's Consumer Fraud Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 56:8-1 to -20, applied. Plaintiff, a union welfare fund, had instigated the consumer fraud action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged that while attempting to market and sell Vioxx, the pharmaceutical corporation fraudulently misrepresented and suppressed material information regarding the drug and its comparative safety and efficacy. According to plaintiff, third-party payors across the nation were specifically targeted with this false marketing, advertising, and promotion in an attempt to justify the high cost that was being charged for the new drug. The court upheld the certification of the nationwide class upon concluding that a common nucleus of operative facts predominated over questions affecting only individual members of the class. The court noted that although the amounts of loss may differ among the class members, such loss was ascertainable by a classwide expert and that, when aggregate damages were ascertained, a mechanism was easily established to calculate damages due to the individual class members. The court also agreed with the application of the Act to the case and the entire plaintiff class since New Jersey's interests in the litigation far outweighed the interests of all other states and New Jersey had the most significant relationship to the alleged fraud and the parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's rulings.


 

375 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Pryce v. Scharff


DOCKET NO. A-2190-04T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


384 N.J. Super. 197; 894 A.2d 668; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 88


February 7, 2006, Argued  
March 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 27, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Bergen County, FD-02-193-86.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Bergen County, which denied the mother's motion to assess interest on defendant father's overdue child support. The Bergen County Board of Social Services participated in the appeal, as it did at the trial level, and various amicus curiae were filed. The father had ceased to participate in the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The mother and father were separated and had one minor daughter. The father's child support payment was set at $ 35 per week in 1986. After he moved out-of-state and fell behind in his support payments, the trial court ordered him to pay $ 100 per week, including arrears, collected through the Probation Division of the Administrative Office of the Courts. The trial court denied the mother's request for post-judgment interest upon determining that the Probation Division was not required to collect post-judgment interest on child support arrears and that it did not have the technology to collect the same. The court held that the mother's motion should have been granted and the interest was required to have been added to the child support judgment which was to be collected through the Probation Division. The court noted that the mother calculated the interest on the overdue child support, which was 17 years in arrears. As such, the Probation Division was not required to use its resources to make the calculation and federal law required it to document interest owed on child support judgments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded the case to the trial court for entry of an order adding post-judgment interest to the father's Probation Division support account.

Stomel v. City of Camden


DOCKET NO. A-0490-04T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


383 N.J. Super. 615; 893 A.2d 32; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 71; 24 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 443


February 1, 2006, Argued  
March 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 10, 2006.
Certification granted by Stomel v. City of Camden, 188 N.J. 491, 909 A.2d 726, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1527 (2006)
Certification granted by Stomel v. City of Camden, 188 N.J. 491, 909 A.2d 726, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1529 (2006)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Stomel v. City of Camden, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 909 (N.J., July 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, L-9164-99.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, attorney, appealed the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, a city, its council, and its mayor. The summary judgment dismissed the attorney's claims alleging violations of the New Jersey Conscientious Employee Protection Act (CEPA), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 34:19-1 to -8, and his claim against the city for a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The attorney's § 1983 claim against the mayor had gone to trial and the attorney was awarded over $ 300,000 in damages. The attorney had been the public defender for the city for seven years when the mayor terminated his employment. The attorney asserted that he was dismissed in retaliation for reporting an extortion attempt and for providing testimony that implicated the mayor in unlawful activity. On appeal, the attorney sought reinstatement of his CEPA claims and his § 1983 claim against the city, asserting that the city was responsible for his judgment against the mayor under principles of agency and vicarious liability. The mayor was in federal prison and the attorney claimed the mayor was indigent. The court upheld the dismissal of the § 1983 claim against the city because the city council, the governing body of the city, never authorized the attorney's termination. The court found, however, that the trial court erred in dismissing the attorney's CEPA claim upon concluding that the attorney was not an employee because the attorney did fit the definition of an employee under the control and relative nature of the work tests and the city was required to have a public defender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, the summary judgment dismissing the attorney's § 1983 claim against the city and reversed, in part, the summary judgment dismissal of the attorney's CEPA claim. The court remanded the CEPA claim to the trial court for further proceedings.


 

379 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


DeSoto v. Smith


DOCKET NO. A-6730-03T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


383 N.J. Super. 384; 891 A.2d 1241; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 54


February 1, 2006, Argued Telephonically  
March 1, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication March 1, 2006.
Certification denied by DeSoto v. City of Jersey City, 187 N.J. 81, 899 A.2d 304, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 953 (N.J., May 23, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, Docket No. L-3394-04.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, former corporate counsel for defendant city, filed a complaint in lieu of prerogative writs against the city and defendant acting mayor to challenge her removal. The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, granted defendants' motion to dismiss. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the mayor who appointed plaintiff died, the council president became acting mayor and removed plaintiff from her position. She claimed that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:9-131, which allowed the council president to serve as both acting mayor and council president, violated the separation of powers doctrine. The appellate court disagreed. That doctrine was not generally applicable to a mayor-council government, and the acting mayor's action did not encroach on the council's functions, as the council could have countered it under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:69A-43(c). N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 40A:9-131 and 40A:16-12 were complementary, and the latter did not invalidate the former. Though N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:9-139 provided a one-year term, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:69A-43(c) authorized the mayor to remove plaintiff earlier unless two-thirds of the council opposed this. As to plaintiff's due process claim, since her employment was terminable at the acting mayor's discretion and her termination did not question her reputation and created no detriment to future employment, she had no property or liberty interest in her position. The acting mayor afforded her sufficient notice and opportunity to be heard.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

380 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Rowe v. Hoffmann-La Roche Inc.


DOCKET NO. A-4522-03T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


383 N.J. Super. 442; 892 A.2d 694; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 52


October 6, 2005, Argued  
February 28, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication February 28, 2006.
Reversed by, Remanded by Rowe v. Hoffman-La Roche, Inc., 2007 N.J. LEXIS 334 (N.J., Mar. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, L-2971-03.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff consumer challenged the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, which granted the motion for summary judgment and dismissal filed by defendants, a pharmaceutical company and its laboratory. The consumer had commenced a products liability suit against defendants, primarily asserting a failure-to-warn with regard to the drug Accutane. The consumer was a resident of the State of Michigan.


OVERVIEW: The consumer contended that, as a result of taking the prescription drug Accutane in 1997 for the treatment of his severe acne when he was 16 years old, he became severely depressed and attempted suicide several times. The consumer asserted that defendants failed to adequately warn him of the possible psychological side-effects of the drug. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment and dismissed the suit upon determining that Michigan law barred the consumer's claims since Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.2946(5) provided immunity to defendants. The court stated that the sole issue on review was whether New Jersey or Michigan law governed the consumer's failure-to-warn claim since a true conflict existed. The court concluded that the quality of New Jersey's contacts in the case, when combined with its strong governmental interest in deterring the manufacture of unsafe products within its borders, substantially outweighed the countervailing Michigan contacts and governmental interests in application of the Michigan statute. As such, the court held that New Jersey law applied to the consumer's products liability failure-to-warn claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Committee for a Better Twin Rivers v. Twin Rivers Homeowners' Ass'n


DOCKET NO. A-4047-03T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


383 N.J. Super. 22; 890 A.2d 947; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 29


April 19, 2005, Argued  
February 7, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Approved for Publication February 7, 2006.
Certification granted by Committee for a Better Twin Rivers v. Twin Rivers Homeowners' Ass'n, 186 N.J. 608, 897 A.2d 1061, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 537 (2006)
Certification denied by Committee for a Better Win Twin Rivers v. Twin Rivers Homeowners' Ass'n (TRHA), 188 N.J. 357, 907 A.2d 1016, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1655 (2006)
Certification denied by Committee for a Better Twin Rivers v. Twin Rivers Homeowners' Ass'n, 186 N.J. 608, 897 A.2d 1061, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 544 (2006)
Reversed by Committee for a Better Twin Rivers v. Twin Rivers Homeowners' Ass'n, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 911 (N.J., July 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, General Equity, Mercer County, C-121-00.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a committee of residents of a planned community and three individual members, and defendants, the community's homeowners' association, the community's trust, and the president of the association, cross-appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, General Equity, Mercer County. Plaintiffs sued for declaratory and injunctive relief regarding free speech and assembly rights.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' suit sought mandatory injunctive relief permitting the posting of political signs on the property of community residents and on common areas, use of the community room, equal access to the community's official newspaper, tape recording of board meetings, access to the association's financial records, and a list of all voting members. Summary judgment was granted to each party on the various counts of the complaint. The court acknowledged the growth of planned communities consisting of privately owned homes and commercial buildings that were open to the public but were trust-owned properties and facilities for the exclusive use of the residents and their invited guests. The main issue was that, much like a shopping mall, the community was like a town that delivered a broad range of traditional municipal services to its residents. As such, the community had a quasi-municipal status which subjected it to the constitutional limitations set forth in N.J. Const. art. I, paras. 6 and 18 as to the residents' expressive rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to defendants with regard to the financial records, alternative dispute resolution, and weighted voting issues. The court vacated the order dismissing the complaint and reversed the general ruling that the association was not subjected to constitutional limitations. Plaintiffs' expressive rights issues were remanded for reconsideration under the proper standard.

State ex rel. L.R.


DOCKET NO. A-3397-03T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


382 N.J. Super. 605; 890 A.2d 343; 2006 N.J. Super. LEXIS 15


December 5, 2005, Submitted  
January 30, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication January 30, 2006.
Certification denied by State ex rel. L.R., 2007 N.J. LEXIS 228 (N.J., Feb. 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Cumberland County, FJ-06-1780-03.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Cumberland County, which ordered him to provide a DNA sample pursuant to the DNA Database and Databank Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 53:1-20.17 to -20.28, after accepting defendant's guilty plea to criminal trespass and after finding that defendant reoffended within the six-month period of adjourned disposition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found a juvenile delinquent for criminal mischief with disposition adjourned for six months. He pled guilty to a later delinquency petition, resulting in probation on both delinquencies since the second occurred within six months of the first. He was ordered to submit a DNA sample under the Act. He appealed, challenging the constitutionality of the Act. He argued that his criminal mischief acts occurred before the effective date of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 53:1-20.20(h), which encompassed juveniles within the DNA sampling requirement, so the order violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws contained in either U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1, or N.J. Const. art. IV, § VII, para. 3. He also argued the sample was a violation of his right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures under either U.S. Const. amend. IV or N.J. Const. art. I, para. 7. The court found that the Act was not penal in nature, so ex post facto did not apply. It also found that taking the sample was a reasonable and minimal intrusion that was substantially outweighed by the State's interest in detecting recidivist offenders and in accurately identifying the perpetrators of crimes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order requiring defendant to submit to DNA testing.

State v. Gonzalez


DOCKET NO. A-0371-03T4, A-5368-02T4

December 20, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 20, 2005.
Certification denied by State v. Gonzalez, 192 N.J. 291, 927 A.2d 1290, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 1017 (2007)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by State v. Herrerra, 2010 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 2731 (App.Div., Nov. 12, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Warren County, I-93-03-0064.
State v. Gonzalez, 156 N.J. 406, 719 A.2d 638, 1998 N.J. LEXIS 1217 (1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the denial from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Warren County, of their respective motions for post-conviction relief. Defendants were tried separately and each was convicted of attempted murder, first-degree possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, attempted possession of a handgun for an unlawful purpose, attempted unlawful possession of a handgun, and hindering apprehension or prosecution.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, two black males, were riding in a car that was speeding along a highway, which was the basis the state trooper stopped their vehicle. The trooper was not satisfied with the identification documentation and responses from defendants. Eventually, one defendant attacked the trooper. Upon a search of defendants' vehicle, 14 ounces of cocaine was discovered. One defendant was also convicted of third-degree aggravated assault on a police officer and speeding, and the other was also convicted of simple assault. Each defendants' convictions were upheld on direct appeal. Defendants asserted in their post conviction relief motions that, the highway stop, subsequent questioning, and request from one defendant for consent to search were based upon unlawful profiling and should have been excluded as fruit of the poisonous tree. The court agreed with defendants that, without the requested discovery, including the trooper's individual records, defendants were unable to establish unlawful profiling and were denied the opportunity to challenge the trooper's credibility on the basis of his alleged history of profile stops.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court and remanded the case for an order granting defendants' discovery requests. The court directed the post-conviction court to thereafter reconsider defendants' post-conviction relief motions solely on issues arising from such discovery.

State v. Williams


DOCKET NO. A-0596-03T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


381 N.J. Super. 572; 887 A.2d 190; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 360


October 31, 2005, Submitted  
December 13, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication December 13, 2005.
Certification granted by State v. Williams, 188 N.J. 355, 907 A.2d 1014, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1349 (2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Williams, 192 N.J. 1, 926 A.2d 340, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 719 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Criminal Part, Union County, convicting him of unlawful possession of a weapon but acquitting him of a charge of obstruction. Among other issues, he argued on appeal that his motion to suppress the weapon found in his possession should have been granted.


OVERVIEW: Police officers received an anonymous tip that a black man dressed in black was selling drugs at a particular location, late at night, in a high-crime area. When the officers arrived, they found two such men. They focused on defendant, and immediately commenced a patdown, supposedly for their safety. Defendant tried to leave, and they arrested him for obstructing them in the performance of their duty, and then searched him, purportedly incident to that arrest. The court held that defendant's motion to suppress the gun found in that search should have been granted. The tipster's physical description had been general, and there was not enough detail about the alleged criminal activity to provide corroboration. The location, the hour, and even defendant's nervousness did not provide a sufficient basis to believe criminal activity was afoot. The State had also argued that the search was incident to a lawful arrest, but that argument also failed. Defendant had a right to try to leave an unlawful detention, so he should not have been arrested when he ran. Since the arrest was not lawful, neither was the search.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

L.W. ex rel. L.G. v. Toms River Regional Schools Bd. of Educ.


DOCKET NO. A-7084-03T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


381 N.J. Super. 465; 886 A.2d 1090; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 353; 97 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 74


October 3, 2005, Argued  
December 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION December 7, 2005. As Revised December 7, 2005.
Certification granted by L.W. ex rel. L.G. v. Toms River Regional Schools Bd. of Educ., 186 N.J. 605, 897 A.2d 1060, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 570 (2006)
Modified by, Affirmed by, Remanded by L.W. v. Toms River Reg'l Schs. Bd. of Educ., 2007 N.J. LEXIS 184 (N.J., Feb. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the a Final Administrative Decision of the Director of the Division on Civil Rights, DCR Docket No. PQ07IE-02596.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, a school district, challenged the final determination of the Director of the Division on Civil Rights (New Jersey), which found that the district violated the Law Against Discrimination (LAD), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 10:5-1 to -49, because complainant student was subjected to harassment by other students on the basis of his perceived sexual orientation. The director imposed equitable relief and awarded compensatory damages.


OVERVIEW: The student was subjected to numerous instances of bias-based harassment at his intermediate school by at least 18 different students in less than four months. The student also experienced such harassment while in high school and had suffered several physical assaults. The harassment revolved around the student's alleged perceived sexual orientation of being homosexual and he was repeatedly called a homo, fagot, and other derogatory terms. The director awarded the student $ 50,000 for emotional distress and his mother $ 10,000. The district was also ordered to take certain remedial actions in the nature of strengthening its anti-discrimination policy by explicitly stating such discrimination was prohibited, establish written procedures for staff to follow, to post such procedures, and distribute the same to all staff. The court upheld the viability of the claim and the award to the student but found that the director was required to reconsider the remedial measures ordered and to, instead, consider the statutory mandates set forth in N.J. Admin. Code tit. 6A, § 7-1.4(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed, in part, the decision with regard to the remedial measures ordered and remanded the case to the director for reconsideration of those mandates in light of the educational equity policies adopted by the district and any other actions taken to address peer harassment on the basis of sexual orientation. The court also reversed the award of damages to the mother. Otherwise, the decision was affirmed.

State v. Lee


DOCKET NO. A-5492-03T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


381 N.J. Super. 429; 886 A.2d 1066; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 349


May 10, 2005, Argued  
December 2, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 2, 2005.
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Lee, 190 N.J. 270, 920 A.2d 80, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 442 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Criminal Part, Passaic County, 05-09-0945.
State v. Lee, 2005 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 621 (App.Div., Nov. 21, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of first degree possession of CDS (cocaine) with intent to distribute, possession of drugs, third-degree escape, aggravated assault, and resisting arrest, appealed the denial of his motion for postconviction relief by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Criminal Part, Passaic County. He also appealed the denial of his motion for discovery that led to the dismissal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief. He sought discovery to support his claim that he had been the victim of racial profiling in the stop of a motor vehicle that had led to the discovery of the drugs on which the CDS charges were based and to the events that generated the other charges. Asserting the attenuation exception to the exclusionary rule defendant sought to rely on, the State filed a counter-motion to remove the case from selective discovery proceedings. The trial judge ruled that defendant was not entitled to discovery by reason of the attenuation exception as defendant and codefendant acted illegally in resisting arrest after they were unlawfully stopped based on their race. The matter was remanded back to Passaic County for disposition on the merits of the postconviction relief application. The appellate court held that while it rejected the practice of racial profiling, it also disfavored resistive and threatening conduct by a person unlawfully stopped or detained against the offending police officers. No good public purpose was served by ignoring or rewarding such anti-social acts.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed both as to the denial of the requested discovery and the dismissal of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

State v. N.G.


DOCKET NO. A-2011-04T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


381 N.J. Super. 352; 886 A.2d 186; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 345


November 10, 2005, Submitted  
November 28, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication November 28, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, 03-05-0434-I.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, that sentenced him to eight years at the Adult Diagnostic and Treatment Center (ADTC) under N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:47-1 to -10 (the Act); defendant claimed, inter alia, that the Act was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Between 1991 and 1997, defendant committed one or more acts of sexual abuse upon his nieces, who were less than 13 years old at the time. Defendant claimed that he was under the influence of alcohol at the time. At a hearing to determine defendant's eligibility for confinement to the ADTC, the parties' experts used the common English language definitions of "repetitive," meaning something that happens more than once, and "compulsive," meaning an irresistible urge to perform some irrational behavior. The appellate court held that although the Act did not define the terms "repetitive" or "compulsive," they were to be given their ordinary and well-understood meanings. Because the definitions were not abstract and could be understood by a citizen of average intelligence, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2C:47-1 to -10 were not unconstitutionally vague. The trial court found that defendant's conduct was characterized by a pattern of repetitive, compulsive behavior at the time it found him qualified for confinement at the ADTC as well as at the time the offenses were committed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

388 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


Daniels v. Daniels


DOCKET NO. A-7123-03T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


381 N.J. Super. 286; 885 A.2d 524; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 338


October 3, 2005, Argued  
November 16, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication November 16, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Reargued October 28, 2005. On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Morris County, FD-14-414-04.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandmother appealed from an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Morris County, that dismissed her complaint under the New Jersey Grandparent Visitation Statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 9:2-7.1, seeking visitation with her grandchildren despite the objections of defendant parents.


OVERVIEW: The grandmother and the parents had always differed in their child-rearing ideas, and the parents had never encouraged contact between the grandmother and the grandchildren. The grandmother brought an action under the Visitation Statute, indicating in her pleadings that contact with grandparents was a good thing and that the children were being deprived of potentially happy memories. The court followed New Jersey case law that interpreted the Statute in a manner that did not violate parents' due process rights to raise their children as they saw fit. Therefore, a grandparent seeking visitation had to show that failure to order visitation would actually harm the children; this would also normally entail a showing of a close relationship of long standing. The grandmother argued that she needed discovery to show that harm could result, but the court held that such a requirement would put too heavy a financial and psychological burden on families. Since the grandmother had failed even to allege that harm would result, dismissal was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of dismissal.

 

389 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


DOCKET NO. A-0789-05T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


381 N.J. Super. 41; 884 A.2d 808; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 308


October 12, 2005, Argued  
October 12, 2005, Decided  
October 12, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] APPROVED FOR PUBLICATION, October 21, 2005.
Appeal granted by State v. Clark, 187 N.J. 75, 899 A.2d 298, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 918 (2006)
Affirmed by, Remanded by, Stay dissolved by New Jersey v. Clark, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 703 (N.J., June 21, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County (New Jersey), order quashing a subpoena issued by the State requiring an investigator for movant New Jersey Supreme Court Advisory Committee on Judicial Conduct (ACJC) to testify, and produce records, regarding a disciplinary investigation of defendant judge, one of three defendants in the underlying criminal action. The ACJC claimed confidentiality under N.J. Ct. R. 2:15-20.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, a municipal judge and two other local officials, had been accused of tampering with public records in order to do an illegal favor for a jail inmate. The ACJC had commenced a judicial disciplinary investigation at the same time the State commenced its criminal investigation. Defendants were eventually indicted, and the State subpoenaed the ACJC's investigation results. The trial court based its decision to quash the subpoena on the N.J. Ct. R. 2:15-20 designation of such materials as confidential, but the court held that the rule did not apply once the reason for its existence could no longer be served. The rule protected the privacy of judges until they had actually been found to have engaged in misconduct, at which point the ACJC's findings were no longer protected by confidentiality. Once a judge had been indicted in the same matter, there was no privacy protection, as in the case of any other defendant. At that point, the strong public policy favoring disclosure trumped the rule's protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order quashing the subpoena and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Visiting Homemaker Service of Hudson County v. Bd. of Chosen Freeholders of County of Hudson


DOCKET NO. A-3180-03T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


380 N.J. Super. 596; 883 A.2d 1074; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 293


September 15, 2005, Argued Telephonically  
October 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication October 7, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, L-1332-03.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee nonprofit home health care provider petitioned the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, to prevent appellant county from imposing an ordinance, Hudson County, N.J., Ordinance No. 362-6-2003, that the county passed. The lower court judge invalidated the ordinance. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county passed an ordinance directing contractors to provide an increased minimum wage and mandatory health benefits to their employees providing food, janitorial, unarmed security guard, and home health care services. On appeal, the court found that the provider's equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and N.J. Const. art. I, para. 1 were not violated as the county did not arbitrarily target the contractors but investigated the stability and needs of contracting industries and enacted the ordinance appropriately. Further, the ordinance rationally related to a legitimate government purpose and was not arbitrary or discriminatory. While the appeal was pending, the New Jersey Legislature amended N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:11-56a4 to permit political subdivisions to establish standards providing wages and protections greater than those required by state or federal law. As a result, the county was then proposing a new ordinance reestablishing a living wage and providing for defined health benefits. Accordingly, the issue of impermissible vagueness in the ordinance was rendered moot by the amendment to § 34:11-56a4 and the county's consideration of a new ordinance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Allstate Ins. Co. v. Sabato


DOCKET NO. A-0380-04T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


380 N.J. Super. 463; 882 A.2d 972; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 287


September 12, 2005, Submitted  
October 3, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication October 3, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County, L-2621-04.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a treating physician, appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County (New Jersey), which vacated an alternative dispute resolution award finding plaintiff insurer in bad faith. The order also reduced the attorney's fees awarded to the physician.


OVERVIEW: A patient received treatment from the physician following an automobile accident. At the time of the accident, the patient was insured for Personal Injury Protection (PIP) benefits under a policy issued by the insurer. After the insurer denied coverage, the physician took an assignment of the patient's claim and filed a demand for PIP arbitration seeking to recover medical expenses totaling $ 5,494.44. An umpire was appointed. The insurer defended, claiming that the physician violated the Patient Records Rule, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 13, § 35-6.5(b), requiring physicians to maintain contemporaneous permanent treatment records. Accepting the insurer's defense, the umpire found that physician's failure to satisfy the requirements of the Patient Records Rule precluded his recovery of PIP benefits. A new umpire subsequently found that the insurer acted in bad faith by allowing its counsel to raise that Rule when it had the records in its file. That decision of bad faith was reversed by another umpire, and the attorney fee award was adjusted. The court held that the reasonableness of the bad faith decision was not within its purview of review but that the attorney fee award was.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal insofar as it sought to reverse the order vacating the finding that the insurer acted in bad faith. The court did reverse the portion of the order reducing the insured's attorney's fees and remanded the case to the lower court for further proceedings.

State v. O'Hagen


DOCKET NO. A-2211-03T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


380 N.J. Super. 133; 881 A.2d 733; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 271


May 24, 2005, Submitted  
September 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication September 7, 2005.
Certification granted State v. O'Hagen, 185 N.J. 391, 886 A.2d 661, 2005 N.J. LEXIS 1555 (2005)
Affirmed by State v. O'Hagen, 189 N.J. 140, 914 A.2d 267, 2007 N.J. LEXIS 16 (N.J., Jan. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County, Ind. No. 02-03-0277-I.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant convicted of drug possession appealed from a Superior Court, Law Division, Passaic County (New Jersey), direction that he submit to collection of a biological sample pursuant to the New Jersey DNA Database and Databank Act of 1994 (DNA Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 53:1-20.17 to -20.20. He argued that the DNA Act violated his state and federal rights to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures and of equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The DNA Act had been expanded far beyond its original focus on violent offenders and sex offenders. Defendant argued that as a small-time drug offender the law was unconstitutional as applied to him. The court held, first, that under a special needs analysis used to determine whether a particular intrusion violated U.S. Const. amend. IV and N.J. Const. art. I, para. 7, it was clear that the minimal intrusion necessary to collect DNA samples accomplished many purposes beyond ordinary law enforcement. Furthermore, persons convicted of crimes or found not guilty by reason of insanity had greatly diminished privacy expectations. To determine whether requiring defendant to provide a sample violated his equal protection guarantees under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and N.J. Const. art. I, § 1, the court looked to whether the law had a rational relationship to the public interest that outweighed private interests. It found that the public interest in reducing recidivism as to all types of crimes justified the classification used.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the challenged portion of the judgment of conviction.

State v. Jimenez


DOCKET NO. A-3736-04T2, A-3737-04T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


380 N.J. Super. 1; 880 A.2d 468; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 251


May 11, 2005, Argued  
August 17, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication August 17, 2005.
Appeal granted by State v. Jimenez, 185 N.J. 286, 884 A.2d 1259, 2005 N.J. LEXIS 1331 (2005)
Reversed by State v. Jimenez, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1520 (N.J., Oct. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County, 04-03-00318-I.
State v. Jimenez, 175 N.J. 475, 815 A.2d 976, 2003 N.J. LEXIS 176 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted interlocutory review to appeals by both the State and defendant from an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County, establishing procedures for determining whether defendant's alleged mild mental retardation made him ineligible for the death penalty, setting a preliminary hearing before the court and a later proceeding before a jury.


OVERVIEW: When the nation's highest court, in Atkins, held that execution of mentally retarded defendants violated the Eighth Amendment, it left it to the states to determine how to assure that such executions did not occur. The trial court, the first in New Jersey to confront the issue, eager to resolve such issues as early as possible, ordered a pretrial hearing, before the judge, at which defendant would have an opportunity to show retardation by clear and convincing evidence. In the absence of such a showing, and if defendant were found guilty, he would have another opportunity, before the penalty phase, to argue mental retardation, at which point it would be the State's burden to show absence of retardation beyond a reasonable doubt. While the first proceeding put an improper burden on defendant, the second was affirmed as an appropriate means of implementing the Atkins directive. The Sixth Amendment probably, and N.J. Const. art. I, para. 9 certainly, required a jury finding on the issue of mental retardation as its absence was a trigger for death penalty eligibility and thus a fact affecting sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the order that required a pretrial hearing on the retardation issue but affirmed that portion of the order that directed a jury determination of the issue between the guilt and penalty phases of defendant's trial, if he were found guilty at the guilt phase. It remanded the matter for further proceedings.

State v. Lopez


DOCKET NO. A-2284-03T4


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


378 N.J. Super. 521; 876 A.2d 795; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 208


May 11, 2005, Submitted  
June 28, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication June 28, 2005.
Certification granted by State v. Lopez, 185 N.J. 295, 884 A.2d 1265, 2005 N.J. LEXIS 1328 (2005)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Lopez, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 665 (N.J., June 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County, 02-08-1018.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County, which found him guilty of reckless manslaughter and robbery and sentenced defendant to consecutive nine-year terms of imprisonment for reckless manslaughter and robbery with 85 percent parole disqualifiers on each count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to a pub and met up with the victim. The victim offered to pay defendant for sex and suggested that they have sex by the nearby railroad tracks. The two men went to another bar and then went to the railroad tracks where, according to defendant, the victim told him that he was either going to have sex voluntarily or be forced. The men started fighting, and defendant struck the victim in the throat with a karate chop using the side of his hand. The victim fell face down in the river, and defendant then stole the victim's necklace. The victim died from fatal injuries to his throat and neck. A jury convicted him of reckless manslaughter and robbery. On appeal, the court found that the robbery conviction could not stand because it was based on an erroneous jury instruction that allowed the jury to convict based on the "afterthought concept" not found in N,J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:15-1. However, the court found that the elements of third-degree theft were clearly present, as defendant admitted he stole from the victim. Because defendant had no prior convictions, the court found that the recidivism exception expressed in Blakely was inapplicable and remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the robbery conviction and remanded for entry of a conviction on the third-degree offense of theft from the person and sentencing on that charge. The court vacated the sentence for reckless manslaughter and remanded for resentencing.

Romeo v. Seton Hall University


DOCKET NO. A-1191-04T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


378 N.J. Super. 384; 875 A.2d 1043; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 197


April 4, 2005, Argued  
June 22, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication June 22, 2005.
Certification denied by Romeo v. Seton Hall Univ., 185 N.J. 295, 884 A.2d 1265, 2005 N.J. LEXIS 1349 (N.J., Oct. 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, Docket No. L-1866-04.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant university sought review of the order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, which reinstated respondent student's complaint alleging breach of contract and violations of the Law Against Discrimination (LAD) and vacated an earlier summary judgment order of dismissal for failure to state a claim.


OVERVIEW: An openly gay student at a Catholic university applied to the university's department of student affairs for provisional recognition of a gay and lesbian student organization. The vice president of student affairs denied his application, stating that the guidance from the Catholic Church opposed an exclusive focus on a person's sexual orientation. Although she stated that the department was prepared to work with gay and lesbian students to meet their needs, the student filed suit. The suit was dismissed but reinstated. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that it was not error to dismiss the complaint because the LAD's prohibition of discrimination based on sexual orientation, N.J. Stat. § 10:5-3, did not apply to religiously affiliated institutions such as the university. Although the student claimed that the university waived its religious exemption by publishing its antidiscrimination policy, the court held that the exemption under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 10:5-5(1) could not be waived. The court found also that the university's antidiscrimination policy did not create a unilateral contract, because a contractual relationship could not be based on isolated provisions in a manual.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order.

Lewis v. Harris


DOCKET NO. A-2244-03T5


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


378 N.J. Super. 168; 875 A.2d 259; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 186


December 7, 2004, Argued  
June 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication June 14, 2005. As Amended January 4, 2006.
Affirmed in part and modified in part by Lewis v. Harris, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1521 (N.J., Oct. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, Docket No. L-15-03.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff couples sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, dismissing their action brought against defendant government officials alleging that the denial of their applications for marriage licenses violated their due process and equal protection rights under the New Jersey Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The couples, all homosexual couples, applied for marriage licenses, which were denied by the government officials. The couples brought an action contending that the denial of the licenses violated their due process and equal protection rights under the New Jersey Constitution. The government officials responded with a motion to dismiss, which was granted, and the couples appealed the judgment. The court noted that N.J. Const. art. I, para. 1, protected both substantive and procedural due process rights, which included the right to privacy. While privacy considerations protected the right to heterosexual marriage, the court concluded that homosexual marriage was not a right rooted in the traditions and collective conscience of the people of New Jersey as to be ranked as fundamental. Evaluation of the equal protection clause, N.J. Const. art. I, para. 1, required a balancing test that considered the nature of the affected right, the extent to which the governmental restriction intruded upon it, and the public need for restriction. Here the couples failed to meet the first prong of the test and show an affected right. Accordingly, the dismissal of the action was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the action for failure to state a claim was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County, Docket Nos. MON-L-798-04; DJ-31866-04; DJ-31880-04.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County, held that the Foreign Country Money-Judgment Recognition Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:49A-16 et seq., permitted judgments to be filed without prior judicial approval. Defendant judgment debtors appealed.


OVERVIEW: At issue in the instant appeal was whether money judgments issued by courts in foreign nations could be filed with the Clerk of the Superior Court and enforced in New Jersey without a prior judicial determination recognizing the judgments and authorizing their enforcement within the State. The appeals court agreed that they could. Further, although reduced by order of the English court, the judgments had not been vacated in their entirety and remained on file with the Clerk of the Court. Therefore, the issue as to whether the English judgments should have been filed without prior judicial authorization was not moot. Third, the court was not convinced that the Legislature intended that the Act would be merely a means to obtain recognition of a foreign country's judgment. Finally, concerns about the constitutionality of the filing pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:49A-27 of judgments from nations that did not adhere to basic principles of due process of law were better left to the legislature.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Schundler v. Donovan


DOCKET NOS. A-4433-04T2, A-4434-04T2, A-4451-04T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


377 N.J. Super. 339; 872 A.2d 1092; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 146


May 3, 2005, Submitted  
May 5, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved For Publication May 6, 2005.
Certification granted Schundler v. Donovan, 183 N.J. 587, 874 A.2d 1106, 2005 N.J. LEXIS 792 (2005)
Certification granted Schundler v. Donovan, 183 N.J. 587, 874 A.2d 1106, 2005 N.J. LEXIS 791 (2005)
Certification granted Schundler v. Donovan, 183 N.J. 587, 874 A.2d 1106, 2005 N.J. LEXIS 790 (2005)
Affirmed by Schundler v. Donovan, 183 N.J. 383, 874 A.2d 506, 2005 N.J. LEXIS 501 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Civil Part, Bergen County, L-2891-05 and L-2897-05.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff primary candidates appealed from an order of the Superior Court, Law Division, Civil Part, Bergen County (New Jersey), that upheld, as within their discretion, defendant county clerks' proposed voting machine ballot layouts despite the candidates' argument that the layouts violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:23-26.1.


OVERVIEW: Section 19:23-26.1 specified that lines and columns on ballots where candidates for gubernatorial and senatorial nominations appeared had to be reserved to those candidates with relative positions within those areas determined by lot. First Amendment case law suggested that requests by candidates that names of allied candidates be bracketed together constituted protected political speech. When they attempted to lay out a ballot for an upcoming primary, the clerks decided that it would not be possible to place seven names of candidates for high office in the manner required by the statute, while also leaving bracketed groups together, so they produced a variant, partly in reliance on opinions of another trial court and New Jersey's Attorney General that questioned § 19:23-26.1's constitutionality. The appellate court considered the issue de novo and held that it had by no means been shown that the statute could not be enforced without violating the First Amendment. Therefore, despite the discretion normally accorded to county clerks in performing their election-related duties, the court ordered them to comply with the statute by conducting a new drawing and abiding by the results.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order and remanded the matter with directions to have the candidates draw lots for ballot positions, while continuing to do whatever could be done to protect the candidates' rights to have bracketed placement with any associated candidates.

Infinity Broadcasting Corp. v. New Jersey Meadowlands Comm'n


DOCKET NO. A-0264-02T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


377 N.J. Super. 209; 872 A.2d 125; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 140


October 5, 2004, Argued  
May 5, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication May 5, 2005.
Certification granted by Infinity Broad. Corp. v. N.J. Meadowlands Comm'n, 185 N.J. 264, 883 A.2d 1061, 2005 N.J. LEXIS 1152 (2005)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Infinity Broad. Corp. v. N.J. Meadowlands Comm'n, 187 N.J. 212, 901 A.2d 312, 2006 N.J. LEXIS 1052 (N.J., June 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey Meadowlands Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the New Jersey Meadowlands Commission, adopted resolutions amending a redevelopment agreement with intervenor developer. The agreement related to a portion of a district. Petitioner radio stations owned land in the district to operate their radio stations and wanted building height limited to prevent interference with radio signals broadcast from their towers. The stations invoked "Rule 2:2-3(a)(2)" and appealed from the resolutions.


OVERVIEW: The redevelopment agreement initially addressed plans for commercial, recreational, and residential uses but did not establish a particular project design or site plan. The Commission held hearings on proposed amendments to the redevelopment agreement to define more specific uses. The stations appeared, testified, and submitted expert opinions that the taller proposed buildings in the project area could interfere with their radio stations' broadcast signals to the extent, possibly, of requiring the radio stations to cease operations. The stations' objections to the Commission's resolution included that it did not fully consider the stations' evidence. However, since the Commission's actions were quasi-legislative, rather than quasi-judicial, the Commission complied with procedural due process requirements by giving public notice and holding a public hearing. Even though the Commission was a state agency, it was compared to a municipality that was enacting a zoning ordinance. If the stations wanted to litigate that the planned development of the district effected a taking or a reverse taking of their pre-district property rights, then their proper forum was the court's law division.


OUTCOME: The appellate court dismissed the appeal without prejudice to the rights of the stations to vindicate their claims in a proceeding in lieu of prerogative writs in the law division.

 

400 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Duncan


DOCKET NO. A-6705-03T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


376 N.J. Super. 253; 870 A.2d 307; 2005 N.J. Super. LEXIS 114


March 9, 2005, Argued  
April 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 14, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County, 03-101.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey in the Law Division at Morris County, which convicted him on a downgraded charge of harassment in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-4(a) in connection with a call he made to 9-1-1 and which sentenced him to a fine and three days of jail time already served.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was initially charged with an improper 9-1-1 call in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-3e for a profane call he made to 9-1-1 complaining about a police roadblock that delayed him on the way to his mother's medical emergency. The prosecutor downgraded the charge to harassment under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-4(a). Defendant appealed his conviction on several grounds, including a challenge as to whether the language he used could be considered harassment under the statute. The court found that defendant's language in venting his frustration about the roadblock, while impolite and rude, was not evidence of a purpose to harass another within the meaning of § 2C:33-4. The State conceded that the call was not at an inconvenient time where 9-1-1 was a 24-hour service. Moreover, the profane language, standing alone, did not establish defendant's intent to harass. The trial court improperly inferred a purpose to harass merely since defendant committed one of the stand-alone offenses listed under § 2C:33-4(a). Finally, all the evidence in the record contradicted any finding of an intent to harass, which was a required element for a conviction, or that the operator felt harassed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction.
